  \exp\!\left[-\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(\mu)}+\ii\theta\right]
  \left(1+O(g_{\rm ht}^2)\right).
  \label{eq:one-instanton-universal-density}
\end{equation}
Here \(\dd\Omega_{N_c}\) is a chosen invariant density on the local
orientation orbit
\[
  SU(N_c)/(SU(N_c-2)\times U(1)),
\]
with the evident \(SU(2)/\mathbb Z_2\) specialization when \(N_c=2\).
The coefficient \(C_{\mathcal S,N_c,N_f}\) is a finite constant depending on
the regulator, subtraction convention, and normalization of
\(\dd\Omega_{N_c}\); obtaining it requires the full renormalized determinant
calculation in the chosen scheme.
The factors
\(\dd^4a\,\dd\rho/\rho^5\), \(\dd\Omega_{N_c}\), and
\((8\pi^2/g_{\rm ht}^2)^{2N_c}\) have just been fixed by dimension,
orientation invariance, and the \(4N_c\) bosonic zero modes.  It remains to
determine the power of \(\mu\rho\) at one loop.  Write the unknown power as
\(\alpha\) and apply \(\mu\dd/\dd\mu\) to the logarithm of the density factor
\[
  g_{\rm ht}^{-4N_c}
  (\mu\rho)^\alpha
  \exp\!\left[-\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(\mu)}\right].
\]
The derivative is
\[
  \alpha
  -4N_c\,\frac{\beta(g_{\rm ht})}{g_{\rm ht}}
  +
  \frac{16\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^3}\,\beta(g_{\rm ht}) .
\]
Substituting \eqref{eq:instanton-density-beta0-definition} gives
\[
  \alpha-b_0+O(g_{\rm ht}^2).
\]
RG invariance of a physical one-instanton contribution through one loop
therefore fixes \(\alpha=b_0\).  The derivative of the zero-mode power
starts at order \(g_{\rm ht}^2\), so it belongs to the next perturbative order
and is absorbed into the higher-loop correction multiplying
\eqref{eq:one-instanton-universal-density}.  The finite constant
\(C_{\mathcal S,N_c,N_f}\) is outside this argument because RG invariance
fixes scale dependence, while the constant term is set by the actual
regularized determinant and measure normalization.

\begin{proposition}[Pure-gauge Pauli--Villars determinant constant]
\label{prop:pure-gauge-pv-instanton-determinant-constant}
In pure \(SU(N)\) Yang--Mills, \(N\geq2\), use the common half-trace
coupling \(g_{\rm PV}(\mu)\) and the Pauli--Villars determinant convention of
the one-instanton calculation
\cite{tHooft1976Pseudoparticle,Bernard1979InstantonDeterminants}.  For
gauge-invariant insertions, integrate the embedded orientation orbit with the
corresponding Haar normalization.  Then the one-loop, one-instanton density is
\begin{equation}
  \dd n^{\rm PV}_{I,N}
  =
  \frac{\dd^4a\,\dd\rho}{\rho^5}\,
  C^{\rm PV}_{N}\,
  \left(\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm PV}^2(\mu)}\right)^{2N}
  (\mu\rho)^{11N/3}
  \exp\!\left[-\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm PV}^2(\mu)}+\ii\theta\right]
  \left(1+O(g_{\rm PV}^2)\right),
  \label{eq:pure-gauge-pv-instanton-density}
\end{equation}
where the finite constant is
\begin{equation}
  C^{\rm PV}_{N}
  =
  \frac{2^{2-2N}}{\pi^2 (N-1)!(N-2)!}\,
  \exp\!\left[-\alpha(1)-2(N-2)\alpha\!\left(\frac12\right)\right].
  \label{eq:pure-gauge-pv-instanton-constant-alpha}
\end{equation}
Here
\[
  \alpha(1)=0.443307\ldots,\qquad
  \alpha\!\left(\frac12\right)=0.145873\ldots .
\]
Equivalently, in the conventional rounded form,
\begin{equation}
  C^{\rm PV}_{N}
  =
  \frac{0.466\,\exp[-1.679\,N]}{(N-1)!(N-2)!}
  \quad\hbox{to the displayed precision}.
  \label{eq:pure-gauge-pv-instanton-constant-rounded}
\end{equation}
For example \(C^{\rm PV}_{3}\simeq1.51\times10^{-3}\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The orientation-integrated singular-gauge collective-coordinate calculation
gives, after the Pauli--Villars zero-mode mass factors have been combined with
the logarithmic determinant into \((\mu\rho)^{11N/3}\), the residual
zero-mode coefficient
\[
  \frac{2^{4N+2}\pi^{4N-2}}{(N-1)!(N-2)!}\,g_{\rm PV}^{-4N}.
\]
Rewriting
\[
  g_{\rm PV}^{-4N}
  =
  \left(\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm PV}^2}\right)^{2N}
  (8\pi^2)^{-2N}
\]
turns this residual coefficient into
\[
  \frac{2^{2-2N}}{\pi^2 (N-1)!(N-2)!}
  \left(\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm PV}^2}\right)^{2N}.
\]
The finite part of the nonzero-mode determinant contributes
\[
  \exp\!\left[-\alpha(1)-2(N-2)\alpha\!\left(\frac12\right)\right],
\]
where \(\alpha(1)\) is the \(SU(2)\) vector-ghost block and the
\(2(N-2)\) copies of \(\alpha(1/2)\) are the additional doublet blocks in the
embedded \(SU(2)\subset SU(N)\) decomposition.  Multiplying these two factors
gives \eqref{eq:pure-gauge-pv-instanton-constant-alpha}; combining it with
the classical action and logarithmic determinant gives
\eqref{eq:pure-gauge-pv-instanton-density}.  Taking logarithms of
\eqref{eq:pure-gauge-pv-instanton-constant-alpha} yields
\[
  \log C^{\rm PV}_{N}
  =
  \log(0.466\ldots)-1.679\ldots\,N
  -\log((N-1)!)-\log((N-2)!),
\]
which is the rounded form
\eqref{eq:pure-gauge-pv-instanton-constant-rounded}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Heat-kernel source of the instanton logarithm]
\label{prop:instanton-heat-kernel-beta0-logarithm}
In the same background-field gauge and half-trace convention, the logarithmic
part of the charge-\(k\) nonzero-mode fluctuation determinant has
\begin{equation}
  \partial_{\log\mu}\log\mathcal W_{\rm log}^{\rm nz}
  =
  k\left[
    \frac{11}{3}C_2(G)
    -\frac{4}{3}\sum_{\text{\rm Dirac }R}T(R)
  \right].
  \label{eq:instanton-heat-kernel-beta0-logarithm}
\end{equation}
For vectorlike \(SU(N_c)\) QCD with \(N_f\) Dirac fundamentals this coefficient
is \(k b_0\), with \(b_0\) as in
\eqref{eq:instanton-density-beta0-definition}.  Hence, in a charge-one BPST
chart,
\begin{equation}
  \log\mathcal W_{\rm log}^{\rm nz}(a,\rho,U;\mu)
  =
  b_0\log(\mu\rho)+\log\mathcal W_{\rm fin}^{\rm nz}(U;\mathcal S),
  \label{eq:instanton-nonzero-mode-log-mu-rho}
\end{equation}
up to higher-loop and local finite-subtraction terms in the chosen scheme.
Equivalently, if \(X_\kappa=8\pi^2/g_{\rm ht}^2(\kappa)\) and
\(X_\Lambda=X_\mu+b_0\log(\Lambda/\mu)\) at one loop, then
\begin{equation}
  \exp[-X_\Lambda+\ii\theta]\,
  (\Lambda\rho)^{b_0}
  =
  \exp[-X_\mu+\ii\theta]\,
  (\mu\rho)^{b_0}.
  \label{eq:instanton-cutoff-renormalized-scale-trade}
\end{equation}
The factor \((\mu\rho)^{b_0}\) in
\eqref{eq:one-instanton-universal-density} is therefore the logarithmic
shadow of the nonzero-mode fluctuation spectrum plus coupling
renormalization, while the finite constant still requires the full spectral
determinant calculation.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The small-proper-time expansion of
\eqref{eq:proper-time-instanton-determinant-ratio} is local in the gauge
background.  With background-field gauge fixing, the vector fluctuation and
ghost complex contribute the coefficient \((11/3)C_2(G)\) multiplying the
topological charge in the logarithmic counterterm, and a Dirac fermion in
representation \(R\) contributes \(-(4/3)T(R)\).  Summing the fields gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-heat-kernel-beta0-logarithm}.  For a fundamental Dirac
fermion of \(SU(N_c)\), \(T(\square)=1/2\), so the matter term is
\(-2N_f/3\).  The coefficient in this convention is therefore
\[
  \frac{11}{3}N_c-\frac{2}{3}N_f=b_0 .
\]

A BPST connection with size \(\rho\) is obtained from the unit-size connection
by translation, global orientation, and dilation.  After the zero modes are
removed, the logarithmic scale dependence of the determinant can therefore
depend on the size only through the dimensionless combination \(\mu\rho\),
apart from finite scheme-dependent terms.  This gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-nonzero-mode-log-mu-rho}.  Finally, the one-loop running of
\(X_\kappa\) gives \(X_\Lambda=X_\mu+b_0\log(\Lambda/\mu)\); substituting this
identity into the cutoff expression proves
\eqref{eq:instanton-cutoff-renormalized-scale-trade}.
\end{proof}

Fermion zero modes are controlled by the index theorem already stated in
\eqref{eq:dirac-index-anomaly}.  In the conventional half-trace notation, a
left-handed Weyl fermion in representation \(R\) has
\begin{equation}
  n_+-n_-=2T_R\,k,
  \qquad
  \operatorname{tr}_R(T_R^aT_R^b)=T_R\delta^{ab}.
  \label{eq:instanton-index-dynkin}
\end{equation}
For a fundamental Weyl fermion of \(SU(N_c)\), \(T_\square=1/2\), so a
\(k=1\) instanton has one normalizable zero mode of the chirality selected by
the self-dual background.  The anti-instanton has the opposite chirality.  In
the trace-delta convention the numerical value called \(T_R\) is doubled, but
the topological density and the coupling coordinate are correspondingly
rewritten; the integer kernel dimension in
\eqref{eq:instanton-index-dynkin} is the invariant statement.

The zero modes determine the Grassmann selection rule.  Expand a massless
fermion in an instanton background as
\[
  \psi(x)=\sum_{\alpha=1}^{n_0}\xi_\alpha\psi_{0,\alpha}(x)
  +\sum_{\lambda\neq0}\xi_\lambda\psi_\lambda(x),
\]
where \(\psi_{0,\alpha}\) are the zero modes and \(\xi_\alpha\) are odd
coefficients.  The quadratic fermion action contains no term involving
\(\xi_\alpha\).  Therefore the Berezin integral over zero-mode variables
vanishes unless operator insertions supply every missing \(\xi_\alpha\).
This is the finite-dimensional Berezin rule \(\int\dd\xi\,1=0\),
\(\int\dd\xi\,\xi=1\) applied after the spectral decomposition of the
regulated fermion field.

\begin{proposition}[Instanton sectors as physical correlator contributions]
\label{prop:instanton-sector-physical-correlator-contribution}
Fix a finite regulator, a \(Q=1\) instanton chart with collective coordinate
\(z=(a,\rho,U)\), smooth chart domain \(\mathcal U_{Q=1}\), and
renormalized insertions \(\mathcal O_1,\ldots,\mathcal O_r\).  After gauge
fixing, collective coordinate separation, and integration of nonzero
fluctuations, the instanton sector contribution has the form
\begin{equation}
  \bigl\langle\mathcal O_1\cdots\mathcal O_r\bigr\rangle_{Q=1,\Lambda}
  =
  \int_{\mathcal U_{Q=1}}
  \ee^{-S_\Lambda(A_z)+\ii\theta}\,
  \mathcal W_{\Lambda}^{\rm nz}(z)\,
  \mathcal Z_{\mathcal O,\Lambda}^{0}(z)\,
  \dd\nu_{\Lambda,\mathcal M}(z),
  \label{eq:instanton-physical-correlator-assembly}
\end{equation}
provided the determinant/Pfaffian line has been paired with the fermion
zero-mode and anomaly-line data to produce a scalar density.  Here
\(\mathcal W_{\Lambda}^{\rm nz}\) is the nonzero-mode determinant datum from
\eqref{eq:finite-regulator-instanton-nonzero-determinant-factor}, while
\(\mathcal Z_{\mathcal O,\Lambda}^{0}(z)\) is the finite Berezin coefficient
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal Z_{\mathcal O,\Lambda}^{0}(z)
  =
  \int\dd\xi_{n_0}\cdots\dd\xi_1\,
  \mathcal O_{1,\Lambda}^{0}(z,\xi)\cdots
  \mathcal O_{r,\Lambda}^{0}(z,\xi)\,
  \exp[-S_{\rm lift,\Lambda}^{0}(z,\xi)] .
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-saturation-functional}
\end{equation}
The superscript \(0\) means that each insertion and each mass, Yukawa, or
source term has been restricted to the zero-mode subspace.  If the integrand
in \eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-saturation-functional} does not contain the
monomial \(\xi_1\cdots\xi_{n_0}\), then
\(\mathcal Z_{\mathcal O,\Lambda}^{0}(z)=0\).  If it does contain that
monomial, the coefficient of that monomial is the only part of the insertions
which is seen by the instanton sector.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
At finite cutoff the gauge-fixed fields split into collective coordinates,
normal bosonic modes, ghosts, fermion zero modes, and fermion nonzero modes.
Gaussian integration over the normal bosonic and ghost variables gives the
determinant factors already isolated in
\(\mathcal W_{\Lambda}^{\rm nz}\); Gaussian or Pfaffian integration over
fermion nonzero modes gives the remaining nonzero-mode determinant-line
factor.  None of these operations integrates over the zero-mode variables
\(\xi_\alpha\), because the quadratic fermion operator vanishes on them.
The only finite-dimensional integral left in the fermionic zero-mode sector is
\eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-saturation-functional}.  Berezin integration
extracts the coefficient of the ordered top monomial
\(\xi_1\cdots\xi_{n_0}\).  All terms missing at least one zero-mode variable
therefore vanish, while terms containing the top monomial contribute exactly
their coefficient.  Multiplying this coefficient by the bosonic
collective-coordinate density and the nonzero-mode determinant gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-physical-correlator-assembly}.
\end{proof}

Thus the moduli space is not the physical answer; it is the domain of a
semiclassical amplitude.  The physical question is which insertions, masses,
or sources saturate the fermion zero modes, what nonzero-mode determinant and
counterterm scheme define \(\mathcal W_{\Lambda}^{\rm nz}\), and whether the
resulting \(a,\rho,U\) integral is finite at its boundary faces.

\paragraph{From collective coordinates to an amplitude.}
For later use, it is helpful to compress the \(Q=1\) calculation into the
ordered finite-regulator pipeline
\begin{equation}
  K_{\Lambda,\mathcal J}^{E}(z)
  =
  \ee^{-S_\Lambda(A_z)+\ii\theta}\,
  \mathcal W_{\Lambda}^{\rm nz}(z)\,
  \mathcal Z_{\mathcal J,\Lambda}^{0}(z)\,
  \dd\nu_{\Lambda,\mathcal M}(z),
  \qquad
  G_{\Lambda,\mathcal J}^{E,Q=1}
  =
  \int_{\mathcal U_{Q=1}}K_{\Lambda,\mathcal J}^{E}(z).
  \label{eq:instanton-amplitude-pipeline-euclidean-kernel}
\end{equation}
The first factor selects the topological sector and its classical action; the
last factor is the collective-coordinate density; the middle two factors are
where the fluctuation and fermion-saturation calculation enters.  A
semiclassical local vertex is obtained only after replacing
\(K_{\Lambda,\mathcal J}^{E}\) on a declared window by a leading kernel and
then projecting it onto an observable coordinate:
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_{\rm phys}^{Q=1}[\mathcal J]
  =
  \operatorname*{Proj}_{\rm phys}
  \operatorname*{Cont}_{\mathcal S}
  \int_{\mathcal U_{\rm win}}
  K_{{\rm lead},\mathcal J}^{E}(z)
  +
  R_{\rm det}+R_{\rm zm}+R_{\rm src}+R_{\rm Schur}
  +R_{\rho}+R_{\rm cont}+R_{\rm spec}+R_{\rm IR}+R_{\rm cut}.
  \label{eq:instanton-amplitude-pipeline-physical-map}
\end{equation}
Here the determinant residual includes the nonzero-mode spectrum and local
counterterms; \(R_{\rm zm}\) records the zero-mode projection or derivative
expansion of the sources; \(R_{\rm src}\) records the color-singlet,
hadronic, or OPE matching layer; \(R_{\rm Schur}\) records finite
nonzero-mode corrections to the zero-mode block; \(R_{\rho}\) is the size and
Uhlenbeck-face endpoint remainder; and the final four terms are the
continuation, spectral-projection, infrared, and unitarity-cut remnants
needed before a physical amplitude is asserted.

This ordering is part of the content of the instanton calculation.  The ADHM
or BPST moduli space supplies the domain and the collective-coordinate
Jacobian.  It does not supply the nonzero-mode determinant, the fermion
zero-mode Berezin coefficient, the source-to-observable matching, or the
endpoint estimates.  Conversely, the local 't Hooft operator is the
small-size, source-adiabatic coordinate of
\eqref{eq:instanton-amplitude-pipeline-euclidean-kernel}; the four-point
amplitude calculation keeps the zero-mode form factors, determinant
normalization, external source residues, and size tails inside the same
integral until a hard, screened, thermal, or Wilsonian window justifies
separating them.

For vectorlike QCD with \(N_f\) massless Dirac fundamentals, a \(Q=1\)
instanton supplies one zero mode for each flavor in one chirality sector.  The
semiclassical functional integral therefore generates the following leading
local term in the derivative expansion around external fields whose variation
scale is much larger than \(\rho\):
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal L_{\rm inst}
  =
  \int_0^\infty\frac{\dd\rho}{\rho^5}\,
  C_{N_c,N_f}(\rho,\mu)
  \exp\!\left(-\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(\mu)}+\ii\theta\right)
  \det_{1\le f,f'\le N_f}
  \left[
    \rho^3\bar\psi_{R f}\psi_{L f'}
  \right]
  +\hbox{anti-instanton conjugate}
  \label{eq:qcd-thooft-vertex-leading-local}
\end{equation}
after integrating over the instanton center and color orientation and after
contracting spin and color indices as dictated by the zero-mode wavefunctions
and gauge invariance.  The determinant is over flavor indices; it is the local
tensor compatible with the nonabelian chiral flavor symmetry.  For flavor
diagonal external sources it reduces to the corresponding alternating sum of
products of \(N_f\) bilinears.  At one loop
\[
  C_{N_c,N_f}(\rho,\mu)
  =
  C^{(0)}_{N_c,N_f}
  \left(\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(\mu)}\right)^{2N_c}
  (\rho\mu)^{b_0}
  \left(1+O(g_{\rm ht}^2(\mu))\right),
  \qquad
  b_0=\frac{11}{3}N_c-\frac23N_f,
\]
where \(b_0\) is defined by
\(\mu\,\dd g_{\rm ht}/\dd\mu=-b_0g_{\rm ht}^3/(16\pi^2)+O(g_{\rm ht}^5)\).
The scale and coupling dependence is the universal content of the running-factor
calculation above; the constant
\(C^{(0)}_{N_c,N_f}\) is fixed only after choosing the determinant and
orientation-volume normalization.  The dimensionless factors
\(\rho^3\bar\psi_R\psi_L\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-thooft-vertex-leading-local} record the normalization of the
external zero-mode wavefunctions in the local limit; changing the
regularization scheme changes \(C^{(0)}_{N_c,N_f}\) and higher-loop factors,
not the zero-mode tensor or the selection rule.  When the external fields vary
on the scale \(\rho\), the same zero-mode integration gives a nonlocal kernel
rather than the local determinant in
\eqref{eq:qcd-thooft-vertex-leading-local}.  Its regulator-independent
selection rule is
\[
  \Delta Q_A=2N_f
\]
for the anomalous axial charge, in agreement with the integrated anomaly.
Small quark masses may replace missing fermion insertions by mass factors,
because the mass term pairs the corresponding zero-mode variables.

\begin{proposition}[Flavor determinant from the instanton zero modes]
\label{prop:qcd-thooft-determinant-zero-mode-amplitude}
In the \(Q=1\) sector of vectorlike \(SU(N_c)\) QCD, let
\(\lambda_f,\widetilde\lambda_f\), \(f=1,\ldots,N_f\), denote the two
Grassmann zero-mode coefficients paired by the local source matrix
\(B=(B_{ff'})\).  Choose the zero-mode orientation so that
\begin{equation}
  \int
  \prod_{f=N_f}^{1}\dd\widetilde\lambda_f\,\dd\lambda_f\,
  \exp\!\left(
    \sum_{f,f'=1}^{N_f}
    \widetilde\lambda_f B_{ff'}\lambda_{f'}
  \right)
  =
  \det B .
  \label{eq:thooft-vertex-berezin-determinant}
\end{equation}
For slowly varying external quark fields,
\(B_{ff'}=\rho^3\bar\psi_{Rf}\psi_{Lf'}\), and
\eqref{eq:thooft-vertex-berezin-determinant} is precisely the flavor
determinant in \eqref{eq:qcd-thooft-vertex-leading-local}.  If instead all
zero modes are saturated by the quark mass term, the same finite-dimensional
calculation replaces \(B\) by the mass-overlap matrix
\(B^{(m)}_{ff'}(z)\).  Its phase is the phase of \(\det M\), so the
one-instanton vacuum term has phase
\(\exp[\ii(\theta+\arg\det M)]\), up to the real positive overlap and
determinant normalizations.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Expand the exponential in
\eqref{eq:thooft-vertex-berezin-determinant}.  Every contributing top-degree
term must contain each \(\widetilde\lambda_f\) once and each \(\lambda_f\)
once.  Such a term is specified by a permutation \(\sigma\in S_{N_f}\):
\[
  \prod_{f=1}^{N_f}
  \widetilde\lambda_f B_{f,\sigma(f)}\lambda_{\sigma(f)} .
\]
Reordering the \(\lambda_{\sigma(f)}\) variables into the chosen Berezin
orientation gives the sign \(\operatorname{sgn}\sigma\).  Berezin integration
therefore extracts
\[
  \sum_{\sigma\in S_{N_f}}
  \operatorname{sgn}\sigma
  \prod_{f=1}^{N_f}B_{f,\sigma(f)}
  =
  \det B .
\]
For \(B_{ff'}=\rho^3\bar\psi_{Rf}\psi_{Lf'}\), this gives the local
\(2N_f\)-fermion operator.  If \(B\) is supplied by the mass term, each
zero-mode overlap is real after the same regulator and zero-mode orientation
have been fixed, so the only flavor phase is \(\arg\det M\).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Two-flavor channel content of the local instanton vertex]
\label{prop:two-flavor-thooft-channel-decomposition}
For \(N_f=2\), set
\[
  \Phi_{ff'}=\bar q_{Rf}q_{Lf'},\qquad
  S_{ff'}=\bar q_fq_{f'},\qquad
  P_{ff'}=\bar q_f\ii\gamma_5q_{f'} .
\]
With the chiral projectors used in this chapter,
\begin{equation}
  \Phi=\frac12(S+\ii P).
  \label{eq:two-flavor-chiral-bilinear-matrix}
\end{equation}
Write the scalar and pseudoscalar flavor matrices in the Pauli basis as
\[
  S=s_0\mathbf 1+\vec s\cdot\vec\tau,\qquad
  P=p_0\mathbf 1+\vec p\cdot\vec\tau .
\]
Then the local instanton plus anti-instanton flavor factor is
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \ee^{\ii\theta}\det\Phi
  +\ee^{-\ii\theta}\det\Phi^\dagger
  &=
  \frac{\cos\theta}{2}
  \left(s_0^2-\vec s^{\,2}-p_0^2+\vec p^{\,2}\right) \\
  &\qquad
  -\sin\theta\left(s_0p_0-\vec s\cdot\vec p\right).
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:two-flavor-thooft-channel-decomposition}
\end{equation}
At \(\theta=0\), the one-instanton local vertex therefore separates the
isosinglet scalar, isotriplet scalar, isosinglet pseudoscalar, and isotriplet
pseudoscalar channels as
\begin{equation}
  \det\Phi+\det\Phi^\dagger
  =
  \frac12
  \left(s_0^2-\vec s^{\,2}-p_0^2+\vec p^{\,2}\right).
  \label{eq:two-flavor-thooft-theta-zero-channels}
\end{equation}
The determinant is invariant under
\(\Phi\mapsto V_R^\dagger\Phi V_L\), \(V_L,V_R\in SU(2)\), but under the
flavor-singlet axial rotation \(q\mapsto\ee^{\ii\alpha\gamma_5}q\) it carries
phase \(\det\Phi\mapsto\ee^{-4\ii\alpha}\det\Phi\).  Hence
\(\ee^{\ii\theta}\det\Phi+\hbox{\rm conjugate}\) is the local channel form of
the same anomalous \(U(1)_A\) selection rule as
\eqref{eq:qcd-thooft-vertex-leading-local}: a compensating
\(\theta\mapsto\theta+4\alpha\) keeps the \(Q=1\) contribution in the same
coordinate.

This channel decomposition is only the zeroth local term of the source
convolution.  The coefficient multiplying
\eqref{eq:two-flavor-thooft-channel-decomposition} is still the
size/orientation/nonzero-mode determinant integral discussed below.  The formula
therefore explains which chiral channels the zero modes select; it is not a
standalone prediction of scalar or pseudoscalar bound-state masses.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The projector identity gives
\[
  \bar q_Rq_L=\bar qP_Lq
  =\frac12(\bar qq-\bar q\gamma_5q)
  =\frac12(\bar qq+\ii\,\bar q\ii\gamma_5q),
\]
which is \eqref{eq:two-flavor-chiral-bilinear-matrix}.  For any matrix
\(X=x_0\mathbf 1+\vec x\cdot\vec\tau\), the Pauli relation
\(\tau_a\tau_b=\delta_{ab}\mathbf 1+\ii\epsilon_{abc}\tau_c\) gives
\(\det X=x_0^2-\vec x^{\,2}\).  Applying this to
\(X=S+\ii P\) gives
\[
  \det(S+\ii P)
  =
  s_0^2-\vec s^{\,2}-p_0^2+\vec p^{\,2}
  +2\ii(s_0p_0-\vec s\cdot\vec p).
\]
Since \(\det\Phi=\frac14\det(S+\ii P)\), taking
\(\ee^{\ii\theta}\det\Phi+\ee^{-\ii\theta}\det\Phi^\dagger\) proves
\eqref{eq:two-flavor-thooft-channel-decomposition}.  The
\(\theta=0\) specialization is immediate.

Finally, an \(SU(2)_L\times SU(2)_R\) rotation multiplies \(\Phi\) by
unit-determinant matrices on the two sides, so its determinant is unchanged.
For \(q\mapsto\ee^{\ii\alpha\gamma_5}q\), one has
\(\bar q_Rq_L\mapsto\ee^{-2\ii\alpha}\bar q_Rq_L\), hence
\(\det\Phi\mapsto\ee^{-4\ii\alpha}\det\Phi\).
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Instanton contribution to two-flavor chiral
source curvatures]
\label{ca:two-flavor-instanton-source-susceptibility}
Suppose the finite-regulator \(Q=\pm1\) calculation, including the
size/orientation integral, nonzero-mode determinant, source normalization, and
local derivative expansion, supplies a finite coefficient
\(\kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}(\mu)\) multiplying the local \(N_f=2\) source density
of Proposition~\ref{prop:two-flavor-thooft-channel-decomposition}.  Equivalently,
for constant renormalized scalar and pseudoscalar source coordinates
\[
  S=s_0\mathbf 1+\vec s\cdot\vec\tau,\qquad
  P=p_0\mathbf 1+\vec p\cdot\vec\tau ,
\]
the instanton part of the source generating-density coordinate
\(\mathcal W=V_4^{-1}\log Z\) has quadratic term
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \mathcal W_{\rm inst}^{(2)}
  &=
  \kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}
  \left[
    \frac{\cos\theta}{2}
    \left(s_0^2-\vec s^{\,2}-p_0^2+\vec p^{\,2}\right)
    -\sin\theta\left(s_0p_0-\vec s\cdot\vec p\right)
  \right]  \\
  &\qquad
  +O(J^3,\partial J),
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:two-flavor-instanton-source-curvature-functional}
\end{equation}
where \(J\) denotes the collection of source coordinates.  Define the local
source curvatures by differentiating \(\mathcal W\) at zero source:
\[
  \chi_\sigma=\partial_{s_0}^2\mathcal W,\quad
  \chi_{\delta_a}=\partial_{s_a}^2\mathcal W,\quad
  \chi_\eta=\partial_{p_0}^2\mathcal W,\quad
  \chi_{\pi_a}=\partial_{p_a}^2\mathcal W,
  \qquad\hbox{no sum on }a .
\]
Then the local instanton contribution is
\begin{equation}
  \chi_\sigma^{\rm inst}
  =
  \chi_{\pi_a}^{\rm inst}
  =
  \kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}\cos\theta,
  \qquad
  \chi_{\delta_a}^{\rm inst}
  =
  \chi_{\eta}^{\rm inst}
  =
  -\kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}\cos\theta ,
  \label{eq:two-flavor-instanton-channel-curvatures}
\end{equation}
and the CP-odd source-mixing curvatures are
\begin{equation}
  \partial_{s_0}\partial_{p_0}\mathcal W_{\rm inst}^{(2)}
  =
  -\kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}\sin\theta,
  \qquad
  \partial_{s_a}\partial_{p_b}\mathcal W_{\rm inst}^{(2)}
  =
  \kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}\sin\theta\,\delta_{ab}.
  \label{eq:two-flavor-instanton-cp-odd-source-mixing}
\end{equation}
At \(\theta=0\), the two \(U(1)_A\)-paired differences supplied by this
finite-activity term are therefore
\begin{equation}
  \left(\chi_{\pi_a}-\chi_{\delta_a}\right)_{\rm inst}
  =
  \left(\chi_\sigma-\chi_\eta\right)_{\rm inst}
  =
  2\kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)} .
  \label{eq:two-flavor-instanton-u1a-susceptibility-splitting}
\end{equation}

Equations
\eqref{eq:two-flavor-instanton-channel-curvatures}--\eqref{eq:two-flavor-instanton-u1a-susceptibility-splitting}
are source-curvature statements in the declared local window.  The full
zero-momentum QCD susceptibilities also contain connected long-distance
propagation, Goldstone poles in the chiral limit, ordinary perturbative and
confining contributions, and finite contact-term conventions.  Thus the
instanton calculation identifies the \(U(1)_A\)-violating local curvature it
adds to the generating functional.  A spectrum statement additionally requires
the color-singlet spectral representation, long-distance matrix elements, and
the continuum/volume limits in the chosen QCD phase.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{proposition}[Axial Ward ledger for the instanton source curvatures]
\label{prop:two-flavor-instanton-source-ward-ledger}
The local two-flavor instanton source functional
\eqref{eq:two-flavor-instanton-source-curvature-functional} obeys the
finite-dimensional anomalous singlet-axial Ward identity
\begin{equation}
  \left[
    4\partial_\theta
    +2p_0\partial_{s_0}
    +2\sum_{a=1}^{3}p_a\partial_{s_a}
    -2s_0\partial_{p_0}
    -2\sum_{a=1}^{3}s_a\partial_{p_a}
  \right]
  \mathcal W_{\rm inst}^{(2)}
  =
  O(J^3,\partial J).
  \label{eq:two-flavor-instanton-source-ward-identity}
\end{equation}
Here the source coordinates transform as the mass/source spurions in the
finite-regulator path integral:
\[
  \delta_\alpha S=2\alpha P,\qquad
  \delta_\alpha P=-2\alpha S,\qquad
  \delta_\alpha\theta=4\alpha .
\]
Thus the same anomalous Jacobian which shifts \(\theta\) also rotates the
local scalar and pseudoscalar source coordinates.  The susceptibility
splittings in
\eqref{eq:two-flavor-instanton-u1a-susceptibility-splitting} are the
second-source derivatives of the same anomalous Ward identity which produces
the 't Hooft vertex.

More explicitly, for each paired coordinate \(s,p\), with \(s=s_0,p=p_0\)
or \(s=s_a,p=p_a\), define
\[
  \chi_s=\partial_s^2\mathcal W_{\rm inst}^{(2)},\qquad
  \chi_p=\partial_p^2\mathcal W_{\rm inst}^{(2)},\qquad
  m_{sp}=\partial_s\partial_p\mathcal W_{\rm inst}^{(2)}
\]
at zero source.  Then the differentiated Ward identity gives
\begin{equation}
  \partial_\theta\chi_s=m_{sp},\qquad
  \partial_\theta\chi_p=-m_{sp},\qquad
  \chi_s-\chi_p=-2\,\partial_\theta m_{sp}.
  \label{eq:two-flavor-instanton-curvature-ward-relations}
\end{equation}
For the singlet pair this is the \((\sigma,\eta)\) relation; for a triplet
pair it is the \((\delta_a,\pi_a)\) relation, so reversing the order of the
difference gives the positive \(\pi_a-\delta_a\) splitting displayed above.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Under an infinitesimal singlet axial rotation,
\(S+\ii P\mapsto (1-2\ii\alpha)(S+\ii P)\), which gives
\(\delta S=2\alpha P\) and \(\delta P=-2\alpha S\).  The anomaly shifts the
source-sector theta coordinate by \(\delta\theta=4\alpha\) for \(N_f=2\).
Consequently the infinitesimal Ward vector field is the operator displayed in
\eqref{eq:two-flavor-instanton-source-ward-identity}.

Let
\[
  A=s_0^2-\vec s^{\,2}-p_0^2+\vec p^{\,2},
  \qquad
  B=s_0p_0-\vec s\cdot\vec p .
\]
The source rotation gives
\[
  \delta_\alpha A=8\alpha B,\qquad
  \delta_\alpha B=-2\alpha A .
\]
The theta derivative of the quadratic part of
\eqref{eq:two-flavor-instanton-source-curvature-functional} contributes
\[
  4\alpha\,\kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}
  \left[-\frac{\sin\theta}{2}A-\cos\theta\,B\right],
\]
whereas the source rotation contributes
\[
  \kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}
  \left[4\alpha\cos\theta\,B+2\alpha\sin\theta\,A\right].
\]
The two terms cancel, proving
\eqref{eq:two-flavor-instanton-source-ward-identity} to the declared local
order.

Now apply \(\partial_s^2\), \(\partial_p^2\), and \(\partial_s\partial_p\) to
the one-pair form of the Ward identity
\((4\partial_\theta+2p\partial_s-2s\partial_p)\mathcal W=0\), and then set all
sources to zero.  The three resulting identities are
\[
  4\partial_\theta\chi_s-4m_{sp}=0,\qquad
  4\partial_\theta\chi_p+4m_{sp}=0,\qquad
  4\partial_\theta m_{sp}+2\chi_s-2\chi_p=0,
\]
which are exactly
\eqref{eq:two-flavor-instanton-curvature-ward-relations}.
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Tested chiral susceptibilities from the
local instanton curvature]
\label{ca:instanton-tested-chiral-susceptibility-contact}
Keep the same two-flavor source convention, but now let the scalar and
pseudoscalar sources depend on Euclidean position in a finite regulator.  Write
\[
  O_\sigma=\bar q q,\qquad
  O_{\delta_a}=\bar q\tau_a q,\qquad
  O_\eta=\bar q\ii\gamma_5q,\qquad
  O_{\pi_a}=\bar q\ii\gamma_5\tau_aq ,
\]
with the same normalization as the source coordinates
\((s_0,s_a,p_0,p_a)\) above.  For a symmetric test kernel \(F(x,y)\), define
the per-volume tested Euclidean susceptibility coordinate
\begin{equation}
  \chi_A[F]
  =
  \frac{1}{V_4}
  \left.
  \int\dd^4x\,\dd^4y\,
  F(x,y)
  \frac{\delta^2\log Z}{\delta J_A(x)\delta J_A(y)}
  \right|_{J=0},
  \qquad
  F_\Delta=
  \frac{1}{V_4}\int\dd^4x\,F(x,x).
  \label{eq:instanton-tested-susceptibility-definition}
\end{equation}
On a lattice or other cutoff regulator the integrals are the corresponding
finite sums and \(F_\Delta\) is the average diagonal value of the test kernel.
If \(F(x,y)=f(x-y)\) is translation-invariant, then \(F_\Delta=f(0)\); if the
observable is point-split so that the diagonal is removed, \(F_\Delta=0\).

The local part of the one-instanton source functional is
\[
  \log Z_{\rm inst,loc}^{(2)}
  =
  \int\dd^4x\,
  \mathcal W_{\rm inst}^{(2)}(J(x)) ,
\]
up to the derivative-expansion and finite-window remainders already declared
in ControlledApproximation~\ref{ca:two-flavor-instanton-source-susceptibility}.
Two functional derivatives of this local term produce only the regulator
diagonal:
\[
  \left.
  \frac{\delta^2\log Z_{\rm inst,loc}^{(2)}}
       {\delta J_A(x)\delta J_B(y)}
  \right|_{J=0}
  =
  C_{AB}^{\rm inst}\,\delta_\Lambda(x,y).
\]
The nonzero diagonal entries are
\[
  C_{\sigma\sigma}^{\rm inst}
  =
  C_{\pi_a\pi_a}^{\rm inst}
  =
  \kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}\cos\theta,
  \qquad
  C_{\delta_a\delta_a}^{\rm inst}
  =
  C_{\eta\eta}^{\rm inst}
  =
  -\kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}\cos\theta,
\]
and the CP-odd contact mixings are
\[
  C_{\sigma\eta}^{\rm inst}
  =
  -\kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}\sin\theta,
  \qquad
  C_{\delta_a\pi_b}^{\rm inst}
  =
  \kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}\sin\theta\,\delta_{ab}.
\]
Consequently the local instanton contribution to a tested susceptibility is
\begin{equation}
  \chi_{A,{\rm inst,loc}}[F]
  =
  C_{AA}^{\rm inst}\,F_\Delta ,
  \label{eq:instanton-tested-susceptibility-local-contact}
\end{equation}
and, at \(\theta=0\),
\begin{equation}
  \left(\chi_{\pi_a}[F]-\chi_{\delta_a}[F]\right)_{\rm inst,loc}
  =
  \left(\chi_{\sigma}[F]-\chi_{\eta}[F]\right)_{\rm inst,loc}
  =
  2\kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}F_\Delta .
  \label{eq:instanton-tested-u1a-contact-splitting}
\end{equation}

Thus the local 't Hooft calculation contributes the diagonal contact
coordinate of the tested correlator, not the full off-diagonal two-point
function.  A full color-singlet susceptibility difference has the
finite-regulator decomposition
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \chi_{\pi_a-\delta_a}[F]
  &=
  2\kappa_{\rm inst}^{(2)}\cos\theta\,F_\Delta
  +
  \left(\mathsf S_{\pi_a}[F]-\mathsf S_{\delta_a}[F]\right)  \\
  &\qquad
  +
  \left(\mathsf C_{\pi_a}^{\rm ct}[F]-\mathsf C_{\delta_a}^{\rm ct}[F]\right)
  +
  R_{\rm loc}[F]+R_{\rm reg}[F]+R_{\rm IR}[F],
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-tested-susceptibility-full-decomposition}
\end{equation}
with the analogous \(\sigma-\eta\) formula.  Here
\(\mathsf S_A[F]\) is the connected propagated, or spectral, part of the
renormalized color-singlet two-point function after the contact convention has
been chosen; \(\mathsf C_A^{\rm ct}\) records finite local counterterm
conventions; \(R_{\rm loc}\) is the omitted derivative expansion of the
instanton source kernel; \(R_{\rm reg}\) is the cutoff and volume residual;
and \(R_{\rm IR}\) contains long-distance phase information such as Goldstone
poles or screening.  In a finite box the propagated term may be extracted from
the usual Hilbert-space spectral representation of the color-singlet
operators.  The instanton calculation fixes the local \(U(1)_A\)-violating
contact coefficient in that representation.  It does not by itself determine
the spectral weights, pole residues, screening masses, or the continuum
contact convention.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{proposition}[Mixed mass-source expansion of the instanton determinant]
\label{prop:instanton-mass-source-minor-expansion}
In the same \(Q=1\) QCD zero-mode sector, let \(M\) be the mass-overlap
matrix and let \(B\) be the matrix supplied by external bilinear sources or
by a specified zero-mode-paired operator insertion.  Ordinary external fermion
wave packets are represented instead by the differentiated linear-source
construction below.  With
\([N_f]=\{1,\ldots,N_f\}\), write \(M_{I^c,J^c}\) for the submatrix obtained
by deleting the rows \(I\subset [N_f]\) and columns \(J\subset [N_f]\), and
write \(B_{I,J}\) for the corresponding \(I\times J\) source submatrix, both
with increasing orders; empty determinants are \(1\).  Then
\begin{equation}
  \det(M+B)
  =
  \sum_{r=0}^{N_f}
  \sum_{\substack{I,J\subset [N_f]\\ |I|=|J|=r}}
  (-1)^{\sum_{i\in I}i+\sum_{j\in J}j}\,
  \det M_{I^c,J^c}\,
  \det B_{I,J}.
  \label{eq:instanton-mass-source-minor-expansion}
\end{equation}
Thus a correlator with \(r\) zero-mode-paired external insertions is not
obtained by appending those insertions to an already-formed vacuum
determinant.  It is the degree-\(r\) part of the same finite Berezin
determinant; the unobserved \(N_f-r\) zero-mode pairs must be saturated by the
complementary mass minor.  Equivalently, for increasing
\(I=(i_1<\cdots<i_r)\), \(J=(j_1<\cdots<j_r)\), and
\(\pi\in S_r\), the coefficient of
\(\prod_{\ell=1}^r B_{i_\ell,j_{\pi(\ell)}}\) in \(\det(M+B)\) is
\begin{equation}
  (-1)^{\sum I+\sum J}\,
  \operatorname{sgn}(\pi)\,
  \det M_{I^c,J^c}.
  \label{eq:instanton-source-differentiation-minor}
\end{equation}
For \(N_f=2\),
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \det(M+B)
  &=
  \det M
  +M_{22}B_{11}-M_{21}B_{12}
  -M_{12}B_{21}+M_{11}B_{22}  \\
  &\hspace{2.5em}
  +B_{11}B_{22}-B_{12}B_{21}.
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-two-flavor-mass-source-expansion}
\end{equation}
The last line is the massless four-fermion 't Hooft vertex.  The middle line
is the mixed amplitude in which one flavor is supplied by an external
zero-mode pair and the other by a mass insertion.  If a flavor is neither
externally inserted nor present in the complementary mass minor, the
instanton contribution to that correlator vanishes.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Apply the determinant expansion to \(M+B\).  Each contributing permutation
\(\sigma\in S_{N_f}\) chooses, for every row, either an \(M\)-entry or a
\(B\)-entry.  Let \(I\) be the set of rows where a \(B\)-entry was chosen and
let \(J=\sigma(I)\).  Reordering the rows and columns so that the \(B\)-block
appears in the \(I,J\) positions gives the cofactor sign
\((-1)^{\sum I+\sum J}\).  Summing over the restriction of \(\sigma\) to
\(I\) gives \(\det B_{I,J}\), while summing over the complementary
restriction gives \(\det M_{I^c,J^c}\).  This proves
\eqref{eq:instanton-mass-source-minor-expansion}.  Extracting a particular
source monomial from \(\det B_{I,J}\) gives the \(\operatorname{sgn}(\pi)\)
factor in \eqref{eq:instanton-source-differentiation-minor}.  The displayed
two-flavor formula is the specialization to \(N_f=2\).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Fermion determinant factor versus zero-mode determinant]
\label{prop:instanton-fermion-determinant-zero-mode-factorization}
Fix the same finite-regulator \(Q=1\) chart \(z=(a,\rho,U)\) for vectorlike
\(SU(N_c)\) QCD, and add a mass matrix and an even bilinear source.  Let
\(\mathcal K_{\Lambda,z}(M,B)\) be the finite Dirac bilinear between the
right and left fermion coefficient spaces in this background.  Decompose
these finite spaces into instanton zero-mode subspaces and nonzero-mode
complements.  In block form,
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal K_{\Lambda,z}(M,B)
  =
  \begin{pmatrix}
    K_{00} & K_{0{\rm n}}\\
    K_{{\rm n}0} & K_{{\rm nn}}
  \end{pmatrix},
  \label{eq:instanton-fermion-block-operator}
\end{equation}
where \(K_{00}\) acts between the zero-mode coefficient spaces and
\(K_{{\rm nn}}\) acts on the nonzero-mode complements.  If \(K_{{\rm nn}}\)
is invertible, then
\begin{equation}
  \det \mathcal K_{\Lambda,z}(M,B)
  =
  \det K_{{\rm nn}}\,
  \det\!\left(
    K_{00}-K_{0{\rm n}}K_{{\rm nn}}^{-1}K_{{\rm n}0}
  \right).
  \label{eq:instanton-fermion-schur-factorization}
\end{equation}
Thus the finite nonzero-mode fermion determinant and the zero-mode
saturation determinant are separate factors before the collective-coordinate
integral is performed.

In the leading local semiclassical approximation, where the mass/source
bilinear is restricted to the zero-mode subspace after the nonzero modes have
supplied their determinant ratio, the Schur complement in
\eqref{eq:instanton-fermion-schur-factorization} reduces to
\begin{equation}
  K_{00}^{\rm eff}(z)
  =
  M^{0}(z)+B^{0}(z),
  \qquad
  M^{0}_{ff'}(z)=\rho\,M_{ff'}(\mu),
  \qquad
  B^{0}_{ff'}(z)=\rho^3\bar\psi_{Rf}\psi_{Lf'}+\cdots .
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-effective-matrix}
\end{equation}
The dots denote derivative corrections to the local source approximation and
the spin-color contractions fixed by the normalized zero-mode wavefunctions.
More generally, the Schur correction
\(-K_{0{\rm n}}K_{{\rm nn}}^{-1}K_{{\rm n}0}\) is a finite
nonzero-mode-propagator correction in the same regulator and scheme.
Consequently the light-fermion part of a one-instanton chart has the
structure
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S}(z;\mu)\,
  \det K_{00}^{\rm eff}(z),
  \label{eq:instanton-fermion-nonzero-zero-factor}
\end{equation}
after trivial-sector normalization and local counterterms in the scheme
\(\mathcal S\).  The finite factor
\(\mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S}\) is the fermion nonzero-mode
determinant datum.  It is not determined by the Berezin determinant
\(\det(M^{0}+B^{0})\).  In particular, in the diagonal massive vacuum
specialization the factor \(\prod_f(m_f\rho)\) is the zero-mode saturation
determinant; the remaining finite spectral determinant is an additional
input to the physical amplitude.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
At fixed cutoff the fermion path integral is a finite Berezin Gaussian, hence
equals the determinant of its finite bilinear matrix after the chosen
trivial-sector normalization.  Decompose the finite coefficient spaces into
the zero-mode subspace and its complement.  Gaussian integration over the
nonzero-mode variables first gives the Schur complement of the lower-right
block, which is exactly
\eqref{eq:instanton-fermion-schur-factorization}.  The determinant of
\(K_{{\rm nn}}\) is the fermionic part of the nonzero-mode determinant factor
in \(\mathcal W_{\Lambda}^{\rm nz}\).  The determinant of the Schur
complement is the finite Berezin integral over the zero-mode coefficients.
When the source and mass insertions are projected to the zero-mode subspace,
this second determinant is the determinant of \(M^0+B^0\), whose minor
expansion is Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-mass-source-minor-expansion}.
If the source or mass also couples zero and nonzero modes, the same finite
Gaussian integral produces the displayed Schur correction.  Since
\(\det K_{{\rm nn}}\) multiplies every zero-mode minor, no zero-mode algebra
can determine its finite value.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Finite source-frame covariance of the light-fermion determinant]
\label{prop:instanton-light-fermion-source-frame-covariance}
In the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-fermion-determinant-zero-mode-factorization},
write the finite zero-mode source functional as
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal V_{\rm inst}^{0,\mathcal S}(z)
  =
  \mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S}(z;\mu)\,
  \det K_{00}^{\rm eff}(z).
  \label{eq:instanton-light-fermion-source-frame-functional}
\end{equation}
Let \(Z_R,Z_L\in {\rm GL}(N_f,\mathbb C)\) be a finite change of the right and left
zero-mode source frames, so that the same source insertion is represented by
\begin{equation}
  K_{00}^{\rm eff\,\prime}=Z_RK_{00}^{\rm eff}Z_L .
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-source-frame-change}
\end{equation}
Then the same finite-regulator amplitude coordinate is represented only if
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S\,\prime}
  =
  \frac{\mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S}}
       {\det Z_R\,\det Z_L},
  \qquad
  \mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S\,\prime}
  \det K_{00}^{\rm eff\,\prime}
  =
  \mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S}
  \det K_{00}^{\rm eff}.
  \label{eq:instanton-light-fermion-source-frame-covariance}
\end{equation}
If the finite scheme is also changed by a local fermion determinant counterterm
\(\Delta C_{\rm f}(z)\), then the determinant coordinate is instead multiplied
by \(\exp[-\Delta C_{\rm f}(z)]\):
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S'}
  =
  \ee^{-\Delta C_{\rm f}(z)}
  \frac{\mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S}}
       {\det Z_R\,\det Z_L}.
  \label{eq:instanton-light-fermion-counterterm-frame-change}
\end{equation}
Thus a numerical value for
\(\mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S}\) is not a standalone output of
the zero-mode determinant.  It has meaning only together with the finite source
frame, local counterterm convention, and operator normalization used to extract
the physical correlator.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Equation~\eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-source-frame-change} and determinant
multiplicativity give
\[
  \det K_{00}^{\rm eff\,\prime}
  =
  \det Z_R\,\det K_{00}^{\rm eff}\,\det Z_L .
\]
The inverse transformation of
\(\mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S}\) in
\eqref{eq:instanton-light-fermion-source-frame-covariance} is therefore exactly
what preserves the finite product
\eqref{eq:instanton-light-fermion-source-frame-functional}.  A finite local
counterterm changes the regulated determinant density by the exponential of
minus the counterterm difference between the instanton and trivial sectors, as
in \eqref{eq:finite-regulator-instanton-measure-density}; this gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-light-fermion-counterterm-frame-change}.  The final
statement follows because source-frame changes and local counterterms act on
the finite spectral determinant factor, while the Berezin determinant records
only the zero-mode saturation algebra.
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Reference-amplitude calibration of the
light-fermion determinant]
\label{ca:instanton-light-fermion-reference-calibration}
The finite light-fermion determinant factor
\(\mathcal R_{{\rm f},\Lambda}^{\mathcal S}(z;\mu)\) in
Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-light-fermion-source-frame-covariance} can be
computed directly from the nonzero-mode spectrum in the chosen regulator, or it
can be fixed by one reference amplitude and then used as a calibrated
source-family coordinate.  This second route is predictive when the reference
projection has a declared positive noncancellation margin.

Fix one finite source frame and a collective-coordinate window
\(\mathcal U_{\rm win}\).  Let \(H_\alpha(z)\) denote the rest of the
one-instanton integrand for a gauge-invariant source channel
\(\mathcal J_\alpha\): the classical action, collective density, pure-gauge and
heavy-field determinants, zero-mode source coefficient, orientation projection,
and any declared source-to-state overlap.  Choose a reference shape
\(\overline R_{\rm f}(z)\) for the light-fermion nonzero-mode factor and write
the retained coefficient integrals
\begin{equation}
  B_\alpha
  =
  \int_{\mathcal U_{\rm win}}
    \overline R_{\rm f}(z)H_\alpha(z)\,\dd z,
  \qquad
  M_\alpha
  =
  \int_{\mathcal U_{\rm win}}
    |\overline R_{\rm f}(z)H_\alpha(z)|\,\dd z .
  \label{eq:instanton-reference-determinant-basis-integrals}
\end{equation}
If the exact one-instanton contribution in this source family has the form
\begin{equation}
  A_\alpha^{Q=1}
  =
  r_{\rm f}^{\mathcal S}B_\alpha+R_\alpha,
  \qquad
  |R_\alpha|\le E_\alpha ,
  \label{eq:instanton-reference-calibrated-family}
\end{equation}
then a reference observable \(\alpha=0\) with
\begin{equation}
  A_0^{\rm phys}
  =
  r_{\rm f}^{\mathcal S}B_0+R_0,
  \qquad
  |R_0|\le E_0,\qquad B_0\ne0
  \label{eq:instanton-reference-amplitude-input}
\end{equation}
fixes the calibrated prediction
\begin{equation}
  \widehat A_\alpha^{Q=1}
  =
  A_0^{\rm phys}\frac{B_\alpha}{B_0}.
  \label{eq:instanton-reference-amplitude-prediction}
\end{equation}
The residual propagates by the exact identity
\begin{equation}
  A_\alpha^{Q=1}-\widehat A_\alpha^{Q=1}
  =
  R_\alpha-\frac{B_\alpha}{B_0}R_0,
  \qquad
  \left|A_\alpha^{Q=1}-\widehat A_\alpha^{Q=1}\right|
  \le
  E_\alpha+\left|\frac{B_\alpha}{B_0}\right|E_0 .
  \label{eq:instanton-reference-calibration-error}
\end{equation}
Thus the reference channel must supply a noncancellation margin
\begin{equation}
  \kappa_0=\frac{|B_0|}{M_0}>0,
  \qquad
  \left|\frac{B_\alpha}{B_0}\right|
  \le
  \frac{M_\alpha}{\kappa_0 M_0}.
  \label{eq:instanton-reference-noncancellation-margin}
\end{equation}

This is the finite-amplitude meaning of a light-fermion determinant
normalization.  A finite source-frame change multiplies every \(B_\alpha\) in
the same family by the corresponding zero-mode determinant factor and changes
\(r_{\rm f}^{\mathcal S}\) inversely, so the calibrated ratio in
\eqref{eq:instanton-reference-amplitude-prediction} is invariant for reference
and target channels kept in the same frame and local counterterm
scheme.  The controlled scope of the calibration is one overall determinant
coordinate; residual \(z\)-dependence of the determinant, the omitted size
window, the Euclidean-to-physical bridge, and the long-distance spectral matrix
element require separate estimates.  If the reference \(B_0\) is small because
of source or orientation cancellations, the uncertainty is amplified by
\eqref{eq:instanton-reference-calibration-error}; precision use for the
remaining channels therefore requires the margin in
\eqref{eq:instanton-reference-noncancellation-margin}.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Finite-scheme transport of an instanton
determinant constant]
\label{ca:instanton-determinant-scheme-transport}
A quoted instanton determinant constant is meaningful only as part of a
finite scheme datum.  Let \(\mathcal S\) and \(\mathcal S'\) be two
mass-independent finite schemes for the same \(Q=1\) amplitude channel, with
the same classical chart and the same physical external observable.  Write
\[
  X_{\mathcal S}(\mu)=\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\mathcal S}^2(\mu)} .
\]
Suppose the finite coupling-coordinate change, source-zero-mode coordinate
change, and final operator/source projection are
\begin{equation}
  X_{\mathcal S'}=X_{\mathcal S}+\delta_X+r_X,\qquad
  B_{\mathcal S'}=z_B\,\ee^{r_B}B_{\mathcal S},\qquad
  O_{\mathcal S'}=z_O\,\ee^{r_O}O_{\mathcal S},
  \label{eq:instanton-finite-scheme-map}
\end{equation}
with \(z_B,z_O\ne0\).  Here \(B_{\mathcal S}\) denotes the retained
zero-mode/source integral or finite-window source tensor, while
\(O_{\mathcal S}\) is the matrix element, OPE-basis element, or physical
projection coordinate multiplying the instanton coefficient.  Logarithms are
taken in the chosen finite coordinate patch; for a positive activity bound one
uses the same formulas with logarithms of absolute values.  For a purely
Euclidean source coefficient one sets \(z_O=1\).  For a mass-saturated vacuum
term, \(z_B\) is the determinant of the finite mass-coordinate change; for a
four-source amplitude it is the product of the right and left source-frame
determinants.

If the leading one-instanton contribution is represented in scheme
\(\mathcal S\) by
\[
  \mathcal A_{\mathcal S}^{\rm lead}
  =
  C_{\mathcal S}^{\rm det}
  \ee^{-X_{\mathcal S}}
  B_{\mathcal S}O_{\mathcal S},
\]
then the transported determinant constant in \(\mathcal S'\) is
\begin{equation}
  C_{\mathcal S'}^{\rm det,lead}
  =
  \frac{\ee^{\delta_X}}{z_Bz_O}\,
  C_{\mathcal S}^{\rm det}.
  \label{eq:instanton-determinant-finite-scheme-transport}
\end{equation}
Indeed, inserting
\eqref{eq:instanton-determinant-finite-scheme-transport} and dropping the
remainders \(r_X,r_B,r_O\) gives the same leading amplitude coordinate.
Thus one may not change from a Pauli--Villars coupling to another finite
coupling convention, or rescale the external source/operator frame, while
reusing the old numerical determinant constant.

More generally, suppose the actually supplied constant satisfies the
logarithmic transport bound
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  \log C_{\mathcal S'}^{\rm det}
  -
  \log C_{\mathcal S}^{\rm det}
  -
  \delta_X+\log z_B+\log z_O
  \right|
  \le\epsilon_C,
  \label{eq:instanton-determinant-scheme-log-bound}
\end{equation}
and that
\[
  |r_X|\le\epsilon_X,\qquad |r_B|\le\epsilon_B,\qquad
  |r_O|\le\epsilon_O .
\]
Then the leading amplitude coordinates in the two schemes obey
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  \frac{\mathcal A_{\mathcal S'}^{\rm lead}}
       {\mathcal A_{\mathcal S}^{\rm lead}}
  -1
  \right|
  \le
  \exp(\epsilon_C+\epsilon_X+\epsilon_B+\epsilon_O)-1 .
  \label{eq:instanton-determinant-scheme-amplitude-bound}
\end{equation}
This bound is a scheme-transport residual.  It is distinct from the
proper-time determinant residual, the rank/source residual, and the endpoint
tail.  A finite determinant constant in a declared scheme is therefore not a
decorative number attached to the BPST moduli measure; it is an amplitude
coordinate whose compensation against the coupling, source, and operator
coordinates must be checked.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{proposition}[Mass/source RG transport of the instanton vertex]
\label{prop:instanton-mass-source-rg-transport}
Work in a mass-independent renormalization scheme in the same \(Q=1\)
vectorlike QCD chart.  Let \(\gamma_m(g)\) be the anomalous dimension of the
quark mass coordinate in the convention
\begin{equation}
  \mu\frac{\dd M}{\dd\mu}=-\gamma_m(g)M,
  \qquad
  \mu\frac{\dd J}{\dd\mu}=-\gamma_m(g)J,
  \label{eq:instanton-mass-source-running}
\end{equation}
where \(J\) is a renormalized source coordinate coupled to the same chiral
scalar density as the mass matrix.  Let \(M^0(z)=\rho M\), and let
\(J^0(z)\) be the zero-mode projection of \(J\), a linear function of \(J\)
with the same anomalous transport as \(J\).  Let
\(\mathcal R_{\rm f}^{\mathcal S}(z;\mu)\) denote the finite light-fermion
nonzero-mode determinant factor in the source convention of
Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-fermion-determinant-zero-mode-factorization}.
If, at the logarithmic accuracy under consideration,
\begin{equation}
  \left(\mu\partial_\mu+\beta(g)\partial_g\right)
  \log \mathcal R_{\rm f}^{\mathcal S}(z;\mu)
  =
  N_f\,\gamma_m(g),
  \label{eq:instanton-fermion-factor-mass-anomalous-rge}
\end{equation}
then the zero-mode source functional
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal V_{\rm inst}^{0}(z;M,J,\mu)
  =
  \mathcal R_{\rm f}^{\mathcal S}(z;\mu)\,
  \det\!\left(M^0(z)+J^0(z)\right)
  \label{eq:instanton-renormalized-source-functional}
\end{equation}
obeys
\begin{equation}
  \left[
    \mu\partial_\mu+\beta(g)\partial_g
    -\gamma_m(g)
    \sum_{f,f'}
    \left(
      M_{ff'}\frac{\partial}{\partial M_{ff'}}
      +J_{ff'}\frac{\partial}{\partial J_{ff'}}
    \right)
  \right]
  \mathcal V_{\rm inst}^{0}
  =
  0 .
  \label{eq:instanton-source-functional-rge}
\end{equation}
Thus the mass/source determinant is not an RG-invariant number by itself.
The source functional is covariant only after the finite nonzero-mode
determinant factor and the source renormalization convention are included.
The symbol \(J\) denotes the source coordinate before differentiation.  The
scalar-density operator obtained after differentiating the generating
functional uses the corresponding operator normalization; in the local
operator convention that differentiated insertion has the
\(B^0_{ff'}=\rho^3\bar\psi_{Rf}\psi_{Lf'}+\cdots\) normalization of
\eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-effective-matrix}.

In particular, for diagonal masses and \(J=0\), the anomalous-dimension part
of the vacuum factor
\[
  \mathcal R_{\rm f}^{\mathcal S}(\mu)\prod_{f=1}^{N_f}m_f(\mu)
\]
is scale invariant at the same logarithmic accuracy.  The phase
\(\theta+\arg\det M\) is unaffected by the positive real mass
renormalization factor; it is fixed instead by the anomalous chiral rotation
described in \eqref{eq:qcd-physical-theta}.  After differentiating
\eqref{eq:instanton-renormalized-source-functional} \(r\) times with respect
to \(J\) and setting \(J=0\), the resulting mixed mass/source minor has the
RG covariance of an \(r\)-fold insertion of the renormalized scalar density,
rather than the covariance of a vacuum activity.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The matrix \(M^0(z)+J^0(z)\) is homogeneous of degree one in the source
coordinates \(M\) and \(J\), while the projection factors depending on
\(\rho\), \(U\), and the normalized zero-mode wavefunctions are collective
coordinate data and are not acted on by the source anomalous dimension.  The
determinant is therefore homogeneous of degree \(N_f\):
\[
  \sum_{f,f'}
  \left(
    M_{ff'}\frac{\partial}{\partial M_{ff'}}
    +J_{ff'}\frac{\partial}{\partial J_{ff'}}
  \right)
  \det(M^0+J^0)
  =
  N_f\det(M^0+J^0).
\]
Combining this identity with
\eqref{eq:instanton-fermion-factor-mass-anomalous-rge} gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-source-functional-rge}.  Setting \(J=0\) gives the
vacuum statement.  Differentiating the source-functional equation \(r\) times
with respect to \(J\) transfers \(r\) source anomalous-dimension terms from
the transport operator to the differentiated coefficient, which is the usual
Callan--Symanzik covariance of \(r\) renormalized scalar-density insertions.
The phase statement follows from a separate observation.  In a vectorlike
mass-independent scheme, multiplicative mass renormalization changes the
magnitude of \(M\).  The anomalous flavor-singlet chiral rotation changes
\(\arg\det M\) and \(\theta\) in opposite directions.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Proper-time determinant and zero-mode source functional]
\label{prop:instanton-proper-time-four-fermion-amplitude}
Fix a finite-regulator \(Q=1\) chart \(z=(a,\rho,U)\), a background gauge
slice, and a proper-time determinant prescription with renormalization scale
\(\mu\).  For each positive nonzero-mode operator \(P_{\Lambda,z}\) in the
instanton background, compared with the corresponding operator
\(P_{\Lambda,0}\) in the trivial sector, define the regulated logarithmic
determinant ratio by
\begin{equation}
  K_\Lambda(P_z,P_0;\mu)
  =
  -\int_{\epsilon_\Lambda}^{\infty}
    \frac{\dd t}{t}\,r(t\mu^2)
    \left(
      \operatorname{Tr}' e^{-tP_{\Lambda,z}}
      -
      \operatorname{Tr} e^{-tP_{\Lambda,0}}
    \right)
  +C_{\Lambda,P}^{\rm loc}(z;\mu),
  \label{eq:proper-time-instanton-determinant-ratio}
\end{equation}
where \(r\) is a smooth cutoff profile with \(r(0)=1\), the prime removes
collective-coordinate, residual-gauge, and fermion zero modes as appropriate,
and \(C_{\Lambda,P}^{\rm loc}\) is the chosen local subtraction in the
instanton background relative to the trivial background.  The determinant
density in \eqref{eq:finite-regulator-instanton-measure-density} is then
\begin{equation}
  \log \mathcal W_{\Lambda,{\rm pt}}^{\rm nz}(z;\mu)
  =
  K_\Lambda(M_z^{\rm gh},M_0^{\rm gh};\mu)
  -\frac12 K_\Lambda(L_z^{\rm bos},L_0^{\rm bos};\mu)
  +\sum_R K_\Lambda^{\rm pf,R}(z,0;\mu),
  \label{eq:proper-time-instanton-Wnz}
\end{equation}
with \(K_\Lambda^{\rm pf,R}\) the Pfaffian or determinant-line version of the
same nonzero-mode construction for the fermion multiplet \(R\).

For two massless Dirac flavors there are two distinct source constructions.
An even bilinear source supplies an independent finite matrix \(B(z)\) in the
zero-mode action \(\sum_{f,f'}\widetilde\lambda_f B_{ff'}(z)\lambda_{f'}\);
its zero-mode factor is \(\det B(z)\), as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-thooft-determinant-zero-mode-amplitude}.  Ordinary
external fermion wave packets are instead introduced by odd generating
coordinates.  Let \(\bar\chi_A,\chi_B\), \(A,B=1,2\), be the four external
source coordinates and set
\begin{equation}
  \alpha_f(z)=\sum_{A=1}^{2}\bar\chi_A R_{Af}(z),
  \qquad
  \beta_f(z)=\sum_{B=1}^{2}L_{fB}(z)\chi_B,
  \label{eq:zero-mode-linear-source-overlaps}
\end{equation}
where \(R_{Af}\) and \(L_{fB}\) are the zero-mode overlaps of the \(A\)th
right-handed and \(B\)th left-handed external slots with the normalized
instanton zero-mode wavefunction.  With the same Berezin orientation used in
\eqref{eq:thooft-vertex-berezin-determinant}, the differentiated source
coefficient is
\begin{equation}
  [\bar\chi_1\bar\chi_2\chi_1\chi_2]\,
  \prod_{f=1}^{2}\alpha_f(z)\prod_{f=1}^{2}\beta_f(z)
  =
  \det R(z)\,\det L(z).
  \label{eq:zero-mode-differentiated-four-slot-coefficient}
\end{equation}
Thus the one-instanton generating-functional contribution is
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \mathcal G_{\eta,\Lambda,Q=1}^{(4)}[\bar\chi,\chi]
  &=
  \int_{\mathcal U_{Q=1}}
  \exp[-S_\Lambda(A_z)+\ii\theta]\,
  \mathcal W_{\Lambda,{\rm pt}}^{\rm nz}(z;\mu)\,
  \prod_{f=1}^{2}\alpha_f(z)\prod_{f=1}^{2}\beta_f(z)\,
  \dd\nu_{\Lambda,\mathcal M}(z),\\
  G^{(4)}_{\eta,\Lambda,Q=1}
  &=
  [\bar\chi_1\bar\chi_2\chi_1\chi_2]\,
  \mathcal G_{\eta,\Lambda,Q=1}^{(4)}[\bar\chi,\chi].
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:proper-time-four-fermion-instanton-amplitude}
\end{equation}
A c-number matrix formed as a single outer product \(u_fv_{f'}\) is not this
four-slot coefficient; for \(N_f=2\) its determinant vanishes.  The
small-\(t\) expansion of
\eqref{eq:proper-time-instanton-determinant-ratio} supplies the local
counterterms and the universal \((\mu\rho)^{b_0}\) factor, while the finite
remainder fixes the scheme-dependent numerical constant in the selected
source functional.  Thus the physics calculation consists of the regulated
fluctuation determinant, the zero-mode source differentiation, and the
collective-coordinate integral as a single object.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For a finite positive operator \(P\), the identity
\(\log\det P=-\int_{\epsilon}^{\infty}\dd t\,t^{-1}\operatorname{Tr}e^{-tP}\)
holds up to the subtraction convention at the lower endpoint.  Applying this
identity to the instanton and trivial-sector operators and adding the chosen
local counterterm gives
\eqref{eq:proper-time-instanton-determinant-ratio}.  Bosonic Gaussian
integration contributes the exponent \(-1/2\), ghost Berezin integration
contributes \(+1\), and fermionic nonzero modes contribute the Pfaffian or
determinant-line factor, giving
\eqref{eq:proper-time-instanton-Wnz}.  Zero modes have already been removed
from the traces and determinants, so their finite Berezin integral is exactly
the calculation in
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-thooft-determinant-zero-mode-amplitude} for an even
bilinear source matrix.  For linear external sources, expanding
\(\prod_f\alpha_f\prod_f\beta_f\) and extracting the
\(\bar\chi_1\bar\chi_2\chi_1\chi_2\) coefficient gives
\(\det R\,\det L\); this is the source-differentiated correlator coefficient,
not the determinant of a single c-number outer product.  Multiplication by the
collective-coordinate density and the classical instanton exponential gives
\eqref{eq:proper-time-four-fermion-instanton-amplitude}.  Finally, the
heat-kernel expansion of the trace difference at small \(t\) separates local
counterterms, the coefficient of \(\log(\mu\rho)\), and the finite
determinant constant; RG invariance identifies the universal logarithmic
coefficient with \(b_0\) in the displayed one-loop density.
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Proper-time determinant residual on an amplitude window]
\label{ca:instanton-proper-time-determinant-residual-window}
The proper-time determinant in
Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-proper-time-four-fermion-amplitude} becomes
useful for a physical source amplitude only after its finite remainder is
controlled uniformly on the same collective-coordinate window as the
zero-mode and source estimates.  Fix a window \(\mathcal U_{\rm win}\) in a
one-instanton chart and write, after the local heat-kernel subtraction and
the universal \(b_0\log(\mu\rho)\) term have been separated,
\[
  \log\mathcal W_{\Lambda,{\rm pt}}^{\rm nz}(z;\mu)
  =
  \log\mathcal W_{{\rm lead}}^{\rm nz}(z;\mu)
  +\delta_{\rm det}(z),
  \qquad z\in\mathcal U_{\rm win}.
\]
For each fluctuation block \(j\) let \(c_j\) be its logarithmic weight:
\[
  c_{\rm gh}=1,\qquad c_{\rm bos}=-\frac12,\qquad
  c_{\rm pf,R}=1
\]
with the Pfaffian or determinant-line pairing convention already fixed.  A
determinant-residual bound on \(\mathcal U_{\rm win}\) is a collection
of trace-remainder bounds
\[
  \left|
    \int_{\epsilon_\Lambda}^{\infty}
    \frac{\dd t}{t}\,r(t\mu^2)\,
    \delta T_{j,\Lambda}(t,z)
  \right|
  \le \epsilon_j,
  \qquad z\in\mathcal U_{\rm win},
\]
where \(\delta T_{j,\Lambda}\) is the remaining trace difference after the
declared local subtraction and leading determinant datum have been removed.
It gives the uniform logarithmic bound
\begin{equation}
  |\delta_{\rm det}(z)|
  \le
  \epsilon_{\rm det}:=\sum_j |c_j|\epsilon_j .
  \label{eq:instanton-proper-time-determinant-log-bound}
\end{equation}
Consequently the multiplicative determinant error satisfies
\begin{equation}
  \left|
    \mathcal W_{\Lambda,{\rm pt}}^{\rm nz}(z;\mu)
    -
    \mathcal W_{{\rm lead}}^{\rm nz}(z;\mu)
  \right|
  \le
  \left|\mathcal W_{{\rm lead}}^{\rm nz}(z;\mu)\right|
  \left(e^{\epsilon_{\rm det}}-1\right).
  \label{eq:instanton-proper-time-determinant-multiplicative-bound}
\end{equation}
Thus the determinant part of the amplitude error budget obeys
\begin{equation}
  |R_{\rm det}|
  \le
  \left(e^{\epsilon_{\rm det}}-1\right)
  \int_{\mathcal U_{\rm win}}
  |\mathcal K_{\rm lead}(z)|\,\dd z ,
  \label{eq:instanton-proper-time-determinant-amplitude-bound}
\end{equation}
provided the leading kernel contains the same zero-mode source coefficient,
collective density, and local counterterm convention.

This is the finite-regulator form of the fluctuation calculation hidden in a
``determinant constant.''  A signed cancellation among the ghost, bosonic,
and fermionic trace remainders is weaker than
\eqref{eq:instanton-proper-time-determinant-log-bound}; the amplitude bound
uses absolute logarithmic control because the determinant multiplies the
zero-mode source coefficient pointwise over the size and orientation window.
The finite constant may be pulled outside the instanton size integral only
when the same residual bound also controls the residual \(z\)-dependence of the
finite determinant over that window.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{proposition}[Instanton zero-mode density form factor and local limit]
\label{prop:instanton-zero-mode-tail-local-limit}
In a BPST \(Q=1\) background, after the spin and color tensors of one
fundamental zero-mode line are factored out, the radial scalar envelope which
weights a local mass, Yukawa, or bilinear source is
\begin{equation}
  h_\rho(y)
  =
  \frac{2\rho^2}{\pi^2(y^2+\rho^2)^3},
  \qquad
  \int_{\mathbb R^4}h_\rho(y)\,\dd^4y=1 .
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-envelope}
\end{equation}
Thus a zero-mode-paired source matrix entry has the form
\begin{equation}
  B_{ff'}^{(s)}(a,\rho,U)
  =
  \rho^{d_s}
  \int_{\mathbb R^4}
  h_\rho(y)\,
  \mathcal B_{ff'}(a+y;U)\,\dd^4y ,
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-source-convolution}
\end{equation}
where \(d_s=1\) for a mass source and \(d_s=3\) for the local quark-bilinear
source in \eqref{eq:qcd-thooft-vertex-leading-local}.  Equivalently, with
the Fourier convention
\[
  \widehat h_\rho(q)=
  \int_{\mathbb R^4}\ee^{\ii q\cdot y}h_\rho(y)\,\dd^4y ,
\]
one has the exact form factor
\begin{equation}
  \widehat h_\rho(q)
  =
  zK_1(z),
  \qquad z=\rho |q|,
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-momentum-form-factor}
\end{equation}
where \(K_1\) is the modified Bessel function.  Hence a zero-mode-paired
source with Fourier momentum \(q\) is not represented by the local vertex
until \(z\ll1\).
The small-momentum expansion is
\begin{equation}
  zK_1(z)
  =
  1+
  \frac{z^2}{2}
  \left[
    \log\frac{z}{2}+\gamma_{\rm E}-\frac12
  \right]
  +O(z^4\log z),
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-form-factor-small-momentum}
\end{equation}
so the first nonlocal correction is \(q^2\rho^2\log(|q|\rho)\), not an
ordinary analytic Taylor coefficient.  At \(z\gg1\),
\begin{equation}
  zK_1(z)
  =
  \sqrt{\frac{\pi z}{2}}\,
  \ee^{-z}
  \left(1+\frac{3}{8z}+O(z^{-2})\right),
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-form-factor-large-momentum}
\end{equation}
which displays the suppression of source components varying on scales
shorter than the instanton size.  This is the density form factor for a local
bilinear or mass-source insertion.  A differentiated correlator with four
ordinary external fermion slots instead uses the Fourier transforms of the
individual zero-mode wavefunctions in those slots; their product reduces to
the local bilinear density only after the slot wavefunctions are fused into a
bilinear source and the local limit is taken.  In position space, for
\(U_R=R/\rho\),
\begin{equation}
  \int_{|y|<R}h_\rho(y)\,\dd^4y
  =
  \frac{U_R^4}{(1+U_R^2)^2},
  \qquad
  \int_{|y|>R}h_\rho(y)\,\dd^4y
  =
  \frac{1+2U_R^2}{(1+U_R^2)^2}.
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-tail-mass}
\end{equation}
The first correction to a local Taylor expansion is more delicate.  The
truncated second moment is
\begin{equation}
  M_2(R)
  :=
  \int_{|y|<R}|y|^2h_\rho(y)\,\dd^4y
  =
  2\rho^2
  \left[
    \log(1+U_R^2)
    +\frac{2}{1+U_R^2}
    -\frac{1}{2(1+U_R^2)^2}
    -\frac32
  \right],
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-second-moment}
\end{equation}
and rotational invariance gives
\[
  \int_{|y|<R}y^\mu y^\nu h_\rho(y)\,\dd^4y
  =
  \frac{\delta^{\mu\nu}}4M_2(R).
\]
Consequently the leading local term in
\eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-source-convolution} is
\(\rho^{d_s}\mathcal B_{ff'}(a;U)\), with a tail bounded by the second
quantity in \eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-tail-mass}.  But the would-be
two-derivative coefficient grows as
\(4\rho^2\log(R/\rho)+O(\rho^2)\) as \(R/\rho\to\infty\).  The local
't Hooft vertex is therefore the zeroth adiabatic term of the zero-mode
source convolution; higher-derivative terms require the external wave-packet,
mass, or infrared regulator that cuts off the zero-mode tail.  In momentum
space the same statement is the logarithm in
\eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-form-factor-small-momentum}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The normalized radial envelope in \eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-envelope} is
the scalar part of the product of two normalized fundamental zero-mode
wavefunctions in the BPST background.  Using
\(\dd^4y=2\pi^2r^3\dd r\) and \(u=r/\rho\),
\[
  \int_{\mathbb R^4}h_\rho(y)\,\dd^4y
  =
  4\int_0^\infty\frac{u^3}{(1+u^2)^3}\,\dd u
  =
  1.
\]
For the Fourier transform, use the Schwinger representation
\[
  \frac1{(y^2+\rho^2)^3}
  =
  \frac12\int_0^\infty s^2\ee^{-s(y^2+\rho^2)}\,\dd s .
\]
Then
\[
\begin{aligned}
  \widehat h_\rho(q)
  &=
  \rho^2\int_0^\infty
  \exp\!\left[-\rho^2s-\frac{q^2}{4s}\right]\dd s  \\
  &=
  \rho |q|\,K_1(\rho |q|),
\end{aligned}
\]
where the last step is the standard integral representation of the modified
Bessel function.  The small-\(z\) and large-\(z\) formulas are the
corresponding standard asymptotic expansions of \(K_1\); the logarithmic
small-\(z\) term is the momentum-space reflection of the logarithmically
divergent second moment computed below.

The same integral cut off at \(U_R\) gives
\[
  4\int_0^{U_R}\frac{u^3}{(1+u^2)^3}\,\dd u
  =
  1-\frac{2}{1+U_R^2}
  +\frac{1}{(1+U_R^2)^2}
  =
  \frac{U_R^4}{(1+U_R^2)^2},
\]
and subtracting from one gives the tail formula in
\eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-tail-mass}.  For the second moment,
\[
  M_2(R)
  =
  4\rho^2\int_0^{U_R}\frac{u^5}{(1+u^2)^3}\,\dd u .
\]
With \(t=1+u^2\), this antiderivative is
\[
  2\rho^2
  \left[
    \log t+\frac2t-\frac{1}{2t^2}-\frac32
  \right]_{t=1}^{1+U_R^2},
\]
which is \eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-second-moment}.  Rotational
invariance in four Euclidean dimensions gives the displayed
\(\delta^{\mu\nu}/4\) tensor moment.  The Taylor expansion of
\(\mathcal B(a+y;U)\) then yields the zeroth local term and the
\((M_2(R)/8)\partial^2\mathcal B(a;U)\) contribution inside the ball
\(|y|<R\), while the exterior contribution is controlled by the tail mass
times the appropriate supremum norm of the source.  Since
\(\log(1+U_R^2)=2\log(R/\rho)+o(1)\), the full second moment is
logarithmically infrared sensitive.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Individual BPST zero-mode slot form factor]
\label{prop:instanton-individual-zero-mode-form-factor}
For an ordinary external fermion slot one must use the Fourier transform of a
single normalized BPST zero-mode wavefunction, not the density form factor
\(\widehat h_\rho\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-zero-mode-tail-local-limit}.  In the standard
singular-gauge momentum-space convention for a charge-one instanton
\cite{tHooft1976Pseudoparticle,DiakonovPetrov1986InstantonVacuum}, the
spin-color tensor and the scalar radial function separate as
\begin{equation}
  \widetilde\psi_{0,i}^{\alpha}(p;\rho,U)
  =
  \sqrt2\,\phi_\rho'(|p|)
  \bigl(\widehat p\,\epsilon U\bigr)_{i}^{\alpha},
  \qquad
  \phi_\rho(p)
  =
  \pi\rho^2
  \bigl[I_0(t)K_0(t)-I_1(t)K_1(t)\bigr],
  \quad
  t=\frac{\rho |p|}{2}.
  \label{eq:instanton-momentum-zero-mode-wavefunction}
\end{equation}
Here \(I_\nu\) and \(K_\nu\) are modified Bessel functions, \(U\) is the color
orientation, and \(\widehat p=p/|p|\).  After the adjacent free Dirac operator
and fixed Fourier-normalization constants are assigned to the external-slot
amputation convention, the dimensionless scalar slot form factor is
\begin{equation}
  F_{\rm zm}(t)
  :=
  -t\frac{\dd}{\dd t}
  \bigl[I_0(t)K_0(t)-I_1(t)K_1(t)\bigr]
  =
  2t\bigl[I_0(t)K_1(t)-I_1(t)K_0(t)\bigr]
  -2I_1(t)K_1(t).
  \label{eq:instanton-individual-zero-mode-form-factor}
\end{equation}
It is normalized by
\begin{equation}
  F_{\rm zm}(0)=1,
  \label{eq:instanton-individual-zero-mode-form-factor-local}
\end{equation}
while at large momentum
\begin{equation}
  F_{\rm zm}(t)
  =
  \frac{3}{4t^3}+O(t^{-5})
  =
  \frac{6}{(\rho |p|)^3}+O((\rho |p|)^{-5}).
  \label{eq:instanton-individual-zero-mode-form-factor-large}
\end{equation}
Thus the individual external zero-mode slot has a power tail.  The exponential
large-momentum suppression in
\eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-form-factor-large-momentum} belongs to the fused
bilinear density \(h_\rho\), not to a single differentiated fermion slot.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The first formula is the standard Fourier-Bessel transform of the normalized
singular-gauge fundamental zero mode after its hedgehog spin-color tensor has
been extracted.  Differentiating
\(\Phi(t)=I_0(t)K_0(t)-I_1(t)K_1(t)\) and using
\[
  I_0'=I_1,\qquad
  I_1'=I_0-\frac{I_1}{t},\qquad
  K_0'=-K_1,\qquad
  K_1'=-K_0-\frac{K_1}{t}
\]
gives the second expression in
\eqref{eq:instanton-individual-zero-mode-form-factor}.  The small-\(t\)
expansions \(I_0(t)=1+O(t^2)\), \(I_1(t)=t/2+O(t^3)\), and
\(K_1(t)=t^{-1}+O(t\log t)\) give \(F_{\rm zm}(0)=1\).  The standard large-\(t\)
asymptotic expansions of \(I_\nu\) and \(K_\nu\) show that the constant,
\(t^{-1}\), and \(t^{-2}\) terms cancel in
\eqref{eq:instanton-individual-zero-mode-form-factor}; the first nonzero term
is \(3/(4t^3)\).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Amputation and source typing of the instanton kernel]
\label{prop:instanton-external-leg-amputation-kernel}
Work in the finite-regulator \(Q=1\) chart of
Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-proper-time-four-fermion-amplitude}, and
suppose an auxiliary infrared deformation or source scheme has been chosen in
which the external quark fields used to probe the kernel have isolated
nonzero external pole-residue factors.  For differentiated linear source
slots, let \(Z^R_A(p_{R,A})\) and \(Z^L_B(p_{L,B})\) be the adjacent
unamputated pole residues for the two right-handed and two left-handed slots.
After the spin and color external covectors are fixed, write the zero-mode
overlap matrices as
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  R^{\rm unamp}_{Af}(z)
  &=
  Z^R_A(p_{R,A})\,R^{\rm amp}_{Af}(z),\\
  L^{\rm unamp}_{fB}(z)
  &=
  L^{\rm amp}_{fB}(z)\,Z^L_B(p_{L,B}),
  \qquad A,B,f=1,2 .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-amputated-linear-source-matrices}
\end{equation}
The four-slot coefficient from
\eqref{eq:zero-mode-differentiated-four-slot-coefficient} obeys
\begin{equation}
  \det R^{\rm unamp}(z)\det L^{\rm unamp}(z)
  =
  \left(\prod_{A=1}^{2}Z^R_A\right)
  \left(\prod_{B=1}^{2}Z^L_B\right)
  \det R^{\rm amp}(z)\det L^{\rm amp}(z).
  \label{eq:instanton-source-determinant-amputation}
\end{equation}
Consequently the source-amputated differentiated four-fermion kernel is
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal M^{(4),{\rm amp}}_{\Lambda,Q=1}
  =
  \int_{\mathcal U_{Q=1}}
  \exp[-S_\Lambda(A_z)+\ii\theta]\,
  \mathcal W_{\Lambda,{\rm pt}}^{\rm nz}(z;\mu)\,
  \det R^{\rm amp}(z)\det L^{\rm amp}(z)\,
  \dd\nu_{\Lambda,\mathcal M}(z).
  \label{eq:instanton-amputated-four-fermion-kernel}
\end{equation}
Amputation removes only the adjacent external propagator residues.  It does
not remove the individual instanton zero-mode Fourier overlaps, the spin-color
orientation tensors, the nonzero-mode determinant, or the
collective-coordinate integral.

For an independent even bilinear source matrix the source type is different.
If \(B^{\rm unamp}=D_RB^{\rm amp}D_L\), with \(D_R,D_L\) diagonal residue
matrices in flavor space, then
\begin{equation}
  \det B^{\rm unamp}
  =
  \det D_R\,\det B^{\rm amp}\,\det D_L .
  \label{eq:instanton-bilinear-source-determinant-amputation}
\end{equation}
For a local bilinear source carrying momentum \(q_{ff'}\), the BPST density
form factor of Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-zero-mode-tail-local-limit}
gives a representative entry
\begin{equation}
  B^{\rm amp}_{ff'}(a,\rho,U)
  =
  \rho^3
  \ee^{\ii q_{ff'}\cdot a}\,
  \widehat h_\rho(q_{ff'})\,
  \mathcal T_{ff'}(U;q_{ff'}),
  \qquad
  q_{ff'}=p_{R,f}-p_{L,f'} .
  \label{eq:instanton-amputated-source-matrix}
\end{equation}
This bilinear-source formula is not the determinant of a single c-number
outer product of external wave packets.  Ordinary external fermions use
\eqref{eq:instanton-amputated-linear-source-matrices} and the source
differentiation in
\eqref{eq:zero-mode-differentiated-four-slot-coefficient}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The linear source overlaps in \eqref{eq:zero-mode-linear-source-overlaps}
attach each external slot to one normalized zero-mode wavefunction.  The
chosen infrared scheme supplies one adjacent pole residue per external slot;
removing those residues gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-amputated-linear-source-matrices}.  Applying the
determinant to the right-slot matrix and to the left-slot matrix gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-source-determinant-amputation}.  Multiplying the
unamputated differentiated Green kernel by the inverse product of the same
four residues therefore gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-amputated-four-fermion-kernel}.

For an even bilinear source, the zero-mode action already contains a matrix
entry \(B_{ff'}\).  Row and column residue factors then multiply that matrix
on the left and right, so ordinary determinant multiplicativity gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-bilinear-source-determinant-amputation}.  The density
form factor in \eqref{eq:instanton-amputated-source-matrix} comes from the
product of two zero-mode wavefunctions in a fused bilinear source.  Linear
external slots are differentiated before the sources are set to zero, so a
single rank-one c-number matrix never appears as the four-fermion coefficient.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Plane-wave assembly of the one-instanton four-fermion
amplitude]
\label{prop:instanton-plane-wave-four-fermion-assembly}
Stay in the \(N_f=2\) source-amputated setup of
Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-external-leg-amputation-kernel}, and suppose
the center coordinate factorizes from the regulated collective-coordinate
density:
\[
  \dd\nu_{\Lambda,\mathcal M}(z)
  =
  \mathcal J_\Lambda(\rho,U)\,
  \dd^4a\,\dd\rho\,\dd\Omega(U).
\]
Let
\[
  \mathcal P
  =
  \sum_{A=1}^{2}p_{R,A}
  -
  \sum_{B=1}^{2}p_{L,B}.
\]
For plane-wave external slots, write the individual amputated zero-mode
overlaps in the form
\[
  R^{\rm amp}_{Af}(a,\rho,U)
  =
  \rho^{3/2}\ee^{\ii p_{R,A}\cdot a}
  \mathcal R_{Af}(\rho,U;p_{R,A}),
  \qquad
  L^{\rm amp}_{fB}(a,\rho,U)
  =
  \rho^{3/2}\ee^{-\ii p_{L,B}\cdot a}
  \mathcal L_{fB}(\rho,U;p_{L,B}),
\]
where \(\mathcal R\) and \(\mathcal L\) are obtained from the Fourier
transforms of the individual normalized zero-mode wavefunctions, with the
chosen spin-color external covectors already contracted.  Then the
source-differentiated zero-mode coefficient in
\eqref{eq:instanton-amputated-four-fermion-kernel} has the factorized form
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \det R^{\rm amp}(a,\rho,U)\det L^{\rm amp}(a,\rho,U)
  &=
  \rho^6\,
  \ee^{\ii\mathcal P\cdot a}\,
  \mathfrak A_2^{\rm lin}(\rho,U;\{p_R,p_L\}),\\
  \mathfrak A_2^{\rm lin}
  &=
  \det\mathcal R(\rho,U;\{p_R\})\,
  \det\mathcal L(\rho,U;\{p_L\}).
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-plane-wave-source-determinant}
\end{equation}
A separate bilinear-source specialization is obtained by inserting
\eqref{eq:instanton-amputated-source-matrix} into \(\det B^{\rm amp}\).  In
that case \(F(z)=zK_1(z)\) appears through the density form factor and
\[
  \det B^{\rm amp}
  =
  \rho^6\ee^{\ii\mathcal P\cdot a}
  \left[
    F(\rho|q_{11}|)F(\rho|q_{22}|)
    \mathcal T_{11}\mathcal T_{22}
    -
    F(\rho|q_{12}|)F(\rho|q_{21}|)
    \mathcal T_{12}\mathcal T_{21}
  \right],
  \qquad q_{ff'}=p_{R,f}-p_{L,f'} ,
\]
provided \(B^{\rm amp}\) is an independent bilinear source matrix.  If
\(B^{\rm amp}_{ff'}=u_fv_{f'}\) is only a c-number outer product, the
two-flavor determinant is zero.
