Consequently the center integral in infinite volume gives the distributional
factor
\begin{equation}
  \int_{\mathbb R^4}\dd^4a\,
  \ee^{\ii\mathcal P\cdot a}
  =
  (2\pi)^4\delta^{(4)}(\mathcal P),
  \label{eq:instanton-center-momentum-conservation}
\end{equation}
and the source-amputated one-instanton contribution may be written as
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \mathcal M^{(4),{\rm amp}}_{\Lambda,Q=1}
  &=
  \ee^{\ii\theta}
  (2\pi)^4\delta^{(4)}(\mathcal P)
  \int
  \exp[-S_\Lambda(A_{\rho,U})]\,
  \mathcal W_{\Lambda,{\rm pt}}^{\rm nz}(\rho,U;\mu) \\
  &\qquad\qquad\qquad
  {}\times
  \rho^6\,
  \mathfrak A_2^{\rm lin}(\rho,U;\{p_R,p_L\})\,
  \mathcal J_\Lambda(\rho,U)\,
  \dd\rho\,\dd\Omega(U).
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-plane-wave-four-fermion-amplitude}
\end{equation}
The anti-instanton term has the conjugate chirality structure and the phase
\(\ee^{-\ii\theta}\).

Thus the instanton calculation does not first create a local vertex and then
decorate it.  The finite-regulator amplitude is assembled from four
load-bearing pieces: the center integral, the individual zero-mode
Fourier-overlap tensors, the nonzero-mode determinant, and the size integral.
The local 't Hooft operator is obtained only after the external slots have
been fused into a local bilinear source, the support of the \(\rho\)-integral
lies in the small-momentum regime of the relevant zero-mode form factors, and
the determinant remainder has been replaced by the finite constant of the
chosen scheme.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
In \(\det R^{\rm amp}\), both permutation terms contain the same phase
\(\ee^{\ii(p_{R,1}+p_{R,2})\cdot a}\).  In \(\det L^{\rm amp}\), both
permutation terms contain the same phase
\(\ee^{-\ii(p_{L,1}+p_{L,2})\cdot a}\).  The product therefore carries
\(\ee^{\ii\mathcal P\cdot a}\).  The four individual zero-mode overlaps carry
the conventional total power \(\rho^6\), leaving
\(\det\mathcal R\,\det\mathcal L\) as the nontrivial form-factor and
orientation coefficient.  This proves
\eqref{eq:instanton-plane-wave-source-determinant}.  Translation invariance of
the center coordinate then gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-center-momentum-conservation} in infinite volume, or the
corresponding Kronecker delta on a finite periodic regulator.  Substituting the
factorized coefficient and collective-coordinate density into
\eqref{eq:instanton-amputated-four-fermion-kernel} gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-plane-wave-four-fermion-amplitude}.  The bilinear-source
formula follows from the same phase count applied to
\eqref{eq:instanton-amputated-source-matrix}; the final rank-one warning is
the elementary identity \(\det(u v^T)=0\) for two-component c-number vectors.
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Hard wave-packet support in the four-slot
instanton kernel]
\label{ca:instanton-hard-wave-packet-source-support}
The plane-wave formula above is a useful coordinate, but a physical hard
source is a wave packet or a source smearing.  In the source-amputated
\(N_f=2\) setup, replace the plane-wave slot covectors by wave packets and
write the reduced zero-mode overlap matrices, after extracting the explicit
\(\rho^{3/2}\) from each slot, as
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \mathcal R_{Af}(\rho,U)
  &=
  \int \widehat f^R_A(p)\,
  F_{\rm zm}(\rho |p|/2)\,
  \mathcal T^R_{Af}(\widehat p,U)\,\dd\Pi_R(p),\\
  \mathcal L_{fB}(\rho,U)
  &=
  \int
  F_{\rm zm}(\rho |p|/2)\,
  \mathcal T^L_{fB}(\widehat p,U)\,
  \widehat f^L_B(p)\,\dd\Pi_L(p),
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-wave-packet-zero-mode-overlaps}
\end{equation}
where \(\dd\Pi_{R,L}\) denote the chosen finite-regulator momentum measures
and \(\mathcal T^{R,L}\) contain the spin-color tensors and source
normalizations.  Suppose each slot is supported in a hard annulus
\[
  c_-Q\le |p|\le c_+Q,\qquad c_->0,
\]
and suppose the source tensors and wave packets give row-norm bounds
\begin{equation}
  \sum_f|\mathcal R_{Af}(\rho,U)|^2\le
  C^2_{R,A}(1+c_-Q\rho)^{-6},
  \qquad
  \sum_f|\mathcal L_{fB}(\rho,U)|^2\le
  C^2_{L,B}(1+c_-Q\rho)^{-6}.
  \label{eq:instanton-wave-packet-row-bound}
\end{equation}
Such a bound follows, for example, from the large-slot estimate
\(|F_{\rm zm}(t)|\le C_{\rm zm}(1+t)^{-3}\) together with bounded source
norms.  Hadamard's inequality then gives the pointwise four-slot estimate
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  \rho^6\det\mathcal R(\rho,U)\det\mathcal L(\rho,U)
  \right|
  \le
  \rho^6 C_{\rm src}(1+c_-Q\rho)^{-12},
  \qquad
  C_{\rm src}:=\prod_A C_{R,A}\prod_B C_{L,B}.
  \label{eq:instanton-wave-packet-four-slot-bound}
\end{equation}
For the one-loop \(SU(3)\), \(N_f=2\) hard density, this gives the explicit
tail bound
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  Q^{b_0}
  \int_{R/Q}^{\infty}
  \rho^{b_0+1}
  C_{\rm src}(1+c_-Q\rho)^{-12}\,\dd\rho
  &\le
  Q^{-2}C_{\rm src}c_-^{-12}
  \frac{R^{\,b_0-10}}{10-b_0}  \\
  &=
  3Q^{-2}C_{\rm src}c_-^{-12}R^{-1/3},
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-wave-packet-hard-tail-bound}
\end{equation}
where \(b_0=29/3\) and the inequality is written for \(R\) in the region
where \(c_-R\ge1\).  This is a source-level version of the hard-tail estimate
in ControlledApproximation~\ref{ca:hard-size-dominance-vs-convergence}.

The same formula also records two failure modes.  First, the source must
remain rank-two in each chirality after projection to the instanton
zero-mode subspace: if the two right-handed rows of \(\mathcal R\), or the
two left-handed columns of \(\mathcal L\), become proportional, then
\(\det\mathcal R\det\mathcal L=0\) and the selected four-slot channel has no
leading zero-mode coefficient.  Second, a wave packet with support reaching
soft momentum has \(c_-=0\), so
\eqref{eq:instanton-wave-packet-hard-tail-bound} is unavailable.  The
calculation must then use the actual soft source profile, a fused bilinear
source, physical screening, or a Wilsonian long-size remainder.  Hardness is
therefore a property of the source projection and endpoint estimate, not of
the BPST moduli coordinates alone.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{proposition}[Orientation projection in the instanton four-slot kernel]
\label{prop:instanton-color-orientation-haar-projection}
The global \(SU(2)\) orientation in the embedded BPST core enters the
amplitude as a projection of colored zero-mode tensors onto invariant color
tensors.  Normalize Haar measure by \(\int_{SU(2)}\dd U=1\), and let
\(U_i{}^\alpha\) denote the fundamental matrix element carrying a core
two-dimensional index \(\alpha\) to a color index \(i\).  Then
\begin{equation}
  \int_{SU(2)} U_i{}^\alpha\,\dd U=0,\qquad
  \int_{SU(2)}
    U_i{}^\alpha \overline{U_j{}^\beta}\,\dd U
  =
  \frac12\delta_{ij}\delta^{\alpha\beta},
  \label{eq:instanton-orientation-one-slot-projection}
\end{equation}
and, because \(\wedge^2\mathbb C^2\) is the trivial representation of
\(SU(2)\),
\begin{equation}
  \int_{SU(2)}
    U_i{}^\alpha U_j{}^\beta\,\dd U
  =
  \frac12\varepsilon_{ij}\varepsilon^{\alpha\beta}.
  \label{eq:instanton-orientation-two-slot-projection}
\end{equation}
Consequently two differentiated external zero-mode slots with core source
vectors \(v_A,v_B\in\mathbb C^2\) have orientation average
\begin{equation}
  \int_{SU(2)}
    (Uv_A)_i(Uv_B)_j\,\dd U
  =
  \frac12\varepsilon_{ij}\,
  \varepsilon_{\alpha\beta}v_A^\alpha v_B^\beta
  =
  \frac12\varepsilon_{ij}\det(v_A,v_B).
  \label{eq:instanton-orientation-two-slot-determinant}
\end{equation}
For an \(N_f=2\) differentiated four-slot source, the four slots share the same
orientation variable.  One must therefore use the single four-point Haar
projector, not the product of two two-point averages.  When all four selected
slots have been written as fundamental \(SU(2)\) core indices, set
\[
  A_{i_1i_2j_1j_2}
  =
  \varepsilon_{i_1i_2}\varepsilon_{j_1j_2},
  \qquad
  B_{i_1i_2j_1j_2}
  =
  \varepsilon_{i_1j_1}\varepsilon_{i_2j_2},
\]
and use the same symbols with upper core indices.  Then
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  &\int_{SU(2)}
    U_{i_1}{}^{\alpha_1}U_{i_2}{}^{\alpha_2}
    U_{j_1}{}^{\beta_1}U_{j_2}{}^{\beta_2}\,\dd U       \\
  &\quad =
  \frac13 A_{i_1i_2j_1j_2}A^{\alpha_1\alpha_2\beta_1\beta_2}
  -\frac16 A_{i_1i_2j_1j_2}B^{\alpha_1\alpha_2\beta_1\beta_2} \\
  &\qquad
  -\frac16 B_{i_1i_2j_1j_2}A^{\alpha_1\alpha_2\beta_1\beta_2}
  +\frac13 B_{i_1i_2j_1j_2}B^{\alpha_1\alpha_2\beta_1\beta_2}.
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-four-slot-orientation-projector}
\end{equation}
If the left slots are kept as conjugate or dual slots instead, they must first
be converted to the chosen fundamental convention by the \(SU(2)\) pseudoreal
\(\varepsilon\)-tensor, or else the corresponding mixed \(U\overline U\)
Weingarten projector must be used.  Contracting
\eqref{eq:instanton-four-slot-orientation-projector} with core source vectors
\(v_1^R,v_2^R,v_1^L,v_2^L\) gives
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  &A_{i_1i_2j_1j_2}
  \left[
    \frac13\Delta_{12|34}
    -\frac16\Delta_{13|24}
  \right]
  +
  B_{i_1i_2j_1j_2}
  \left[
    -\frac16\Delta_{12|34}
    +\frac13\Delta_{13|24}
  \right],
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-four-slot-source-projector}
\end{equation}
where
\[
  \Delta_{12|34}
  =
  \varepsilon_{\alpha_1\alpha_2}v_1^{R,\alpha_1}v_2^{R,\alpha_2}\,
  \varepsilon_{\beta_1\beta_2}v_1^{L,\beta_1}v_2^{L,\beta_2},
  \qquad
  \Delta_{13|24}
  =
  \varepsilon_{\alpha_1\beta_1}v_1^{R,\alpha_1}v_1^{L,\beta_1}\,
  \varepsilon_{\alpha_2\beta_2}v_2^{R,\alpha_2}v_2^{L,\beta_2}.
\]
Thus the color-orientation collective coordinate is a genuine part of the
amplitude rather than a passive coordinate volume: it enforces the full
invariant four-slot projector.  A product of right and left flavor
determinants appears only after the Berezin source coefficient and the final
color-singlet source contraction impose that additional structure.  For an
\(SU(N_c)\) instanton
embedded through an \(SU(2)\) subgroup, the full orientation-orbit integral
is the corresponding \(SU(N_c)\)-invariant projection with a convention
dependent normalization; the displayed \(SU(2)\) core identity is the local
finite projection used by the zero-mode tensor.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
There is no nonzero invariant vector in the fundamental representation, so
the one-slot average vanishes.  The mixed two-point average is an intertwiner
\(\mathbb C^2\otimes(\mathbb C^2)^*\to
\mathbb C^2\otimes(\mathbb C^2)^*\), hence Schur orthogonality makes it a
multiple of \(\delta_{ij}\delta^{\alpha\beta}\).  Contracting \(i=j\) and
\(\alpha=\beta\) gives \(2\), so the multiple is \(1/2\).

Similarly, the average of \(U_i{}^\alpha U_j{}^\beta\) is an invariant tensor
in \(\wedge^2\mathbb C^2\otimes\wedge^2(\mathbb C^2)^*\), and must be
\(c\,\varepsilon_{ij}\varepsilon^{\alpha\beta}\).  Contracting with
\(\varepsilon^{ij}\varepsilon_{\alpha\beta}\) gives
\[
  4c
  =
  \int
  \varepsilon^{ij}\varepsilon_{\alpha\beta}
  U_i{}^\alpha U_j{}^\beta\,\dd U
  =
  2\int\det U\,\dd U
  =
  2,
\]
so \(c=1/2\).  Multiplying the averaged matrix elements by the two source
vectors gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-orientation-two-slot-determinant}.

For four slots, the invariant subspace of
\((\mathbb C^2)^{\otimes4}\) is two-dimensional.  Use the two spanning
invariant tensors \(A\) and \(B\) above.  Their Gram matrix is
\[
  \begin{pmatrix}
  \langle A,A\rangle & \langle A,B\rangle\\
  \langle B,A\rangle & \langle B,B\rangle
  \end{pmatrix}
  =
  \begin{pmatrix}4&2\\2&4\end{pmatrix},
  \qquad
  G^{-1}
  =
  \begin{pmatrix}\frac13&-\frac16\\[2pt]-\frac16&\frac13\end{pmatrix}.
\]
The Haar average is the orthogonal projection onto this invariant subspace,
with one copy of \(G^{-1}\) connecting the color invariant basis to the core
invariant basis.  This gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-four-slot-orientation-projector}.  Contracting that
projector with the four core source vectors gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-four-slot-source-projector}.  The calculation uses one
shared Haar variable throughout; replacing it by a product of two two-slot
averages would project two independent orientations and gives the wrong
four-slot normalization.
\end{proof}

The qualification in
Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-external-leg-amputation-kernel} is essential.
Colored quark legs in confining QCD do not define ordinary physical
asymptotic states.  The displayed object is an auxiliary source-amputated, or
partonic hard-kernel, coordinate useful for matching the finite-regulator
Green function to the local effective operator.  Gauge-invariant amplitudes
must contract the same instanton kernel with color-singlet external
operators, hadronic matrix elements, or a separately specified infrared
deformation.  This is the amplitude-level content of the original
one-instanton computation of 't Hooft
\cite{tHooft1976Pseudoparticle}: collective coordinates, nonzero-mode
fluctuation determinants, fermion zero-mode saturation, and external-leg
normalization are one calculation.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Color-singlet matching of the instanton
kernel]
\label{ca:instanton-color-singlet-hadronic-matching}
Stay in the finite-regulator \(Q=1\) setup of
Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-external-leg-amputation-kernel}, but replace
the auxiliary colored external quark representatives by renormalized
gauge-invariant source families.  Local examples are chiral color-singlet
bilinears \(\bar q_{R f}\Gamma q_{L f'}\); nonlocal examples must include the
Wilson line which makes the two quark fields a color singlet.  In a selected
\(N_f=2\) chirality-violating channel, suppose that the zero-mode projection
of the chosen source family has the short-distance form
\begin{equation}
  B^{\mathcal J}_{AB}(z)
  =
  \sum_{f,f'=1}^{2}
  \Phi^{R}_{A f}(z;\mu)\,
  B^{\rm amp}_{ff'}(z)\,
  \Phi^{L}_{f' B}(z;\mu)
  +
  B^{\rm rem}_{AB}(z),
  \label{eq:instanton-color-singlet-source-projection}
\end{equation}
where \(A,B\) label two independent color-singlet source coordinates,
\(\Phi^R,\Phi^L\) are the source-to-zero-mode overlap matrices in the chosen
renormalization scheme, and \(B^{\rm rem}\) collects higher-dimension source
components, soft channels not represented by the hard zero-mode kernel, and
terms outside the selected chirality structure.  The corresponding
gauge-invariant source correlator receives the one-instanton contribution
\begin{equation}
  G^{(4)}_{\mathcal J,\Lambda,Q=1}
  =
  \int_{\mathcal U_{Q=1}}
  \exp[-S_\Lambda(A_z)+\ii\theta]\,
  \mathcal W_{\Lambda,{\rm pt}}^{\rm nz}(z;\mu)\,
  \det B^{\mathcal J}(z)\,
  \dd\nu_{\Lambda,\mathcal M}(z),
  \label{eq:instanton-color-singlet-source-correlator}
\end{equation}
up to the same remainder specification.  If the overlap matrices are square
and vary only on scales which are soft compared with the hard instanton
support, then pointwise in \(z\)
\begin{equation}
  \det B^{\mathcal J}(z)
  =
  \det\Phi^R(z;\mu)\,
  \det B^{\rm amp}(z)\,
  \det\Phi^L(z;\mu)
  +
  \hbox{terms containing }B^{\rm rem}.
  \label{eq:instanton-color-singlet-determinant-projection}
\end{equation}
Thus the zero-mode form factors appropriate to the selected source family, the
orientation tensor, the nonzero-mode determinant, and the size integral remain
the short-distance instanton kernel; the color-singlet source overlaps are an
additional matching layer, not a replacement for the fluctuation calculation.

For stable hadron external states, the physical amplitude is obtained only
after applying the usual color-singlet spectral or LSZ extraction to the
gauge-invariant correlator.  For example, if interpolating sources
\(\mathcal I_H,\mathcal I_{H'}\) have nonzero isolated overlaps
\(Z_H,Z_{H'}\) with stable finite-volume states in the sense of
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-stable-current-three-point-extraction}, then a
termwise semiclassical extraction requires the same pole-residue operation:
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A^{(Q=1)}_{H'\leftarrow H}
  =
  \bigl(\overline Z_{H'}Z_H\bigr)^{-1}
  \operatorname*{Res}_{H',H}
  G_{\mathcal I_{H'}^\dagger\,\mathcal X\,\mathcal I_H,\Lambda,Q=1},
  \label{eq:instanton-hadronic-residue-extraction}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal X\) is the chosen gauge-invariant current or source product
and the residue notation means the finite-volume large-time projection, or
the corresponding infinite-volume pole extraction when it exists.  The BPST
calculation does not determine \(Z_H,Z_{H'}\), the hadronic matrix element of
the induced 't Hooft operator, or the long-distance part of
\(\Phi^{R,L}\).  Those are nonperturbative QCD data.  In a hard OPE or
factorization regime, the small-\(\rho\) instanton calculation can supply a
Wilson coefficient multiplying a gauge-invariant operator such as
\(\det[\bar q_R q_L]_\mu\); outside such a regime
\eqref{eq:instanton-color-singlet-source-correlator} is a source correlator,
not a prediction for a hadronic amplitude by itself.
\end{controlledapproximation}

The finite-regulator bookkeeping behind
\eqref{eq:instanton-color-singlet-source-projection} is entirely
finite-dimensional.
At finite regulator the fermion fields have finitely many odd coefficients,
and every regulated source has a finite expansion in those coefficients.
Restricting the source to the instanton zero-mode subspace produces a
finite-dimensional polynomial in the zero-mode variables.  The hypothesis
\eqref{eq:instanton-color-singlet-source-projection} says that, in the
chosen hard channel, the part of this polynomial which is bilinear in the
right and left zero-mode variables factors through the same amputated
zero-mode kernel \(B^{\rm amp}\), with source-dependent overlap maps on the
two sides.  Substituting this zero-mode source matrix into the Berezin
coefficient in
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-thooft-determinant-zero-mode-amplitude} gives
\(\det B^{\mathcal J}(z)\), and multiplying by the determinant density and
collective-coordinate measure gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-color-singlet-source-correlator}.

The determinant relation
\eqref{eq:instanton-color-singlet-determinant-projection} is the finite
identity
\[
  \det(\Phi^R B^{\rm amp}\Phi^L)
  =
  \det\Phi^R\,\det B^{\rm amp}\,\det\Phi^L,
\]
applied pointwise in the collective coordinate.  If the overlaps vary with
\(z\), the same identity still holds pointwise but the overlap factors must
remain inside the collective-coordinate integral.  Finally, because
\(G_{\mathcal I_{H'}^\dagger\,\mathcal X\,\mathcal I_H,\Lambda,Q=1}\) is a
correlator of gauge-invariant sources, the hadronic extraction is the
standard spectral-residue operation for color-singlet correlators.  Applying
that operation termwise in a controlled semiclassical expansion gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-hadronic-residue-extraction}; it never produces an
ordinary colored-quark \(S\)-matrix element.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Euclidean instanton kernel to physical
amplitude]
\label{ca:instanton-euclidean-to-physical-amplitude-budget}
Let \(G^{E,Q=1}_{\mathcal J,\Lambda}\) be the finite-regulator
gauge-invariant Euclidean source correlator obtained from the one-instanton
chart after zero modes, nonzero-mode determinants, source projections, and
collective coordinates have all been paired.  Let
\[
  \mathcal A_{\rm inst}^{\rm lead}
  =
  \operatorname*{Proj}_{\rm phys}
  \operatorname*{Cont}_{\mathcal S}
  G^{E,Q=1}_{\mathcal J,{\rm lead}}
\]
denote the result of first replacing the finite-regulator density by the
declared leading instanton kernel, then analytically continuing on a specified
sheet \(\mathcal S\), and finally applying the chosen physical projection:
a stable-particle pole residue, an inclusive spectral weight, or a hard OPE
coefficient.  The corresponding physical one-instanton contribution
\(\mathcal A_{\rm phys}^{Q=1}\) differs from this coordinate by
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_{\rm phys}^{Q=1}
  -
  \mathcal A_{\rm inst}^{\rm lead}
  =
  R_{\rm reg}
  +
  R_{\rm cont}
  +
  R_{\rm spec}
  +
  R_{\rm IR}
  +
  R_{\rm cut}
  +
  R_{\rm match}
  +
  R_{\rho}.
  \label{eq:instanton-euclidean-to-physical-residual-budget}
\end{equation}
Here \(R_{\rm reg}\) records finite-volume, cutoff, and order-of-limits errors
between the regulated Euclidean sector and its continuum source correlator;
\(R_{\rm cont}\) records analytic-continuation and sheet choices, including
thresholds and singularities crossed by the chosen continuation;
\(R_{\rm spec}\) records the pole, spectral, or OPE projection error;
\(R_{\rm IR}\) records confinement, massless radiation, inclusive-sum, or
external Wilson-line data not contained in a colored partonic kernel;
\(R_{\rm cut}\) records unitarity-cut and conjugate-sector effects, including
instanton--anti-instanton sectors needed before an \(S\)-matrix statement can
obey an optical theorem; \(R_{\rm match}\) records the matching from the
chosen source family to the local operator or hadronic observable; and
\(R_{\rho}\) is the remaining instanton-size endpoint and determinant-tail
contribution after the selected hard, screened, or Wilsonian window has been
declared.

If on the selected kinematic window each residual satisfies
\[
  |R_\kappa|\le \varepsilon_\kappa,
  \qquad
  \kappa\in
  \{{\rm reg},{\rm cont},{\rm spec},{\rm IR},{\rm cut},{\rm match},\rho\},
\]
then
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  \mathcal A_{\rm phys}^{Q=1}
  -
  \mathcal A_{\rm inst}^{\rm lead}
  \right|
  \le
  \sum_\kappa\varepsilon_\kappa .
  \label{eq:instanton-physical-amplitude-residual-bound}
\end{equation}
The point is not to add another approximation.  It is to identify where the
physics lives after the moduli-space and determinant calculation has been
done.  In a weakly coupled Higgsed theory, a thermal screened regime, or a
hard Euclidean OPE window, the physical projection and endpoint controls can
sometimes be declared explicitly.  In confining zero-temperature QCD, a
colored four-slot kernel is only a short-distance source coordinate until the
gauge-invariant spectral or OPE projection and the long-size remainder have
been supplied.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Instanton cut pairing for inclusive rates]
\label{ca:instanton-unitarity-cut-pairing}
Stay in the source channel of
ControlledApproximation~\ref{ca:instanton-euclidean-to-physical-amplitude-budget}.
Before making a rate statement, separate the amplitude into the sectors which
can interfere on the chosen cut:
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_{\rm phys}[\mathcal J]
  =
  A_0[\mathcal J]
  +
  \ee^{-S_I+\ii\theta}a_I[\mathcal J]
  +
  \ee^{-S_I-\ii\theta}a_{\bar I}[\mathcal J]
  +
  \cdots .
  \label{eq:instanton-amplitude-sector-expansion}
\end{equation}
For a finite-regulator inclusive cut pairing \(\langle\,,\,\rangle_{\rm cut}\),
the first terms in the corresponding rate are therefore
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \Gamma[\mathcal J]
  &=
  \langle A_0,A_0\rangle_{\rm cut}
  +
  2\operatorname{Re}\!
  \left[
    \ee^{-S_I+\ii\theta}
    \langle A_0,a_I\rangle_{\rm cut}
  \right] \\
  &\quad
  +
  2\operatorname{Re}\!
  \left[
    \ee^{-S_I-\ii\theta}
    \langle A_0,a_{\bar I}\rangle_{\rm cut}
  \right]
  +
  \ee^{-2S_I}
  \langle a_I,a_I\rangle_{\rm cut}
  +
  \cdots .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-inclusive-rate-sector-expansion}
\end{equation}
Thus an order-\(\ee^{-S_I}\) interference term is present unless the selected
source and final-state projection kill it.  In the chirality-violating
't Hooft channel this can happen because the perturbative \(Q=0\) sector has no
zero modes to supply the selected axial-charge violation, but this is a
selection statement supplied by the source projection and final-state cut.
The hypothesis needed below is
\begin{equation}
  \langle B,a_I\rangle_{\rm cut}
  =
  \langle B,a_{\bar I}\rangle_{\rm cut}
  =
  0
  \quad
  \text{for every lower-action sector }B\text{ retained by the projection}.
  \label{eq:instanton-cut-selection-hypothesis}
\end{equation}

After the determinant, zero-mode, orientation, and source-matching factors
have been assembled, write a finite one-instanton amplitude coordinate as
\begin{equation}
  A_I[\mathcal J]
  =
  \ee^{\ii\theta}
  \int_{\mathcal U_I}
  K_I(z;\mathcal J)\,\dd\nu_I(z),
  \label{eq:instanton-one-amplitude-kernel-coordinate}
\end{equation}
where \(z\) denotes the collective coordinates and finite fluctuation/source
data retained in the chosen regulator.  The conjugate channel has an
anti-instanton density
\[
  A_{\bar I}[\mathcal J^\dagger]
  =
  \ee^{-\ii\theta}
  \int_{\mathcal U_{\bar I}}
  K_{\bar I}(\bar z;\mathcal J^\dagger)\,\dd\nu_{\bar I}(\bar z).
\]
The factorized diagonal instanton contribution to the selected inclusive
spectral weight or cut rate has the paired form
\begin{equation}
  \Gamma^{(0),{\rm diag}}_{I\bar I}[\mathcal J]
  =
  \int_{\mathcal U_I\times\mathcal U_{\bar I}}
  K_I(z;\mathcal J)\,
  K_{\bar I}(\bar z;\mathcal J^\dagger)\,
  \mathcal C_{\rm cut}^{(0)}(z,\bar z)\,
  \dd\nu_I(z)\,\dd\nu_{\bar I}(\bar z).
  \label{eq:instanton-cut-paired-rate-leading}
\end{equation}
Here \(\mathcal C_{\rm cut}^{(0)}\) contains the chosen leading final-state
sum, on-shell or spectral projector, relative \(I\bar I\) separation and
orientation weight, and leading relative fluctuation determinant.  At the
factorized diagonal level the topological phases cancel in the cut channel,
\[
  \ee^{\ii\theta}\ee^{-\ii\theta}=1,
  \qquad
  \ee^{\ii\theta}\ee^{\ii\theta}=\ee^{2\ii\theta}.
\]
Thus a same-charge pair belongs to a charge-two amplitude sector rather than
to the amplitude-times-conjugate contribution to a neutral inclusive rate.  The
displayed kernel is the diagonal \(I\bar I\) contribution to the selected
inclusive rate.  It is the leading nonperturbative contribution to the full
selected rate, with semiclassical exponential \(e^{-2S_I}\) and no explicit
\(\theta\) phase, only when
\eqref{eq:instanton-cut-selection-hypothesis} has removed the lower-order
interference terms in \eqref{eq:instanton-inclusive-rate-sector-expansion}.
Without that hypothesis, the order-\(\ee^{-S_I}\) interference is part of the
physical rate and can carry explicit \(\theta\)-dependence.

The full cut kernel can be organized as
\[
  \mathcal C_{\rm cut}
  =
  \mathcal C_{\rm cut}^{(0)}(1+\delta_{\rm cut}),
  \qquad
  |\delta_{\rm cut}(z,\bar z)|\le \varepsilon_{\rm cut},
\]
where \(\delta_{\rm cut}\) absorbs the difference between the declared leading
cut package and the actual final-state sum, relative \(I\bar I\) interaction,
valley or quasi-zero-mode treatment, and nonzero-mode determinant ratio.  If
\[
  M^{(0)}_{I\bar I}
  =
  \int
  |K_I(z;\mathcal J)|\,|K_{\bar I}(\bar z;\mathcal J^\dagger)|\,
  |\mathcal C_{\rm cut}^{(0)}(z,\bar z)|\,
  \dd\nu_I(z)\,\dd\nu_{\bar I}(\bar z)
  <\infty ,
\]
then the exact cut contribution satisfies
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  \Gamma_{I\bar I}[\mathcal J]
  -
  \Gamma^{(0),{\rm diag}}_{I\bar I}[\mathcal J]
  \right|
  \le
  \varepsilon_{\rm cut} M^{(0)}_{I\bar I}.
  \label{eq:instanton-cut-pairing-error-bound}
\end{equation}
This is the concrete finite-regulator content of the \(R_{\rm cut}\) entry in
\eqref{eq:instanton-euclidean-to-physical-residual-budget}.  The local
't Hooft vertex supplies the chirality-violating amplitude kernel.  Inclusive
cross sections, decay rates, and spectral weights require the conjugate
anti-instanton density, final-state cut, and relative \(I\bar I\)
fluctuation determinants and interactions in addition to that kernel.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[One-instanton sector isolation bound]
\label{ca:one-instanton-sector-isolation-bound}
The previous cut-pairing discussion separates amplitude sectors for rates.
For a selected one-instanton amplitude there is a prior, more elementary
question: has the \(Q=1\) source coordinate actually been isolated from the
neighboring sectors in the observable under study?  Let \(\Pi_{\mathcal O}\)
denote the finite source, charge, chirality, or spectral projection used to
extract the coefficient.  On the same regulator and kinematic window write
the projected amplitude-sector expansion as
\begin{equation}
  \Pi_{\mathcal O}\mathcal A
  =
  \Pi_{\mathcal O}A_0
  +
  \Pi_{\mathcal O}A_I
  +
  \Pi_{\mathcal O}A_{\bar I}
  +
  \Pi_{\mathcal O}A_{2I}
  +
  \Pi_{\mathcal O}A_{I\bar I}^{\rm amp}
  +
  R_{\ge2}^{\rm other}.
  \label{eq:instanton-one-sector-isolation-expansion}
\end{equation}
Here \(A_{I\bar I}^{\rm amp}\) is an amplitude-sector contribution before
forming an inclusive cut rate; it is not the diagonal rate term in
\eqref{eq:instanton-cut-paired-rate-leading}.  Let \(J_I\) be the retained
leading \(Q=1\) coefficient, obtained after the determinant, zero-mode,
orientation, source, and size-window choices have all been made, and let
\(M_I\) be the absolute mass of that retained \(Q=1\) window.  Suppose
\begin{equation}
  \left|\Pi_{\mathcal O}A_I-J_I\right|
  \le
  \epsilon_I M_I,
  \qquad
  \left|\Pi_{\mathcal O}A_\alpha\right|
  \le
  \lambda_\alpha M_\alpha
  \quad
  (\alpha=0,\bar I,2I,I\bar I),
  \qquad
  |R_{\ge2}^{\rm other}|\le E_{\ge2}.
  \label{eq:instanton-one-sector-isolation-hypotheses}
\end{equation}
Then the selected observable differs from the retained one-instanton
coefficient by
\begin{equation}
  \left|\Pi_{\mathcal O}\mathcal A-J_I\right|
  \le
  \epsilon_I M_I
  +
  \lambda_0M_0
  +
  \lambda_{\bar I}M_{\bar I}
  +
  \lambda_{2I}M_{2I}
  +
  \lambda_{I\bar I}M_{I\bar I}
  +
  E_{\ge2}.
  \label{eq:instanton-one-sector-isolation-bound}
\end{equation}
If in addition the retained one-instanton coefficient has a noncancellation
margin
\[
  |J_I|\ge\kappa_I M_I,\qquad \kappa_I>0,
\]
then \eqref{eq:instanton-one-sector-isolation-bound} gives a relative
isolation bound after division by \(|J_I|\).  The projection factors
\(\lambda_\alpha\) are part of the physics, not bookkeeping decoration.  In a
chirality-violating source the perturbative leakage \(\lambda_0M_0\) can
vanish by an exact zero-mode selection rule.  In an ordinary gauge-invariant
spectral channel it usually does not, and a small instanton saddle can be
buried under a lower-action sector.  Likewise, signed cancellation between
\(\bar I\), \(2I\), and \(I\bar I\) contributions is not an isolation
bound; the estimate uses absolute sector majorants in the same source
normalization.  A quoted ``one-instanton amplitude'' is therefore a leading
sector coordinate until the sector projection and leakage bounds above have
also been supplied.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{proposition}[One-instanton amplitude assembly and error budget]
\label{prop:instanton-amplitude-assembly-error-budget}
Fix a finite-regulator \(Q=1\) chart and a gauge-invariant source channel.
Let
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_{\Lambda,Q=1}^{\mathcal J}
  =
  \int_{\mathcal U_{Q=1}}
  \mathcal K_{\rm ex}(z)\,\dd z
  \label{eq:instanton-exact-source-amplitude-density}
\end{equation}
denote the exact one-instanton contribution to the selected source
correlator after gauge fixing but before replacing any finite factor by its
semiclassical leading term.  Choose a controlled subdomain
\(\mathcal U_{\rm hard}\subset\mathcal U_{Q=1}\) and a leading density
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \mathcal K_{\rm lead}(z)
  &=
  \ee^{\ii\theta}
  \mathcal C_{\rm pg}^{\mathcal S}(z)\,
  \mathcal R_{\rm f}^{\mathcal S}(z;\mu)
  \left(\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(\mu)}\right)^{2N_c}
  \exp\!\left[-\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(\mu)}\right]
  (\mu\rho)^{b_0}\rho^{-5}\,
  \mathcal Z_{\rm lead}^{0}(z).
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-leading-amplitude-density}
\end{equation}
Here \(\mathcal C_{\rm pg}^{\mathcal S}(z)\) is the pure-gauge
collective-coordinate and determinant density in the chosen convention.  In
the Pauli-Villars convention after the embedded orientation orbit has been
integrated it contains \(C_{N_c}^{\rm PV}\); in an unintegrated orientation
chart it contains the corresponding orientation density instead of an
already-integrated orbit volume.  The factor
\(\mathcal R_{\rm f}^{\mathcal S}\) is the light-fermion nonzero-mode
determinant factor in the same source scheme, and
\(\mathcal Z_{\rm lead}^{0}\) is the leading zero-mode source coefficient.
Depending on the source type,
\(\mathcal Z_{\rm lead}^{0}\) is one of
\(\det(M^0+J^0)\), \(\det R^{\rm amp}\det L^{\rm amp}\), or the
color-singlet determinant \(\det B^{\mathcal J}\) after the source matching
of \eqref{eq:instanton-color-singlet-source-projection}.

Suppose that on \(\mathcal U_{\rm hard}\) the exact density decomposes as
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal K_{\rm ex}
  =
  \mathcal K_{\rm lead}
  \bigl(1+\varepsilon_{\rm det}
          +\varepsilon_{\rm zm}
          +\varepsilon_{\rm src}\bigr)
  +\Delta_{\rm Schur},
  \label{eq:instanton-amplitude-error-density}
\end{equation}
where \(\varepsilon_{\rm det}\) records the higher-loop and finite determinant
remainder after the chosen determinant convention, \(\varepsilon_{\rm zm}\)
records the zero-mode projection or local-source truncation error,
\(\varepsilon_{\rm src}\) records the color-singlet source-matching or
hadronic/OPE matching remainder, and \(\Delta_{\rm Schur}\) records the
finite nonzero-mode Schur correction from
\eqref{eq:instanton-fermion-schur-factorization}.  Then
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_{\Lambda,Q=1}^{\mathcal J}
  =
  \mathcal A_{\rm lead}^{\mathcal J}
  +R_{\rm det}+R_{\rm zm}+R_{\rm src}+R_{\rm Schur}+R_{\rm end},
  \label{eq:instanton-amplitude-error-decomposition}
\end{equation}
with
\[
  \mathcal A_{\rm lead}^{\mathcal J}
  =
  \int_{\mathcal U_{\rm hard}}\mathcal K_{\rm lead}(z)\,\dd z,
  \qquad
  R_{\rm end}
  =
  \int_{\mathcal U_{Q=1}\setminus\mathcal U_{\rm hard}}
  \mathcal K_{\rm ex}(z)\,\dd z .
\]
Moreover, whenever the right-hand side is absolutely integrable,
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \bigl|
  \mathcal A_{\Lambda,Q=1}^{\mathcal J}
  -\mathcal A_{\rm lead}^{\mathcal J}
  \bigr|
  &\le
  \int_{\mathcal U_{\rm hard}}
  |\mathcal K_{\rm lead}|
  \bigl(
    |\varepsilon_{\rm det}|
    +|\varepsilon_{\rm zm}|
    +|\varepsilon_{\rm src}|
  \bigr)\,\dd z  \\
  &\quad
  +\int_{\mathcal U_{\rm hard}}|\Delta_{\rm Schur}|\,\dd z
  +
  \int_{\mathcal U_{Q=1}\setminus\mathcal U_{\rm hard}}
  |\mathcal K_{\rm ex}|\,\dd z .
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-amplitude-error-bound}
\end{equation}
Thus replacing the finite-regulator instanton contribution by the local
't Hooft operator, or by a hard source-amputated kernel, is justified only
after the determinant remainder, zero-mode/source projection, matching
remainder, Schur correction, and endpoint integral have all been controlled
in the same scheme.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Split the exact integral into the chosen hard/source domain and its complement:
\[
  \int_{\mathcal U_{Q=1}}\mathcal K_{\rm ex}
  =
  \int_{\mathcal U_{\rm hard}}\mathcal K_{\rm ex}
  +
  \int_{\mathcal U_{Q=1}\setminus\mathcal U_{\rm hard}}\mathcal K_{\rm ex}.
\]
Substituting
\eqref{eq:instanton-amplitude-error-density} on
\(\mathcal U_{\rm hard}\) gives the five remainders in
\eqref{eq:instanton-amplitude-error-decomposition}.  The bound
\eqref{eq:instanton-amplitude-error-bound} is the triangle inequality.  The
content is the identification of the separate physical origins of the five
terms: collective-coordinate geometry supplies only \(\mathcal J_{\rm coll}\)
or, equivalently, the collective part of
\(\mathcal C_{\rm pg}^{\mathcal S}\) and the integration domain; the
fluctuation determinant, light-fermion nonzero-mode factor, zero-mode source
coefficient, source matching, and endpoint behavior are independent
load-bearing inputs to the amplitude.
\end{proof}

Consequently an instanton moduli-space measure by itself is never the
computed QFT amplitude.  It becomes a physical contribution only after it is
multiplied by the nonzero-mode fluctuation determinant, the correctly typed
zero-mode source coefficient, the source or hadron matching data, and an
endpoint estimate for the selected kinematic regime.  The original
one-instanton calculation is deep precisely because it performs this whole
assembly, rather than because it merely parametrizes the BPST collective
coordinates.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Instanton observable assembly ladder]
\label{ca:instanton-observable-assembly-ladder}
The preceding bounds address different layers of the same physical
calculation.  To prevent the reader from mistaking them for independent
annexes, fix a selected observable channel \(\mathcal O\), a source family
\(\mathfrak h\), and a retained one-instanton window.  Let
\[
  J_I[\mathfrak h]
\]
be the leading finite-window coefficient after the collective-coordinate
density, pure-gauge determinant convention, light-fermion nonzero-mode
factor, source zero-mode determinant, orientation projection, and hard-size
window have all been included.  Let \(M_I[\mathfrak h]\) be its absolute
window mass.  The physical observable map is not the identity map on this
Euclidean source coefficient.  It contains analytic continuation, LSZ or OPE
projection, infrared or hadronic matching, possible inclusive cuts, and the
sector projection used to isolate the \(Q=1\) amplitude coordinate.  Write its
leading linear part as \(\mathfrak L_{\mathcal O}\).

The finite-regulator statement has the form
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \mathcal O_{\rm phys}^{(Q=1)}
  &=
  \mathfrak L_{\mathcal O}\!\left[J_I[\mathfrak h]\right]
  +R_{\rm spec}+R_{\rm fluc}+R_{\rm rank}+R_{\rm Schur}
  +R_{\rm end}                                      \\
  &\qquad{}
  +R_{\rm sector}+R_{\rm cont}+R_{\rm proj}
  +R_{\rm IR}+R_{\rm cut}+R_{\rm scheme}.
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:instanton-observable-assembly-ladder}
\end{equation}
The first line is internal to the Euclidean instanton source integral.  It
records determinant and counterterm remainders, source fluctuation cumulants,
zero-mode rank or source-overlap loss, finite Schur complement corrections,
and the omitted size or boundary tail.  The second line promotes that source
coordinate to the declared physical observable.  It records leakage from
neighboring amplitude sectors, continuation residuals, LSZ/OPE or hadronic
projection errors, infrared and volume residuals, cut errors when a rate is
formed, and finite scheme transport errors.

If these residuals are bounded in the same source normalization by
\[
  |R_\alpha|\le\delta_\alpha M_I[\mathfrak h],
  \qquad
  \alpha\in
  \{\mathrm{spec},\mathrm{fluc},\mathrm{rank},\mathrm{Schur},
    \mathrm{end},\mathrm{sector},\mathrm{cont},\mathrm{proj},
    \mathrm{IR},\mathrm{cut},\mathrm{scheme}\},
\]
then
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  \mathcal O_{\rm phys}^{(Q=1)}
  -
  \mathfrak L_{\mathcal O}[J_I]
  \right|
  \le
  M_I
  \sum_\alpha\delta_\alpha .
  \label{eq:instanton-observable-assembly-bound}
\end{equation}
A relative physical statement further requires a margin
\[
  |\mathfrak L_{\mathcal O}[J_I]|\ge\kappa_{\mathcal O} M_I,
  \qquad \kappa_{\mathcal O}>0.
\]
Only after this margin is present may one divide
\eqref{eq:instanton-observable-assembly-bound} by the quoted leading
observable.  Signed cancellation among the residuals, or between neighboring
amplitude sectors, does not replace the absolute budget.

This ladder is the structural distinction between an instanton-moduli
calculation and an instanton contribution to a QFT observable.  The moduli
space supplies the variables and zero-mode Jacobian inside \(J_I\).  The
fluctuation determinant, source stability, boundary estimates, sector
projection, and physical observable map decide whether \(J_I\) is a
controlled contribution to a scattering amplitude, an OPE coefficient, a
susceptibility, or an inclusive rate.  The operations are deliberately ordered:
one first assembles and bounds the finite source coefficient, then applies
the physical projection and its own residual budget.  Reversing this order
usually replaces a controlled amplitude calculation by a formal local vertex.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Source-dependent fluctuation bound]
\label{ca:instanton-source-fluctuation-cumulant-bound}
The nonzero-mode determinant in
\eqref{eq:instanton-leading-amplitude-density} is only the Gaussian
normalization of the fluctuation integral.  For an actual source or operator
insertion one must also control how the same nonzero modes enter the insertion.
After zero modes and residual gauge modes have been projected out, let
\(\eta\in\mathcal N_z\) be the finite-regulator normal fluctuation coordinate
at the instanton \(A_z\), let \(d\gamma_z(\eta)\) be the normalized Gaussian
measure defined by the nonzero-mode Hessian, let \(V_z(\eta;g)\) collect cubic
and higher action vertices together with finite counterterm remainders, and let
\(\mathcal Z_z(\eta;\mathcal J)\) be the source factor after the explicit
fermion zero-mode coefficient has been separated.  On a chart where
\(\mathcal Z_z(0;\mathcal J)\ne0\), the source-dependent fluctuation ratio is
\[
  \mathcal R_{\rm fluc}(z;\mathcal J)
  =
  \frac{
    \left\langle
      \mathcal Z_z(\eta;\mathcal J)
      \exp[-V_z(\eta;g)]
    \right\rangle_{\gamma_z}
  }{
    \mathcal Z_z(0;\mathcal J)
  } .
\]
Thus the determinant constant and the source fluctuation correction are
different coordinates: the first normalizes \(d\gamma_z\), while the second
tests the selected source under the same fluctuation measure.

Suppose that on the retained hard/source window
\[
  \mathcal R_{\rm fluc}(z;\mathcal J)
  =
  1+C_1(z;\mathcal J)+C_2(z;\mathcal J)+R_{\ge3}(z;\mathcal J)
\]
and that
\[
  |C_1|\le\epsilon_1,\qquad
  |C_2|\le\epsilon_2,\qquad
  |R_{\ge3}|\le\epsilon_{\ge3}.
\]
Then the fluctuation part of the determinant residual in
\eqref{eq:instanton-amplitude-error-density} is bounded by
\[
  \epsilon_{\rm fluc}
  =
  \epsilon_1+\epsilon_2+\epsilon_{\ge3}.
\]
For the hard finite-window bound this refines
\eqref{eq:hard-instanton-window-absolute-bound} to
\[
  \left|
  C_{\rm inst}^{(4),{\rm ex}}(Q)-\mathcal N(Q)J_R
  \right|
  \le
  |\mathcal N(Q)|M_R
  \bigl(
    \epsilon_{\rm spec}
    +\epsilon_{\rm fluc}
    +\epsilon_{\rm zm}
    +\epsilon_{\rm src}
    +\epsilon_{\rm Schur}
    +\tau_R
  \bigr),
\]
where \(\epsilon_{\rm spec}\) denotes the source-independent spectral
determinant and counterterm remainder.  If
\(\mathcal Z_z(0;\mathcal J)\) loses its rank or noncancellation margin, this
relative form is invalid; the fluctuation contribution must then be kept as an
absolute source residual of the kind represented by \(\Delta_{\rm Schur}\) or
\(R_{\rm src}\).

This is the semiclassical point hidden by many shorthand presentations of the
't Hooft vertex.  A vacuum determinant calibration can fix the Gaussian
normalization and still say too little about a four-fermion amplitude, because
the latter asks whether the source insertion is stable under fluctuations
around the instanton.  The controlled weak-coupling claim is therefore not
``BPST moduli space plus a determinant constant.''  It is a uniform statement,
on the chosen source and size window, about the determinant, zero-mode
overlaps, fluctuation cumulants, endpoint tails, and physical projection
residuals together.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Hard-momentum size window]
\label{ca:hard-momentum-instanton-size-window}
Consider the \(N_f=2\) source-amputated four-fermion kernel
\eqref{eq:instanton-amputated-four-fermion-kernel} in a kinematic region
where the hard arguments of the zero-mode form factors are
\[
  |k_\ell|=c_\ell Q,
  \qquad c_\ell>0,\qquad \ell=1,\ldots,m,
\]
with \(Q\) much larger than the infrared scale of the theory.  For
differentiated external fermion slots, \(m=4\) and the
\(\mathcal F_\ell\) below are the individual amputated zero-mode form factors
of Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-individual-zero-mode-form-factor}.  In the
singular-gauge normalization,
\(\mathcal F_\ell(c_\ell Q\rho)=F_{\rm zm}(c_\ell Q\rho/2)\), up to the
fixed spin-color tensor already included in \(\mathcal C_{\rm hard}\).
For a fused bilinear source, \(m=2\) and
\(\mathcal F_\ell(z)=zK_1(z)\).  Keep only the one-loop universal density, the
total four-zero-mode power \(\rho^6\), and the dimensionless hard form-factor
product \(\prod_{\ell=1}^m\mathcal F_\ell(c_\ell Q\rho)\).  Choosing
\(\mu=Q\), the corresponding size factor has the form
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal I_{\rm hard}(Q)
  =
  \exp\!\left[-\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(Q)}+\ii\theta\right]
  \left(\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(Q)}\right)^{2N_c}
  Q^{b_0}
  \int_0^\infty
  \rho^{\,b_0+1}
  \prod_{\ell=1}^{m}
  \mathcal F_\ell(c_\ell Q\rho)\,\dd\rho
  \times\mathcal C_{\rm hard},
  \label{eq:hard-momentum-instanton-size-factor}
\end{equation}
up to finite determinant remainders, orientation tensors, source
normalizations, and higher-loop matching factors.  With \(s=Q\rho\),
\begin{equation}
  Q^{b_0}
  \int_0^\infty
  \rho^{\,b_0+1}
  \prod_{\ell=1}^{m}
  \mathcal F_\ell(c_\ell Q\rho)\,\dd\rho
  =
  Q^{-2}
  \int_0^\infty
  s^{\,b_0+1}
  \prod_{\ell=1}^{m}
  \mathcal F_\ell(c_\ell s)\,\dd s .
  \label{eq:hard-momentum-instanton-size-scaling}
\end{equation}
This \(Q^{-2}\) is the engineering dimension of the source-amputated
four-fermion coefficient after the renormalization point has been set to
\(\mu=Q\).  If the one-loop running exponential is instead traded for the
RG-invariant scale
\[
  \Lambda_{\rm ht}^{b_0}
  =
  Q^{b_0}
  \exp\!\left[-\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(Q)}\right]
  \quad\hbox{at one-loop order},
\]
then the same hard factor is
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal I_{\rm hard}(Q)
  =
  \ee^{\ii\theta}
  \left(\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(Q)}\right)^{2N_c}
  \Lambda_{\rm ht}^{b_0}\,
  Q^{-b_0-2}\,
  \mathcal J_{b_0}(\mathbf c;\mathcal F)\,
  \mathcal C_{\rm hard},
  \label{eq:hard-momentum-instanton-rg-invariant-scaling}
\end{equation}
with
\[
  \mathcal J_{b_0}(\mathbf c;\mathcal F)
  =
  \int_0^\infty
  s^{\,b_0+1}
  \prod_{\ell=1}^{m}
  \mathcal F_\ell(c_\ell s)\,\dd s .
\]
Thus the semiclassical exponential and the size measure together become a
power-suppressed hard coefficient.  The remaining displayed
\((8\pi^2/g_{\rm ht}^2(Q))^{2N_c}\) is the familiar one-loop collective-mode
Jacobian prefactor; higher-loop matching changes the logarithmic factor and
scheme coordinate, not the endpoint mechanism described here.
The small-\(\rho\) endpoint is finite in asymptotically free QCD because the
integrand behaves as \(\rho^{b_0+1}\).  The large-\(\rho\) endpoint depends on
which source construction is being used.  For fused bilinear density entries,
\(zK_1(z)\) gives the exponential cutoff
\[
  \prod_{\ell=1}^{m}\mathcal F_\ell(c_\ell Q\rho)
  =
  O\!\left((Q\rho)^\gamma\exp[-d(\mathbf c)Q\rho]\right),
  \qquad d(\mathbf c)>0,
  \qquad Q\rho\to\infty .
\]
For differentiated singular-gauge fermion slots, however,
\eqref{eq:instanton-individual-zero-mode-form-factor-large} gives only the
power behavior
\[
  \prod_{\ell=1}^{m}F_{\rm zm}(c_\ell Q\rho/2)
  =
  O\!\left((Q\rho)^{-3m}\right)
  \qquad(c_\ell>0).
\]
The large-\(\rho\) part of the size integral is then controlled only if
\begin{equation}
  b_0+1-3m<-1 .
  \label{eq:hard-momentum-individual-slot-large-rho-test}
\end{equation}
For the \(N_f=2\) four-slot hard kernel, \(m=4\), so this condition is
\(b_0<10\); in \(SU(3)\) QCD with two Dirac fundamentals,
\(b_0=29/3\), and the margin is \(1/3\).  If a determinant monomial contains a
soft slot with \(c_\ell=0\), or if the power test fails, the hard source
profile has not by itself produced a controlled large-size instanton
amplitude.  This is a physical endpoint condition in the amplitude integral,
not a cutoff on the instanton moduli space.  The approximation is controlled
only when the dominant range also has \(1/\rho\) in the weak-coupling regime.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Hard-size dominance versus endpoint convergence]
\label{ca:hard-size-dominance-vs-convergence}
The convergence test in
\eqref{eq:hard-momentum-individual-slot-large-rho-test} is not yet a
dominance statement.  In the notation of
\eqref{eq:hard-momentum-instanton-size-factor}, set
\[
  \mathcal F_{\rm hard}(s)
  =
  \prod_{\ell=1}^{m}\mathcal F_\ell(c_\ell s),
  \qquad
  a=b_0+1 .
\]
After the change of variables \(s=Q\rho\), the absolute tail of the one-loop
hard size integral outside the band \(\rho\le R/Q\) is
\begin{equation}
  Q^{b_0}
  \int_{R/Q}^{\infty}
  \rho^{\,b_0+1}\,
  |\mathcal F_{\rm hard}(Q\rho)|\,\dd\rho
  =
  Q^{-2}
  \int_{R}^{\infty}
  s^{\,a}\,|\mathcal F_{\rm hard}(s)|\,\dd s .
  \label{eq:hard-size-tail-change-variable}
\end{equation}
Thus a statement that the amplitude is dominated by instantons of size
\(\rho\sim Q^{-1}\) requires a bound on the right-hand tail in addition to
the formal local vertex.

For example, suppose that for \(s\ge s_0\)
\[
  |\mathcal F_{\rm hard}(s)|\le C_\infty s^{-\sigma},
  \qquad \sigma>b_0+2 .
\]
Then for \(R\ge s_0\),
\begin{equation}
  Q^{b_0}
  \int_{R/Q}^{\infty}
  \rho^{\,b_0+1}\,
  |\mathcal F_{\rm hard}(Q\rho)|\,\dd\rho
  \le
  Q^{-2}\,
  \frac{C_\infty\,R^{\,b_0+2-\sigma}}
       {\sigma-b_0-2}.
  \label{eq:hard-size-power-tail-bound}
\end{equation}
If instead the fused bilinear-density source gives
\(|\mathcal F_{\rm hard}(s)|\le C_\infty s^\gamma e^{-ds}\), \(d>0\), then
the corresponding tail is bounded by
\[
  Q^{-2}C_\infty
  \int_R^\infty s^{\,b_0+1+\gamma}e^{-ds}\,\dd s ,
\]
and is exponentially small once \(R\) is large.  The two source
constructions therefore have different endpoint control.

For the differentiated singular-gauge four-slot \(SU(3)\), \(N_f=2\) hard
kernel, the individual zero-mode form factors have
\(\sigma=3m=12\), while \(b_0=29/3\).  Hence
\[
  b_0+2-\sigma=-\frac13 .
\]
The contribution from \(\rho>R/Q\) is only \(O(R^{-1/3})\), up to the
spin-color and \(c_\ell\)-dependent constants.  The size integral is
convergent, but the convergence margin is narrow: claiming that the
one-instanton hard kernel is numerically dominated by \(\rho\sim Q^{-1}\)
requires an additional estimate showing that this slowly decaying tail is
small in the chosen source and kinematic window.  This is a physical
endpoint-control hypothesis on the amplitude, not a property of the BPST
moduli coordinates alone.

The same statement is often clearer per logarithmic size shell.  Define the
absolute log-shell density after the hard change of variables by
\begin{equation}
  \mathfrak s_{\rm hard}(s)
  =
  s^{\,b_0+2}\,
  |\mathcal F_{\rm hard}(s)|,
  \qquad
  Q^{b_0}\rho^{\,b_0+1}
  |\mathcal F_{\rm hard}(Q\rho)|\,\dd\rho
  =
  Q^{-2}\mathfrak s_{\rm hard}(s)\,\dd\log s .
  \label{eq:hard-instanton-log-size-shell}
\end{equation}
If \(|\mathcal F_{\rm hard}(s)|\le C_\infty s^{-\sigma}\), the shell and the
tail both decay with the exponent
\[
  \Delta=\sigma-b_0-2 .
\]
For the \(SU(3)\), \(N_f=2\) differentiated four-slot kernel,
\(\Delta=1/3\).  One extra decade in the cutoff \(R\) then suppresses the
tail by only \(10^{-1/3}\), and a tenfold suppression of this power-tail
majorant requires three decades in \(R\).  With the normalized bound used in
\eqref{eq:hard-size-power-tail-bound}, the tail estimate is
\[
  3R^{-1/3};
\]
making this smaller than \(0.1\) requires \(R>27000\).  This number is not a
prediction of the amplitude.  It is a warning about evidence: a formally hard
one-instanton coefficient is not physically dominated by small instantons
until the chosen source profile, kinematics, or matching calculation improves
this log-shell bound.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Hard source envelope with physical screening]
\label{ca:hard-screened-instanton-size-shell}
The hard and screened size estimates above address different failures of the
same amplitude integral.  A hard source can suppress large instantons through
external form factors, while a physical Higgs, thermal, or medium scale can
screen them through the fluctuation determinant.  When both mechanisms are
present, the dominant size is not obtained by choosing whichever formula is
more convenient.  It is fixed by the combined size density.

Assume that in the selected one-instanton channel the absolute value of the
fully assembled density is bounded in the retained window by
\begin{equation}
  |\mathcal K(\rho)|
  \le
  K_0\,\rho^{A-1}
  \exp[-dQ\rho-m_{\rm scr}^2\rho^2],
  \qquad
  A>0,\quad d>0,\quad m_{\rm scr}>0.
  \label{eq:hard-screened-size-majorant}
\end{equation}
Here \(A=b_0+\beta_{\mathcal X}-4\) contains the collective density,
determinant convention, and zero-mode/source power of the chosen amplitude
channel.  The coefficient \(dQ\) is a proven exponential envelope for the
hard form factors or source wave packets; it is absent for the differentiated
individual zero-mode slots unless such a stronger source bound has actually
been supplied.  The scale \(m_{\rm scr}\) is a physical screening mass from
the same regulated problem, not a hand-inserted cutoff.

The absolute logarithmic size shell of the majorant is
\[
  \rho^A\exp[-dQ\rho-m_{\rm scr}^2\rho^2]\,\dd\log\rho .
\]
Its stationary point solves
\begin{equation}
  2m_{\rm scr}^2\rho_*^2+dQ\rho_*-A=0,
  \qquad
  \rho_*
  =
  \frac{2A}
       {dQ+\sqrt{d^2Q^2+8A m_{\rm scr}^2}}.
  \label{eq:hard-screened-log-shell}
\end{equation}
Thus the hard-only shell \(A/(dQ)\) and the screened-only shell
\(\sqrt{A/2}/m_{\rm scr}\) are limiting coordinates of one combined
problem:
\[
  \frac{\rho_*}{A/(dQ)}
  =
  \frac{2}{1+\sqrt{1+8A m_{\rm scr}^2/(d^2Q^2)}}.
\]
The two limiting diagnostics are
\[
  \epsilon_{\rm hard}=\frac{A m_{\rm scr}}{dQ},
  \qquad
  \epsilon_{\rm scr}=\frac{dQ}{m_{\rm scr}}\sqrt{\frac A2}.
\]
If \(\epsilon_{\rm hard}\ll1\), the hard envelope sets the shell and
screening is a perturbation.  If \(\epsilon_{\rm scr}\ll1\), the physical
screening scale sets the shell and the hard source is only a slowly varying
factor.  In the intermediate regime the two suppressions cooperate and the
dominant size is smaller than either pure estimate.

This criterion is deliberately stronger than convergence.  A hard instanton
coefficient is a controlled short-distance object only if the combined shell
and a surrounding tail bound lie inside a weak-coupling region,
\[
  \Lambda_{\rm QCD}\rho_*\ll1
\]
or inside the corresponding Higgs/thermal weak-coupling window.  If
\(\rho_*\) is instead set by a soft screening scale comparable to the
confinement scale, the formula is at best an absolute majorant on a
semiclassical coordinate; it is not a derivation of a physical QCD amplitude.
This is exactly the point hidden by a moduli-space-only discussion: the
collective coordinate supplies the integration variable, but the determinant,
zero-mode form factors, physical screening, and endpoint estimate decide
whether the instanton sector contributes a controlled observable coefficient.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[\(SU(3)\), two-flavor hard instanton
coefficient]
\label{ca:su3-two-flavor-hard-instanton-coefficient}
Specialize the source-amputated four-slot construction to vectorlike
\(SU(3)\) QCD with \(N_f=2\) Dirac fundamentals.  Use the Pauli--Villars
pure-gauge convention of
Proposition~\ref{prop:pure-gauge-pv-instanton-determinant-constant}, choose a
finite normalization of the light-fermion nonzero-mode determinant in the same
scheme, and suppose all four differentiated external zero-mode slots are hard:
\[
  |k_\ell|=c_\ell Q,\qquad c_\ell>0,\qquad \ell=1,\ldots,4 .
\]
Let \(\mathcal P_{\rm orient}\) denote the shared \(SU(2)\) orientation
projector of
\eqref{eq:instanton-four-slot-orientation-projector}, contracted with the
chosen spin-color source covectors.  In the leading one-instanton hard window,
the short coefficient multiplying the selected four-fermion source tensor has
the form
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  C^{(4)}_{\rm inst}(Q;R)
  &=
  \ee^{\ii\theta}\,
  C^{\rm PV}_{3}\,\mathcal R_{\rm f}^{\rm PV}(Q)\,
  \left(\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(Q)}\right)^6
  \Lambda_{\rm ht}^{29/3}\,Q^{-35/3}        \\
  &\qquad{}\times
  \mathcal P_{\rm orient}
  \int_0^{R}
    s^{32/3}
    \prod_{\ell=1}^{4}F_{\rm zm}(c_\ell s/2)\,\dd s
  +R_{\rm det}+R_{\rm zm}+R_{\rm src}+R_{\rm Schur}+R_{s>R}.
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:su3-nf2-hard-instanton-coefficient}
\end{equation}
Here \(C^{\rm PV}_{3}\simeq1.51\times10^{-3}\) is the orientation-integrated
pure-gauge constant in
\eqref{eq:pure-gauge-pv-instanton-density}, while
\(\mathcal R_{\rm f}^{\rm PV}\) is not fixed by the pure-gauge determinant
calculation; it is the finite light-fermion nonzero-mode determinant factor of
the same regulator and source normalization, with the finite-frame covariance
fixed by
Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-light-fermion-source-frame-covariance}.  The
five remainders are the
determinant, zero-mode/source, source-matching, Schur, and endpoint residuals
of Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-amplitude-assembly-error-budget}.

The powers in \eqref{eq:su3-nf2-hard-instanton-coefficient} are fixed as
follows.  For \(SU(3)\) with two Dirac fundamentals,
\[
  b_0=\frac{11}{3}3-\frac23\,2=\frac{29}{3}.
\]
The four differentiated zero-mode slots supply \(\rho^6\), so the size
integrand before form factors is \(\rho^{b_0+1}\).  After \(s=Q\rho\) and the
one-loop trade
\(\exp[-8\pi^2/g_{\rm ht}^2(Q)]Q^{b_0}=\Lambda_{\rm ht}^{b_0}\), the hard
coefficient carries
\[
  \Lambda_{\rm ht}^{29/3}Q^{-29/3-2}
  =
  \Lambda_{\rm ht}^{29/3}Q^{-35/3}.
\]
Thus the dimension of the coefficient is \(-2\), as required for a
source-amputated four-fermion operator.  This dimension count is not a
standalone amplitude: the orientation projector, the light-fermion determinant,
the zero-mode form factors, and the endpoint residual are still part of the
calculation.

The endpoint term is especially restrictive.  From
\eqref{eq:instanton-individual-zero-mode-form-factor-large},
\[
  F_{\rm zm}(c_\ell s/2)
  =
  6c_\ell^{-3}s^{-3}+O(s^{-5}),
  \qquad s\to\infty .
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \int_R^\infty
  s^{32/3}\prod_{\ell=1}^{4}F_{\rm zm}(c_\ell s/2)\,\dd s
  &=
  3\cdot6^4
  \left(\prod_{\ell=1}^{4}c_\ell^{-3}\right)R^{-1/3}
  +O(R^{-7/3}).
\end{aligned}
  \label{eq:su3-nf2-hard-tail-asymptotic}
\end{equation}
So even this hard four-slot coefficient has only a slow \(R^{-1/3}\) endpoint
tail unless the external source construction supplies stronger suppression.
This is the amplitude-level warning in 't Hooft's calculation: the BPST
moduli measure, the determinant constant, and the zero-mode tensor do not yet
give a controlled physical four-point contribution until the hard-source tail
and the remaining remainders have been bounded in the same scheme.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Finite-window bound for a hard
instanton coefficient]
\label{ca:hard-instanton-finite-window-bound}
The hard coefficient
\eqref{eq:su3-nf2-hard-instanton-coefficient} should be quoted only with a
window error bound.  After the center delta function, source tensor, and
orientation projection have been fixed, write the retained dimensionless
leading size integrand as
\[
  H_{\rm lead}(s)
  =
  s^{32/3}\,
  \mathcal P_{\rm orient}(s)
  \prod_{\ell=1}^{4}F_{\rm zm}(c_\ell s/2),
\]
where \(\mathcal P_{\rm orient}(s)\) includes any source or orientation
weight which remains inside the size integral.  For a cutoff \(R\), define
\begin{equation}
  J_R=\int_0^R H_{\rm lead}(s)\,\dd s,\qquad
  M_R=\int_0^R |H_{\rm lead}(s)|\,\dd s,\qquad
  T_R=\int_R^\infty |H_{\rm lead}(s)|\,\dd s .
  \label{eq:hard-instanton-window-jmt}
\end{equation}
The number \(M_R\) is not the coefficient; it is the absolute mass of the
retained window.  Its role is to measure how much cancellation is present in
the actual signed or complex coefficient \(J_R\).

Suppose the finite-regulator density on \(0<s<R\) differs from the displayed
leading density by multiplicative determinant, zero-mode, and source errors
with absolute window bounds
\[
  |\varepsilon_{\rm det}(s)|\le\epsilon_{\rm det},\qquad
  |\varepsilon_{\rm zm}(s)|\le\epsilon_{\rm zm},\qquad
  |\varepsilon_{\rm src}(s)|\le\epsilon_{\rm src},
\]
and suppose the Schur-complement remainder satisfies
\[
  \int_0^R|\Delta_{\rm Schur}(s)|\,\dd s
  \le\epsilon_{\rm Schur}M_R .
\]
Finally suppose the exact contribution from the omitted tail, including the
difference between the exact and leading kernels beyond \(R\), is bounded by
\[
  |R_{s>R}|\le \tau_R M_R .
\]
Then, after restoring the common prefactor \(\mathcal N(Q)\) in
\eqref{eq:su3-nf2-hard-instanton-coefficient},
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  C_{\rm inst}^{(4),{\rm ex}}(Q)
  -
  \mathcal N(Q)J_R
  \right|
  \le
  |\mathcal N(Q)|\,M_R\,
  \bigl(
    \epsilon_{\rm det}
    +\epsilon_{\rm zm}
    +\epsilon_{\rm src}
    +\epsilon_{\rm Schur}
    +\tau_R
  \bigr).
  \label{eq:hard-instanton-window-absolute-bound}
\end{equation}
If the retained leading window is nondegenerate in the sense that
\[
  |J_R|\ge \kappa_R M_R,\qquad \kappa_R>0,
\]
the same data give the relative error bound
\begin{equation}
  \frac{
  \left|
  C_{\rm inst}^{(4),{\rm ex}}(Q)
  -
  \mathcal N(Q)J_R
  \right|}
  {|\mathcal N(Q)J_R|}
  \le
  \frac{
    \epsilon_{\rm det}
    +\epsilon_{\rm zm}
    +\epsilon_{\rm src}
    +\epsilon_{\rm Schur}
    +\tau_R}
  {\kappa_R}.
  \label{eq:hard-instanton-window-relative-bound}
\end{equation}
Thus endpoint convergence is only one ingredient.  A hard instanton
coefficient can be numerically unstable if the retained window is small after
signed source or orientation cancellations, even when \(T_R/M_R\) is small.

For the differentiated \(SU(3)\), \(N_f=2\) four-slot kernel, a power-tail
majorant of the form
\[
  |H_{\rm lead}(s)|
  \le
  B_\infty s^{-4/3},
  \qquad s\ge R_0,
\]
gives
\begin{equation}
  T_R
  \le
  3B_\infty R^{-1/3},
  \qquad R\ge R_0 .
  \label{eq:hard-instanton-window-tail-bound}
\end{equation}
With only the individual zero-mode large-\(s\) envelope one may take
\(B_\infty\) proportional to
\(6^4\prod_\ell c_\ell^{-3}\) times the source-orientation norm bound.  This
is the quantitative meaning of the slow-tail warning above: a finite hard
coefficient becomes a controlled short-distance observable only after the
chosen source supplies a usable \(M_R\), a noncancellation margin
\(\kappa_R\), and a tail/error budget in the same normalization.  Otherwise
the calculation has produced a valuable source coordinate, not yet a
controlled physical coefficient.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Four-source instanton amplitude rank-and-error bound]
\label{ca:four-source-instanton-amplitude-rank-bound}
The finite-window coefficient above still assumes that the four external
fermion slots have already been converted into a nondegenerate zero-mode
source tensor.  This is the step which turns the collective-coordinate
integral into the kind of four-point amplitude computed in the original
instanton calculation.  For \(N_f=2\), let
\(h^R_1,h^R_2,h^L_1,h^L_2\) be four fixed external test spinors or amputated
source covectors in the chosen regulator and source frame.  On a selected
instanton chart define the right and left zero-mode overlap matrices
\[
  B_R(z)_{if}=\langle h_i^R,\psi_{0,f}^R(A_z)\rangle,\qquad
  B_L(z)_{jf}=\langle h_j^L,\psi_{0,f}^L(A_z)\rangle,
  \qquad i,j,f=1,2 .
\]
After orientation and spin-color contraction, the fermion zero-mode part of
the four-source instanton integrand contains
\[
  Z_0(z)=\det B_R(z)\det B_L(z).
\]
Thus a hard momentum scale by itself does not guarantee a nonzero four-point
instanton amplitude.  The two right slots and the two left slots must each
span the corresponding zero-mode coefficient plane after the same
orientation and source projection have been applied.

Let \(B_R^0(s,U)\) and \(B_L^0(s,U)\) be the retained leading overlap matrices
inside \(0<s<R\).  Suppose their entries are bounded by \(L_R,L_L\), while
the exact overlaps obey
\[
  |(B_R-B_R^0)_{if}|\le\eta_R,\qquad
  |(B_L-B_L^0)_{jf}|\le\eta_L .
\]
For any \(2\times2\) matrix \(B^0\) with \(|B^0_{ab}|\le L\),
\begin{equation}
  |\det(B^0+\Delta B)-\det B^0|
  \le
  4L\eta+2\eta^2,
  \qquad |\Delta B_{ab}|\le\eta .
  \label{eq:four-source-determinant-stability}
\end{equation}
Consequently, if
\[
  |\det B_R^0|\ge d_R>0,\qquad
  |\det B_L^0|\ge d_L>0
\]
on the retained window, the zero-mode source factor has relative error
\begin{equation}
  \epsilon_{\rm rank}
  \le
  \frac{E_R}{d_R}
  +
  \frac{E_L}{d_L}
  +
  \frac{E_RE_L}{d_Rd_L},
  \qquad
  E_R=4L_R\eta_R+2\eta_R^2,\quad
  E_L=4L_L\eta_L+2\eta_L^2 .
  \label{eq:four-source-rank-error}
\end{equation}
The word ``rank'' in \(\epsilon_{\rm rank}\) is intentional: if either
determinant margin \(d_R\) or \(d_L\) is absent, the four-source amplitude is
not controlled by the BPST measure, by the nonzero-mode determinant, or by the
large-momentum tail estimate.

Write \(J_R\) and \(M_R\) for the signed retained integral and absolute mass
from \eqref{eq:hard-instanton-window-jmt}, now including
\(\det B_R^0\det B_L^0\) in the leading source tensor.  If the determinant,
Schur, projection/matching, and endpoint bounds on the same window are
\(\epsilon_{\rm det}\), \(\epsilon_{\rm Schur}\),
\(\epsilon_{\rm proj}\), and \(\tau_R\), then the Euclidean four-source
coefficient obeys
\begin{equation}
  \left|
    C_{\rm inst}^{(4),{\rm ex}}[\mathfrak h]
    -\mathcal N(Q)J_R[\mathfrak h]
  \right|
  \le
  |\mathcal N(Q)|M_R[\mathfrak h]\,
  \bigl(
    \epsilon_{\rm det}
    +\epsilon_{\rm rank}
    +\epsilon_{\rm Schur}
    +\epsilon_{\rm proj}
    +\tau_R
  \bigr).
  \label{eq:four-source-instanton-amplitude-bound}
\end{equation}
A physical scattering, spectral, or OPE coefficient still requires the
continuation/projection residuals already displayed in
\eqref{eq:instanton-amplitude-pipeline-physical-map}.  The point of
\eqref{eq:four-source-instanton-amplitude-bound} is narrower but crucial:
the hard four-point instanton calculation is not an analysis of the instanton
moduli space alone.  It is a stability statement for a product of the
collective-coordinate density, the fluctuation determinant, the four
zero-mode source overlaps, the size-window tail, and the final observable
projection.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Instanton size-factor split]
\label{ca:instanton-wilsonian-size-factorization}
Let \(K_{\Lambda}(\rho;\mu,\mathcal J)\) denote the fully paired
finite-regulator one-instanton size integrand for a selected source family:
the center phase, orientation tensor, nonzero-mode determinant, zero-mode
source coefficient, and any anomaly-line pairing have already been included.
Fix a finite upper regulator \(\rho_{\max}\) and a factorization scale
\(\mu_I\) with
\[
  0<\rho_I:=\mu_I^{-1}<\rho_{\max}.
\]
Then the exact finite-regulator contribution on this size window has the
split
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_{\Lambda}^{[0,\rho_{\max}]}
  =
  \mathcal A_{\Lambda}^{<}(\mu_I)
  +
  \mathcal A_{\Lambda}^{>}(\mu_I),
  \qquad
  \mathcal A_{\Lambda}^{<}(\mu_I)
  =
  \int_0^{\rho_I}K_\Lambda(\rho)\,\dd\rho ,
  \quad
  \mathcal A_{\Lambda}^{>}(\mu_I)
  =
  \int_{\rho_I}^{\rho_{\max}}K_\Lambda(\rho)\,\dd\rho .
  \label{eq:instanton-size-wilsonian-split}
\end{equation}
If \(K_\Lambda\) is continuous at \(\rho_I\), the factorization-scale
derivatives are the boundary flux through the artificial cut:
\begin{equation}
  \partial_{\log\mu_I}\mathcal A_{\Lambda}^{<}(\mu_I)
  =
  -\rho_I K_\Lambda(\rho_I),
  \qquad
  \partial_{\log\mu_I}\mathcal A_{\Lambda}^{>}(\mu_I)
  =
  +\rho_I K_\Lambda(\rho_I).
  \label{eq:instanton-size-factorization-boundary-flow}
\end{equation}
Thus \(\mathcal A_{\Lambda}^{[0,\rho_{\max}]}\) is independent of
\(\mu_I\), while the short-size piece alone is not.

The semiclassical local 't Hooft vertex is therefore a Wilsonian object.  If
one replaces \(K_\Lambda\) by the one-loop small-size approximation
\(K_{\rm sc}^{<}\) only for \(0<\rho<\rho_I\), then
\[
  C_{\rm inst}^{<}(\mu_I;\mathcal J)
  =
  \int_0^{\rho_I}K_{\rm sc}^{<}(\rho;\mu,\mathcal J)\,\dd\rho
\]
is a short-instanton coefficient.  Its
\(-\rho_IK_{\rm sc}^{<}(\rho_I)\) scale derivative is cancelled only by the
long-distance matrix element or remainder assigned to \(\rho>\rho_I\), up to
the matching error between \(K_\Lambda\) and \(K_{\rm sc}^{<}\) near the cut.
Discarding that long part leaves a spurious \(\mu_I\)-dependence whose size is
precisely the boundary density.  For a hard external scale \(Q\), choosing
\(\rho_I=R/Q\) identifies this boundary term with the same large-size tail
diagnostic in \eqref{eq:hard-size-tail-change-variable}.  The computed
short-instanton coefficient is useful only when this boundary flux and the
remaining \(\rho>\rho_I\) contribution are controlled by the physical source,
screening scale, phase, or matching calculation under consideration.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Short-instanton OPE coefficient]
\label{ca:short-instanton-ope-coefficient}
The short side of
ControlledApproximation~\ref{ca:instanton-wilsonian-size-factorization} becomes
a local 't Hooft vertex only after it is projected onto a renormalized local
operator basis.  Let \(\{[O_I]_\mu\}_{I\in\mathcal B}\) be a finite
source-normalized basis in the selected quantum-number channel, containing
\([\det(\bar q_Rq_L)]_\mu\) and any operators of the same dimension and
symmetry which are retained by the chosen hard OPE.  Suppose the short-size
part of a gauge-invariant source correlator admits the expansion
\begin{equation}
  G_{\mathcal J,\Lambda}^{<}(\mu_I)
  =
  \sum_{I\in\mathcal B}
    C_I^{<}(\mu_I,\mu)\,
    \left\langle\mathcal J\,[O_I]_\mu\right\rangle
  +
  R_{\rm OPE}^{<}(\mu_I,\mu).
  \label{eq:short-instanton-ope-coefficient-expansion}
\end{equation}
The coefficient \(C_I^{<}\) is obtained by integrating the small-size instanton
density, the nonzero-mode determinant, the zero-mode source coefficient, and
the orientation tensor against the projector onto \([O_I]_\mu\), over
\(0<\rho<\rho_I=\mu_I^{-1}\).  For the leading \(N_f=2\) determinant channel,
this is the coefficient of \([\det(\bar q_Rq_L)]_\mu\); derivative operators,
mass insertions, and source-matching remnants belong either to the retained
basis or to \(R_{\rm OPE}^{<}\).

This projection has two different scale laws.  The renormalization scale
\(\mu\) is the composite-operator scale.  In the convention of
Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-renormalized-operators-minimal-subtraction},
\[
  \frac{\dd}{\dd\log\mu}[O_I]_\mu
  =
  -\gamma_{IK}(\mu)[O_K]_\mu .
\]
Therefore the coefficient row must obey
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd}{\dd\log\mu}C_K^{<}(\mu_I,\mu)
  =
  \sum_{I\in\mathcal B}C_I^{<}(\mu_I,\mu)\,\gamma_{IK}(\mu)
  \label{eq:short-instanton-coefficient-rg}
\end{equation}
up to the truncation error \(R_{\rm OPE}^{<}\).  A finite operator-frame change
\([\widetilde O_A]_\mu=M_{AI}(\mu)[O_I]_\mu\) changes the displayed coefficient
by the inverse rule
\begin{equation}
  \widetilde C_A^{<}=C_I^{<}(M^{-1})_{IA},
  \qquad
  \sum_A\widetilde C_A^{<}[\widetilde O_A]_\mu
  =
  \sum_I C_I^{<}[O_I]_\mu .
  \label{eq:short-instanton-coefficient-frame-change}
\end{equation}
Thus the local 't Hooft vertex coefficient is not a scheme-independent number;
only its pairing with the renormalized operator basis and matrix elements is.

The factorization scale \(\mu_I\) is different.  If
\(K_I^{\rm OPE}(\rho;\mu)\) is the \([O_I]_\mu\)-projected short-size
integrand, then
\begin{equation}
  \partial_{\log\mu_I}C_I^{<}(\mu_I,\mu)
  =
  -\rho_I K_I^{\rm OPE}(\rho_I;\mu).
  \label{eq:short-instanton-coefficient-factorization-flow}
\end{equation}
This artificial boundary flow is not cancelled by operator anomalous
dimensions.  It is cancelled by the long-size matrix element or remainder, as
in \eqref{eq:instanton-size-factorization-boundary-flow}.  Consequently a
standalone local 't Hooft operator with no declared \(\mu_I\), no operator
scheme, and no long-distance remainder is not a physical instanton amplitude.
\end{controlledapproximation}

This hard-size window is the amplitude counterpart of the local
't Hooft vertex.  The local operator records the \(Q\rho\ll1\) tensor and
selection rule, while \eqref{eq:hard-momentum-instanton-size-factor} records
how the same zero modes and fluctuation determinant enter an actual hard
correlator.  It also explains why the mass-saturated vacuum activity below is
a different object: a vacuum theta term has no external form factor to
exclude \(\rho\to\infty\), so its large-size behavior is an infrared
question, not a semiclassical prediction.

Thus the \(Q=1\) amplitude is the microscopic origin of the \(U(1)_A\)
selection rule.  The determinant in
\eqref{eq:qcd-thooft-vertex-leading-local} carries axial charge \(2N_f\);
equivalently, a mass-saturated instanton contribution depends on the CP-odd
combination \(\bar\theta=\theta+\arg\det M\) from
\eqref{eq:qcd-physical-theta}.  This gives the same anomalous Jacobian in the
coordinate system where the fermion zero modes of the instanton background
have been integrated.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Mass-saturated vacuum activity and the
size integral]
\label{ca:mass-saturated-instanton-vacuum-activity}
Assume vectorlike \(SU(N_c)\) QCD with \(N_f\) Dirac fundamentals, a diagonal
renormalized mass matrix \(M(\mu)\), and a one-instanton size window
\(\rho_-<\rho<\rho_+\) in which the one-loop density and the leading
zero-mode mass overlaps are valid.  In the same local normalization as
\eqref{eq:qcd-thooft-vertex-leading-local}, saturating one Dirac zero-mode
pair by the mass term supplies the dimensionless factor \(m_f(\mu)\rho\).
Thus the mass-saturated one-instanton vacuum activity in this window has the
form
\begin{equation}
  \zeta_m^{[\rho_-,\rho_+]}(\mu)
  =
  \mathcal C_{\mathcal S,N_c,N_f}\,
  \left(\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(\mu)}\right)^{2N_c}
  \exp\!\left[-\frac{8\pi^2}{g_{\rm ht}^2(\mu)}\right]
  |\det M(\mu)|\,\mu^{b_0}
  \int_{\rho_-}^{\rho_+}
  \rho^{\,b_0+N_f-5}\,\dd\rho ,
  \label{eq:mass-saturated-instanton-window-activity}
\end{equation}
up to higher-loop/operator-renormalization factors of the chosen scheme.  The
constant \(\mathcal C_{\mathcal S,N_c,N_f}\) contains the pure-gauge
orientation and determinant convention together with the light-fermion
nonzero-mode factor \(\mathcal R_{\rm f}^{\mathcal S}\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-fermion-determinant-zero-mode-factorization},
evaluated in the same small-mass window.  It does not include the displayed
\(\prod_f(m_f\rho)\) factor: that product is the zero-mode saturation
determinant.  The corresponding \(Q=1\) vacuum term carries the phase
\begin{equation}
  V_4\zeta_m^{[\rho_-,\rho_+]}
  \exp\!\left[\ii(\theta+\arg\det M)\right],
  \label{eq:mass-saturated-instanton-vacuum-phase}
\end{equation}
while the anti-instanton term carries the complex conjugate phase.

The displayed size integral isolates the two endpoint questions:
\begin{equation}
  \int_{\rho_-}^{\rho_+}
  \rho^{\,b_0+N_f-5}\,\dd\rho
  =
  \begin{cases}
    \dfrac{\rho_+^{\,b_0+N_f-4}-\rho_-^{\,b_0+N_f-4}}
          {b_0+N_f-4},
      & b_0+N_f\ne4,\\[10pt]
    \log(\rho_+/\rho_-),
      & b_0+N_f=4 .
  \end{cases}
  \label{eq:mass-saturated-size-window-integral}
\end{equation}
The small-size endpoint is locally finite precisely when
\(b_0+N_f>4\).  For \(SU(3)\), this margin is
\[
  b_0+N_f-4
  =
  7+\frac{N_f}{3},
\]
so the mass-saturated one-instanton vacuum term is not obstructed at
\(\rho=0\) in the asymptotically free range.  The same positive power means
that extending the one-loop formula to \(\rho_+=\infty\) would give an
infrared power divergence.  That divergence is not a new ultraviolet
counterterm; it says that the zero-temperature large-size region is outside
the controlled weak-coupling instanton calculation.  A finite dilute activity
therefore requires an additional physical infrared cutoff or mechanism, such
as a Higgs scale, a thermal screening scale, or a separately justified
confining/chiral-dynamics input.

If one quark is massless and no external source saturates its zero modes,
\(\det M=0\) and the vacuum activity
\eqref{eq:mass-saturated-instanton-window-activity} vanishes.  This is
compatible with nonzero instanton contributions to fermionic correlators:
those correlators use the source-differentiated zero-mode coefficient in
\eqref{eq:proper-time-four-fermion-instanton-amplitude} instead of the mass
determinant in \eqref{eq:mass-saturated-instanton-window-activity}.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{proposition}[Screened one-instanton size integral]
\label{prop:screened-one-instanton-size-integral}
Let a selected one-instanton amplitude channel have the one-loop small-size
density
\[
  K_{\rm sc}(\rho)
  =
  K_0\,\rho^{A-1},
  \qquad A=b_0+\beta_{\mathcal X}-4>0,
\]
after the collective-coordinate density, nonzero-mode determinant convention,
and zero-mode source coefficient have been assembled.  Suppose a physical
infrared mechanism in the same regulated problem contributes a positive
screening factor
\[
  \exp[-m_{\rm scr}^2\rho^2],
  \qquad m_{\rm scr}>0,
\]
for example from Higgsing, thermal screening, or a declared source envelope.
The screened leading contribution is then
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_{\rm scr}^{(0)}
  =
  K_0\int_0^\infty
  \rho^{A-1}\ee^{-m_{\rm scr}^2\rho^2}\,\dd\rho
  =
  \frac{K_0}{2}\,
  m_{\rm scr}^{-A}\,
  \Gamma\!\left(\frac A2\right).
  \label{eq:screened-one-instanton-size-integral}
\end{equation}
In the leading screened density, even moments of the instanton size are
\begin{equation}
  \bigl\langle\rho^{2n}\bigr\rangle_0
  =
  m_{\rm scr}^{-2n}
  \frac{\Gamma(A/2+n)}{\Gamma(A/2)},
  \qquad
  m_{\rm scr}^2\langle\rho^2\rangle_0=\frac A2 .
  \label{eq:screened-one-instanton-size-moments}
\end{equation}
If \(A>1\), the logarithmic size-shell density
\(\rho^{A}\exp[-m_{\rm scr}^2\rho^2]\) is stationary at
\begin{equation}
  m_{\rm scr}^2\rho_{\rm shell}^2=\frac{A}{2},
  \label{eq:screened-one-instanton-log-shell}
\end{equation}
while the ordinary \(\dd\rho\)-density is stationary at
\begin{equation}
  m_{\rm scr}^2\rho_{\rm dens}^2=\frac{A-1}{2}.
  \label{eq:screened-one-instanton-density-saddle}
\end{equation}
For \(SU(3)\) with \(N_f=2\) massive Dirac fundamentals in the mass-saturated
vacuum channel, \(\beta_{\mathcal X}=N_f\) and
\[
  A=b_0+N_f-4=\frac{23}{3}.
\]
Thus the screened leading activity is proportional to
\[
  m_{\rm scr}^{-23/3}\Gamma(23/6),
  \qquad
  m_{\rm scr}^2\langle\rho^2\rangle_0=\frac{23}{6},
  \qquad
  m_{\rm scr}^2\rho_{\rm shell}^2=\frac{23}{6}.
\]
This is a controlled amplitude formula only when the same physical screening
scale keeps the dominant shell inside the weak-coupling and finite-regulator
window.  Sending \(m_{\rm scr}\to0\) recovers the infrared divergence of
\eqref{eq:mass-saturated-size-window-integral}; the screened formula is not a
license to use the one-loop instanton density at arbitrarily large size.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The substitution \(u=m_{\rm scr}^2\rho^2\) gives
\[
  \int_0^\infty\rho^{A-1}\ee^{-m_{\rm scr}^2\rho^2}\,\dd\rho
  =
  \frac12m_{\rm scr}^{-A}
  \int_0^\infty u^{A/2-1}\ee^{-u}\,\dd u,
\]
which is \eqref{eq:screened-one-instanton-size-integral}.  Dividing the same
integral with \(A\) replaced by \(A+2n\) by the \(n=0\) integral gives
\eqref{eq:screened-one-instanton-size-moments}.  The stationary-shell formulas
come from differentiating
\(A\log\rho-m_{\rm scr}^2\rho^2\) for the \(\dd\log\rho\) shell and
\((A-1)\log\rho-m_{\rm scr}^2\rho^2\) for the ordinary density.  The
\(SU(3)\), \(N_f=2\) specialization substitutes
\(b_0=29/3\) and \(\beta_{\mathcal X}=2\).
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Thermal determinant screening of the size integral]
\label{ca:thermal-instanton-determinant-screening}
Consider weak-coupling finite-temperature \(SU(N_c)\) QCD with \(N_f\) light
Dirac fundamentals and a one-instanton amplitude channel whose zero-temperature
small-size density has the form used in
