Proposition~\ref{prop:screened-one-instanton-size-integral}.  The leading
high-temperature fluctuation determinant around the periodic one-instanton
background supplies the Gaussian size weight
\begin{equation}
  K_T(\rho)
  =
  K_0\,\rho^{A-1}
  \exp[-m_T^2\rho^2]\,
  \exp[R_T(\rho)],
  \qquad
  m_T^2=\pi^2T^2\,\frac{2N_c+N_f}{3}.
  \label{eq:thermal-instanton-screening-density}
\end{equation}
Here \(R_T\) denotes the nonquadratic finite-temperature determinant and
caloron-shape remainder in the same regulator and source convention.  In the
trace-delta coupling convention of
Chapter~\ref{ch:thermal-gauge-theory-screening},
\eqref{eq:one-loop-debye-mass-general} gives
\[
  \frac{m_D^2}{g_{\rm YM}^2}
  =
  T^2\,\frac{2N_c+N_f}{3}
\]
for fundamental Dirac matter, so \(m_T^2=\pi^2m_D^2/g_{\rm YM}^2\).  The
thermal instanton cutoff is therefore a determinant response of the plasma,
not a classical bound on the BPST moduli space.

If the chosen amplitude window controls the residual by
\[
  |R_T(\rho)|\le\varepsilon_T ,
\]
define the Gaussian approximation
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_T^{G}
  =
  \frac{K_0}{2}
  \left(\pi^2T^2\frac{2N_c+N_f}{3}\right)^{-A/2}
  \Gamma\!\left(\frac A2\right)
  \label{eq:thermal-instanton-gaussian-amplitude}
\end{equation}
and the absolute Gaussian majorant
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal M_T^{G}
  =
  \frac{|K_0|}{2}
  \left(\pi^2T^2\frac{2N_c+N_f}{3}\right)^{-A/2}
  \Gamma\!\left(\frac A2\right).
  \label{eq:thermal-instanton-gaussian-majorant}
\end{equation}
Since
\(|\ee^{R_T(\rho)}-1|\le\ee^{\varepsilon_T}-1\), the general
source-projected amplitude satisfies the manifestly positive estimate
\begin{equation}
  \left|\mathcal A_T-\mathcal A_T^{G}\right|
  \le
  \bigl(\ee^{\varepsilon_T}-1\bigr)\mathcal M_T^{G}
  \label{eq:thermal-instanton-residual-bound}
\end{equation}
whenever the same size window contains the support of the amplitude.  The
stronger positive-activity form
\[
  \left|\mathcal A_T-\mathcal A_T^{G}\right|
  \le
  \bigl(\ee^{\varepsilon_T}-1\bigr)\mathcal A_T^{G}
\]
is allowed only when \(K_0\ge0\) and the residual is real in the selected
channel, so that the integrand is a positive activity density.  If
\(K_0=\ee^{\ii\varphi}|K_0|\) has a fixed phase and \(R_T\) is real, the same
proof gives the fixed-phase estimate with \(|\mathcal A_T^{G}|\) on the
right-hand side.  For a genuinely complex source amplitude, only
\eqref{eq:thermal-instanton-residual-bound} is an absolute-error bound.  The
leading thermal size moments are the moments in
\eqref{eq:screened-one-instanton-size-moments} with \(m_{\rm scr}=m_T\); in a
complex channel they are moments of the Gaussian majorant, not probability
moments of the amplitude itself.

For the mass-saturated \(SU(3)\), \(N_f=2\) vacuum channel,
\[
  m_T^2=\frac83\pi^2T^2,\qquad
  A=\frac{23}{3},
\]
so
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_T^{G}
  =
  \frac{K_0}{2}
  \left(\frac83\pi^2T^2\right)^{-23/6}
  \Gamma\!\left(\frac{23}{6}\right),
  \qquad
  \pi^2T^2\langle\rho^2\rangle_G
  =
  \pi^2T^2\rho_{\rm shell}^2
  =
  \frac{23}{16}.
  \label{eq:thermal-su3-nf2-screened-instanton}
\end{equation}
The formula is useful only in a regime where the periodic-instanton determinant,
the residual \(R_T\), and the source or volume limits are controlled.  Near the
thermal transition, or in zero-temperature QCD after sending \(T\to0\), it
does not replace the large-size dynamics by a semiclassical prediction.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Dilute instanton gas as an amplitude expansion]
\label{ca:dilute-instanton-gas-amplitude}
Suppose the regulated one-instanton and one-anti-instanton amplitudes obtained
above admit finite, translation-invariant vacuum activities \(\zeta_\Lambda\)
per Euclidean four-volume after the size, orientation, nonzero-mode
determinant, and any required zero-mode mass-overlap factors have all been
included.  Assume further that the multi-instanton cluster expansion has a
window in which overlap corrections, instanton--anti-instanton interactions,
and boundary-face remainders contribute \(o(V_4)\) to \(\log Z\).  Then the
leading dilute-gas theta dependence is not a new moduli-space statement; it is
the Poisson sum of the already constructed amplitudes:
\begin{equation}
  \frac{Z_{\rm dig}(\bar\theta)}{Z_0}
  =
  \sum_{n_+,n_-\ge0}
  \frac{(V_4\zeta_\Lambda)^{n_+}}{n_+!}
  \frac{(V_4\zeta_\Lambda)^{n_-}}{n_-!}
  \ee^{\ii(n_+-n_-)\bar\theta}
  =
  \exp\!\left(2V_4\zeta_\Lambda\cos\bar\theta\right).
  \label{eq:dilute-instanton-gas-partition}
\end{equation}
Thus the vacuum-energy difference in this approximation is
\begin{equation}
  E_{\rm dig}(\bar\theta)-E_{\rm dig}(0)
  =
  2\zeta_\Lambda(1-\cos\bar\theta),
  \label{eq:dilute-instanton-gas-energy}
\end{equation}
and the topological-charge cumulants at \(\bar\theta=0\) obey
\begin{equation}
  \kappa_{2m}(Q)=2V_4\zeta_\Lambda,
  \qquad
  \kappa_{2m+1}(Q)=0,
  \qquad
  \chi_{\rm top}^{\rm dig}=2\zeta_\Lambda .
  \label{eq:dilute-instanton-gas-cumulants}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, writing
\[
  E_{\rm dig}(\bar\theta)-E_{\rm dig}(0)
  =
  \frac12\chi_{\rm top}^{\rm dig}\bar\theta^2
  \left(
    1+b_2^{\rm dig}\bar\theta^2+O(\bar\theta^4)
  \right)
\]
gives \(b_2^{\rm dig}=-1/12\).

This is a controlled semiclassical amplitude expansion only when the activity
is finite and dilute in the relevant correlation volume.  If a massless quark
zero mode is not saturated by a mass or source, the vacuum activity for this
term vanishes; instanton sectors may still contribute to fermionic correlators
such as \eqref{eq:proper-time-four-fermion-instanton-amplitude}.  If the
\(\rho\)-integral is infrared divergent, if small-instanton boundary terms are
not controlled, or if instanton interactions are not negligible, then the
Poisson form \eqref{eq:dilute-instanton-gas-partition} has not been derived.
In particular, this dilute four-dimensional gas is not a derivation of
confinement in zero-temperature Yang--Mills.  Its output is the conditional
theta-dependence and zero-mode-saturated amplitude data above.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[First cluster correction to the dilute
instanton gas]
\label{ca:first-cluster-correction-dilute-instantons}
The Poisson formula
\eqref{eq:dilute-instanton-gas-partition} is the zeroth term in a cluster
expansion.  The collective-coordinate chart supplies the integration
variables, while the finite-regulator amplitude scheme must also supply
finite two-body connected cluster integrals \(\mathfrak B_{\sigma\tau}\),
\(\sigma,\tau\in\{+,-\}\), after all relative centers, sizes, orientations,
nonzero-mode determinants, zero-mode saturations, and interaction remainders
in the selected window have been included.  With
\(z_+=\zeta_\Lambda\ee^{\ii\bar\theta}\) and
\(z_-=\zeta_\Lambda\ee^{-\ii\bar\theta}\), the first Mayer correction to the
logarithm has the local form
\begin{equation}
  \frac1{V_4}\log\frac{Z_{\rm cl}(\bar\theta)}{Z_0}
  =
  z_+ + z_-
  +
  \frac12
  \sum_{\sigma,\tau=\pm}
    z_\sigma z_\tau\,\mathfrak B_{\sigma\tau}
  +O(\zeta_\Lambda^3).
  \label{eq:instanton-first-mayer-pressure}
\end{equation}
Assume CP symmetry in this window, so
\[
  \mathfrak B_{++}=\mathfrak B_{--}=:\mathfrak B_2,
  \qquad
  \mathfrak B_{+-}=\mathfrak B_{-+}=:\mathfrak B_0 .
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
  \frac1{V_4}\log\frac{Z_{\rm cl}(\bar\theta)}{Z_0}
  =
  2\zeta_\Lambda\cos\bar\theta
  +
  \zeta_\Lambda^2
  \bigl(\mathfrak B_2\cos(2\bar\theta)+\mathfrak B_0\bigr)
  +O(\zeta_\Lambda^3).
  \label{eq:instanton-first-mayer-theta-pressure}
\end{equation}
The neutral instanton--anti-instanton molecule \(\mathfrak B_0\) changes the
vacuum pressure and the validity of the dilute expansion, but it cancels from
the energy difference \(E(\bar\theta)-E(0)\) at this order.  The same-charge
clusters carry topological charge \(\pm2\), and therefore generate a second
theta harmonic:
\begin{equation}
  E_{\rm cl}(\bar\theta)-E_{\rm cl}(0)
  =
  2\zeta_\Lambda(1-\cos\bar\theta)
  +
  \zeta_\Lambda^2\mathfrak B_2(1-\cos(2\bar\theta))
  +O(\zeta_\Lambda^3).
  \label{eq:instanton-first-cluster-energy}
\end{equation}
Consequently
\begin{equation}
  \chi_{\rm top}^{\rm cl}
  =
  2\zeta_\Lambda+4\zeta_\Lambda^2\mathfrak B_2+O(\zeta_\Lambda^3),
  \qquad
  \partial_{\bar\theta}^4E_{\rm cl}\big|_{0}
  =
  -2\zeta_\Lambda-16\zeta_\Lambda^2\mathfrak B_2+O(\zeta_\Lambda^3),
  \label{eq:instanton-first-cluster-curvatures}
\end{equation}
and, in the expansion convention of
\eqref{eq:dilute-instanton-gas-energy},
\begin{equation}
  b_2^{\rm cl}
  =
  -\frac{1+8\zeta_\Lambda\mathfrak B_2}
         {12(1+2\zeta_\Lambda\mathfrak B_2)}
  +O(\zeta_\Lambda^2)
  =
  -\frac1{12}-\frac12\zeta_\Lambda\mathfrak B_2
  +O(\zeta_\Lambda^2).
  \label{eq:instanton-first-cluster-b2}
\end{equation}
Thus \(b_2=-1/12\) is not a universal instanton prediction.  It is the
Poisson limit of independent \(Q=\pm1\) amplitudes.  The first same-charge
connected cluster already changes the fourth theta curvature, while a neutral
instanton--anti-instanton molecule first tests the cluster expansion and
neutral observables rather than the theta dependence at this order.

The identities above are only as controlled as the two-body cluster
integrals.  They require a single regulator and source convention for the
one-body amplitudes, relative collective-coordinate measure, fluctuation
determinants, zero-mode overlap factors, and boundary-face estimates.  They
do not derive \(\mathfrak B_{\sigma\tau}\) from ADHM data without the
determinant and interaction estimates, nor do they prove that the omitted
three-body and higher clusters are small.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Thermal dilute topological susceptibility]
\label{ca:thermal-dilute-instanton-susceptibility}
Combine the thermal determinant-screened one-instanton activity of
ControlledApproximation~\ref{ca:thermal-instanton-determinant-screening} with
the dilute-gas hypothesis in
ControlledApproximation~\ref{ca:dilute-instanton-gas-amplitude}.  Write the
Gaussian one-instanton activity per Euclidean four-volume in a positive
mass/source-saturated channel as
\begin{equation}
  \zeta_T^{G}
  =
  \frac{K_{T,0}}{2}
  \left(\pi^2T^2\,\frac{2N_c+N_f}{3}\right)^{-A/2}
  \Gamma\!\left(\frac A2\right),
  \qquad
  A=b_0+\beta_{\mathcal X}-4,
  \label{eq:thermal-dilute-gaussian-activity}
\end{equation}
where \(K_{T,0}\) contains the collective-coordinate normalization,
zero-temperature nonzero-mode determinant convention, mass/source
zero-mode-saturation coefficient, and any finite source-frame normalization in
the selected channel.  Here \(K_{T,0}\ge0\) and the residual is real; otherwise
one has a source amplitude controlled by the majorant
\eqref{eq:thermal-instanton-gaussian-majorant}, not a positive dilute-gas
activity.  If the finite-temperature determinant residual obeys
\(|R_T(\rho)|\le\varepsilon_T\) on the same size window, the exact positive
activity \(\zeta_T\) satisfies
\begin{equation}
  \left|\zeta_T-\zeta_T^{G}\right|
  \le
  \bigl(\ee^{\varepsilon_T}-1\bigr)\zeta_T^{G}.
  \label{eq:thermal-dilute-activity-residual}
\end{equation}
Consequently the leading dilute topological susceptibility and fourth theta
curvature are
\begin{equation}
  \chi_{\rm top}^{T,{\rm dig}}
  =
  2\zeta_T,\qquad
  \partial_\theta^4E_T^{\rm dig}\big|_{\theta=0}
  =
  -2\zeta_T,\qquad
  b_2^{T,{\rm dig}}=-\frac1{12},
  \label{eq:thermal-dilute-topological-cumulants}
\end{equation}
with Gaussian approximants obtained by replacing \(\zeta_T\) by
\(\zeta_T^G\).  The susceptibility error is bounded by
\begin{equation}
  \left|
  \chi_{\rm top}^{T,{\rm dig}}-\chi_{\rm top}^{T,G}
  \right|
  \le
  \bigl(\ee^{\varepsilon_T}-1\bigr)\chi_{\rm top}^{T,G},
  \qquad
  \chi_{\rm top}^{T,G}=2\zeta_T^{G}.
  \label{eq:thermal-dilute-susceptibility-residual}
\end{equation}

For mass-saturated \(SU(3)\), \(N_f=2\) QCD,
\[
  A=\frac{23}{3},\qquad
  \chi_{\rm top}^{T,G}
  =
  K_{T,0}
  \left(\frac83\pi^2T^2\right)^{-23/6}
  \Gamma\!\left(\frac{23}{6}\right).
\]
After the one-loop action has been traded for
\(\Lambda_{\rm ht}^{29/3}\) in the hard convention used above, this is the
dimension-four scaling
\begin{equation}
  \chi_{\rm top}^{T,G}
  \propto
  |m_u m_d|\,
  \Lambda_{\rm ht}^{29/3}\,
  T^{-23/3}
  \label{eq:thermal-su3-nf2-topological-susceptibility-scaling}
\end{equation}
up to the displayed finite determinant, source-frame, and running-mass
coordinates.  This is a statement about the theta curvature of a dilute,
screened thermal instanton ensemble.  It is not a proof that isolated
instantons dominate the topological susceptibility near the crossover or at
zero temperature.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Topological diffusion and axial-charge
relaxation]
\label{ca:qcd-topological-diffusion-axial-relaxation}
The thermal instanton susceptibility in
ControlledApproximation~\ref{ca:thermal-dilute-instanton-susceptibility} is a
Euclidean theta-curvature observable.  It is not yet a real-time chirality
relaxation rate.  Let
\[
  Q_5(t)=\int\dd^3x\,J_5^0(t,\mathbf x),\qquad
  n_5=Q_5/V,\qquad
  \mathcal Q(t)=\int\dd^3x\,q(t,\mathbf x),
\]
where \(q=(32\pi^2)^{-1}F^a\widetilde F^a\) in the same topological-charge
normalization used above.  For \(N_f\) Dirac flavors with mass matrix \(M\),
the singlet anomaly gives
\begin{equation}
  \dot Q_5(t)
  =
  2N_f\,\mathcal Q(t)
  +
  \Xi_m(t),
  \qquad
  \Xi_m(t)=2\ii\int\dd^3x\,\bar q M\gamma_5 q(t,\mathbf x).
  \label{eq:qcd-axial-charge-anomaly-time}
\end{equation}
In the massless limit \(\Xi_m=0\), but for massive quarks the chirality-flip
operator is a separate real-time datum.

Let \(\rho_{AB}(\omega)\) be the zero-momentum retarded spectral matrix of the
spatially integrated operators \(A,B\in\{\mathcal Q,\Xi_m\}\), divided by
volume after the thermodynamic limit.  The KMS relation defines the
zero-frequency symmetric weights
\begin{equation}
  \Gamma_{AB}^{(0)}
  =
  \lim_{\omega\downarrow0}
  \frac{T}{\omega}\rho_{AB}(\omega),
  \label{eq:qcd-axial-kms-zero-frequency-weights}
\end{equation}
whenever the limit exists in the selected hydrodynamic window.  The topological
entry is the Chern--Simons diffusion rate,
\[
  \Gamma_{\rm CS}=\Gamma_{qq}^{(0)}
  =
  \lim_{Vt\to\infty}
  \frac{\left\langle
  (N_{\rm CS}(t)-N_{\rm CS}(0))^2\right\rangle}{Vt}.
\]
By contrast, after the local \(\theta\)-contact convention of
Definition~\ref{def:topological-susceptibility} has been fixed, the propagated
part of the Euclidean static susceptibility is the integral
\begin{equation}
  \chi_{\rm top}^{E,{\rm prop}}
  =
  \int_0^\beta\dd\tau\int\dd^3x\,
    \langle q(\tau,\mathbf x)q(0,\mathbf0)\rangle_{\rm c}
  =
  \int_0^\infty\frac{\dd\omega}{\pi}\,
    \frac{2\rho_{qq}(\omega)}{\omega}.
  \label{eq:qcd-euclidean-topological-susceptibility-spectral}
\end{equation}
Equations
\eqref{eq:qcd-axial-kms-zero-frequency-weights} and
\eqref{eq:qcd-euclidean-topological-susceptibility-spectral} therefore ask
different questions: the static theta curvature measures a Euclidean spectral
area, together with the declared local contact convention, while
\(\Gamma_{\rm CS}\) measures the low-frequency slope selected by real-time
diffusion.  A dilute instanton calculation of \(\chi_{\rm top}^{T}\) can
control a static theta curvature without fixing the transport coefficient.

If the long-wavelength axial free energy is
\[
  f_5(n_5)=\frac{n_5^2}{2\chi_5},\qquad
  \mu_5=\frac{n_5}{\chi_5},
\]
then linear response gives
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd n_5}{\dd t}
  =
  -
  \frac{\Gamma_{\dot Q_5}^{(0)}}{2\chi_5T}\,n_5,
  \qquad
  \Gamma_{\dot Q_5}^{(0)}
  =
  (2N_f)^2\Gamma_{qq}^{(0)}
  +
  4N_f\Gamma_{qm}^{(0)}
  +
  \Gamma_{mm}^{(0)} .
  \label{eq:qcd-axial-charge-relaxation-rate}
\end{equation}
For massless quarks this reduces to the topological contribution
\begin{equation}
  \gamma_5^{\rm top}
  =
  \frac{(2N_f)^2\Gamma_{\rm CS}}{2\chi_5T}.
  \label{eq:qcd-massless-topological-axial-relaxation}
\end{equation}
The factor \(1/2\) is fixed by the displayed variance convention for
\(\Gamma_{\rm CS}\): diffusion of \(N_{\rm CS}\) has Fokker--Planck
coefficient \(\Gamma_{\rm CS}V/2\), and a step of axial charge
\(2N_f\) then drifts in the free energy \(Vn_5^2/(2\chi_5)\) with coefficient
\((2N_f)^2\Gamma_{\rm CS}/(2\chi_5T)\).
Thus an instanton-induced Euclidean \(U(1)_A\) susceptibility, a theta
curvature, and a real-time axial relaxation rate are related by the anomaly
but are not the same observable.  The rate requires the retarded low-frequency
spectral problem, the axial susceptibility of the thermal plasma, and, when
the quarks are massive, the pseudoscalar mass-term and cross spectral weights.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{proposition}[Zero-mode overlap determinant in an instanton ensemble]
\label{prop:instanton-ensemble-zero-mode-overlap}
Fix a finite-volume, finite-regulator vectorlike \(SU(N_c)\) QCD background
which contains \(n_+\) instanton cores and \(n_-\) anti-instanton cores in a
window where the individual zero modes are identifiable and have been
orthonormalized.  Let \(\psi_I^+\), \(I=1,\ldots,n_+\), denote the isolated
zero-mode basis in the chirality sector carried by the instanton cores and let
\(\psi_{\bar J}^-\), \(\bar J=1,\ldots,n_-\), denote the opposite-chirality
basis carried by the anti-instanton cores.  The leading overlap matrix is
\begin{equation}
  T_{I\bar J}
  =
  \bigl\langle
    \psi_I^+,\mathcal D_E[A_{\rm ens}]\psi_{\bar J}^-
  \bigr\rangle ,
  \qquad
  T:\mathbb C^{n_-}\longrightarrow\mathbb C^{n_+},
  \label{eq:instanton-ensemble-overlap-matrix}
\end{equation}
where \(A_{\rm ens}\) is the chosen multi-lump gauge field.  After the
nonzero-mode determinant and source-convention factors have been separated as
in Proposition~\ref{prop:instanton-fermion-determinant-zero-mode-factorization},
the one-flavor massive Dirac operator restricted to this near-zero-mode
subspace is
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal D_{\rm zm}(m)
  =
  \begin{pmatrix}
    m\,\mathbf 1_{n_+} & T\\
    -T^\dagger & m\,\mathbf 1_{n_-}
  \end{pmatrix}
  +E_{\rm zm},
  \label{eq:instanton-ensemble-zero-mode-block}
\end{equation}
where \(E_{\rm zm}\) collects Gram errors, regulator chirality-breaking terms,
and Schur-complement terms from the nonzero-mode sector.  If
\(s_1,\ldots,s_r\) are the singular values of \(T\),
\(r=\min(n_+,n_-)\), then in the leading projected block
\(E_{\rm zm}=0\),
\begin{equation}
  \det\mathcal D_{\rm zm}(m)
  =
  m^{|n_+-n_-|}
  \prod_{\alpha=1}^{r}\left(m^2+s_\alpha^2\right),
  \label{eq:instanton-ensemble-overlap-determinant}
\end{equation}
and, for real \(m>0\),
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Tr}\mathcal D_{\rm zm}(m)^{-1}
  =
  \frac{|n_+-n_-|}{m}
  +
  2m\sum_{\alpha=1}^{r}\frac1{m^2+s_\alpha^2}.
  \label{eq:instanton-ensemble-overlap-resolvent}
\end{equation}
For \(N_f\) Dirac flavors with masses \(m_f\), the zero-mode part of the
leading-block fermion determinant is the product of
\eqref{eq:instanton-ensemble-overlap-determinant} over \(f\).  Hence, inside
the leading projected block, a sector with \(n_+\ne n_-\) has
\(|n_+-n_-|\) unpaired zero modes at \(m=0\), while a balanced
instanton--anti-instanton ensemble can acquire small near-zero Dirac
eigenvalues from the singular values of \(T\).

The corresponding exact statement for the full finite-regulator Dirac
operator requires stronger hypotheses.  If the regulator preserves an exact
chiral/index structure and the full gauge field has topological charge
\(Q=n_+-n_-\), then the full massless operator has
\(|Q|\) index-protected zero modes of the corresponding chirality, up to the
usual convention for whether one counts the kernel of \(\mathcal D\) or
\(\mathcal D^\dagger\).  A generic nonzero \(E_{\rm zm}\) may lift zero modes
of the leading projected block; when \(E_{\rm zm}\) is small, the lifted
near-zero eigenvalues are controlled by the finite-dimensional perturbation
size of \(E_{\rm zm}\), while the index-protected kernel survives only in an
index-preserving setup.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The massless Euclidean Dirac operator anticommutes with \(\gamma_5\), so in a
chiral zero-mode basis it has only off-diagonal matrix elements at leading
order.  The choice of signs in \eqref{eq:instanton-ensemble-zero-mode-block} is
the anti-Hermitian Euclidean convention; replacing it by an equivalent
Hermitian convention changes phases, not the positive factors below.  Take a
singular-value decomposition \(T=U\Sigma V^\dagger\).  The unitary change of
basis \(\operatorname{diag}(U,V)\) preserves the determinant and decomposes the
block with \(E_{\rm zm}=0\) into \(r\) two-dimensional blocks
\[
  \begin{pmatrix}m&s_\alpha\\ -s_\alpha&m\end{pmatrix}
\]
plus \(|n_+-n_-|\) unpaired one-dimensional \(m\)-blocks.  Each paired block
has determinant \(m^2+s_\alpha^2\) and inverse trace
\(2m/(m^2+s_\alpha^2)\); each unpaired block contributes \(m\) to the
determinant and \(1/m\) to the trace.  Multiplying these factors gives
\eqref{eq:instanton-ensemble-overlap-determinant} and
\eqref{eq:instanton-ensemble-overlap-resolvent}.  Different flavors have
independent Grassmann coefficient spaces, so their finite determinants
multiply.

The exact-kernel statement is a separate index input.  The displayed
singular-value reduction diagonalizes the projected leading block with
\(E_{\rm zm}=0\).  Adding \(E_{\rm zm}\) changes the finite matrix being
diagonalized; ordinary finite-dimensional perturbation estimates bound the
movement of the leading-block eigenvalues by the size of this remainder, but
they do not turn the leading block count into an index theorem.  Exact
full-operator zero modes follow only when the regulator supplies an exact
chiral index and the total charge of the full background is the stated
\(Q=n_+-n_-\).
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Instanton-liquid spectral-density criterion]
\label{ca:instanton-liquid-spectral-density-criterion}
The determinant \eqref{eq:instanton-ensemble-overlap-determinant} is the finite
linear-algebra core of the instanton-liquid mechanism
\cite{DiakonovPetrov1986InstantonVacuum}.  It is not a statement about the
instanton moduli space by itself.  A physical ensemble measure must also include
the bosonic action, collective-coordinate Jacobians, pure-gauge and fermionic
nonzero-mode determinants, instanton--anti-instanton interactions, regulator
remainders \(E_{\rm zm}\), and the determinant reweighting from the overlap
matrix.  Suppose that, after all those weights are included, the positive
singular-value density
\begin{equation}
  \rho_{\rm zm,\mathcal V_4}(s)
  =
  \frac1{\mathcal V_4}
  \left\langle
    \sum_{\alpha}\delta(s-s_\alpha)
  \right\rangle_{\rm ens}
  \label{eq:instanton-liquid-singular-density}
\end{equation}
has a thermodynamic limit \(\rho_{\rm zm}(s)\) continuous at \(s=0\), and that
the unpaired topological zero-mode density
\(|n_+-n_-|/\mathcal V_4\) vanishes in the same limit.  Then the zero-mode-zone
contribution to the scalar-source derivative has the Banks--Casher form
\begin{equation}
  \Sigma_{\rm zm}
  =
  \lim_{m\downarrow0}
  \int_0^\infty
  \frac{2m\,\rho_{\rm zm}(s)}{m^2+s^2}\,\dd s
  =
  \pi\rho_{\rm zm}(0),
  \label{eq:instanton-liquid-banks-casher-criterion}
\end{equation}
in the normalization of
\eqref{eq:qcd-phase-sigma-definition}--\eqref{eq:qcd-phase-banks-casher}.

This is a criterion, not a derivation of the QCD chiral condensate.  The hard
physics is the generation and control of a finite density of small singular
values of the overlap matrix after the fluctuation determinants and interactions
are included.  A dilute Poisson gas with finite isolated activities gives
theta-cumulants as in \eqref{eq:dilute-instanton-gas-cumulants}; it does not by
itself prove \(\rho_{\rm zm}(0)>0\).  Conversely, if a controlled ensemble has a
nonzero near-zero singular-value density, then the instanton zero modes have
become physical near-zero Dirac eigenstates, and the connection to chiral
symmetry breaking is the spectral statement above rather than another
collective-coordinate volume formula.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Zero-mode-zone \(U(1)_A\) susceptibility
criterion]
\label{ca:instanton-zero-mode-zone-u1a-susceptibility}
The same leading zero-mode-zone block distinguishes two different physical
questions.  A nonzero \(\rho_{\rm zm}(0)\) gives the condensate criterion
\eqref{eq:instanton-liquid-banks-casher-criterion}; restoration of the
\(U(1)_A\)-paired isovector scalar and pseudoscalar susceptibilities is a
stronger infrared test.  Use the source convention of
\eqref{eq:qcd-axial-current-pseudoscalar-density} and the local curvature
normalization of
\eqref{eq:two-flavor-instanton-source-curvature-functional}--\eqref{eq:two-flavor-instanton-u1a-susceptibility-splitting}.
For a finite leading block with positive singular values \(s_\alpha\), define
the zero-mode-zone spectral contribution to the \(U(1)_A\)-odd splitting by
\begin{equation}
  \Delta_{\pi-\delta}^{\rm zm}(m;\mathcal V_4)
  =
  \frac{2|n_+-n_-|}{\mathcal V_4m^2}
  +
  \frac{4m^2}{\mathcal V_4}
  \sum_{\alpha}
  \frac1{(m^2+s_\alpha^2)^2}.
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-zone-u1a-finite}
\end{equation}
The first term is the exact topological zero-mode pole in this projected
coordinate; it must be removed by taking the thermodynamic limit before the
chiral limit, just as in the Banks--Casher statement.  The paired term follows
directly from the source derivatives of a two-dimensional chiral block:
for \(D_{\alpha,m}=\left(\begin{smallmatrix}m&s_\alpha\\
-s_\alpha&m\end{smallmatrix}\right)\) and
\(\gamma_5=\operatorname{diag}(1,-1)\),
\[
  \operatorname{Tr}(D_{\alpha,m}^{-1}\gamma_5D_{\alpha,m}^{-1}\gamma_5)
  +
  \operatorname{Tr}(D_{\alpha,m}^{-1}D_{\alpha,m}^{-1})
  =
  \frac{4m^2}{(m^2+s_\alpha^2)^2}.
\]
The plus sign is the Euclidean source sign: differentiating twice with respect
to the scalar source gives \(-\operatorname{Tr}D^{-1}D^{-1}\), whereas the
pseudoscalar source \(i\gamma_5p\) gives
\(+\operatorname{Tr}D^{-1}\gamma_5D^{-1}\gamma_5\).

Assume now that the ensemble measure in
\eqref{eq:instanton-liquid-singular-density} has a thermodynamic limit, the
topological zero-mode density vanishes first, and the ultraviolet part of the
near-zero-zone density is locally dominated so that the small-\(s\) behavior
controls the chiral singularity.  Then
\begin{equation}
  \Delta_{\pi-\delta}^{\rm zm}(m)
  =
  4m^2\int_0^\infty
  \frac{\rho_{\rm zm}(s)}{(m^2+s^2)^2}\,\dd s .
  \label{eq:instanton-zero-mode-zone-u1a-kernel}
\end{equation}
Consequently
\begin{align}
  \rho_{\rm zm}(s)=\rho_0+o(1)
  &\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
  \Delta_{\pi-\delta}^{\rm zm}(m)
  =
  \frac{\pi\rho_0}{m}+o(m^{-1}), \\
  \rho_{\rm zm}(s)=c_1s+o(s)
  &\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
  \Delta_{\pi-\delta}^{\rm zm}(m)
  =
  2c_1+o(1), \\
  \rho_{\rm zm}(s)=O(s^{1+\epsilon}),\quad \epsilon>0
  &\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
  \Delta_{\pi-\delta}^{\rm zm}(m)\longrightarrow0
\end{align}
under the same local domination hypothesis.  Thus an instanton ensemble that
produces a Banks--Casher condensate automatically leaves a divergent
\(U(1)_A\)-odd zero-mode-zone susceptibility.  Even an ensemble with
\(\rho_{\rm zm}(0)=0\) can retain a finite \(U(1)_A\)-odd remnant if the
near-zero density is only linear.  Suppression of this channel in the chiral
limit requires a stronger depletion of the overlap singular values than the
vanishing of the condensate alone.

This criterion is deliberately phrased in terms of the weighted ensemble
spectral density, not the geometry of isolated instantons.  The ADHM or
collective-coordinate measure supplies only part of the input.  The physical
question is whether the full fluctuation determinant, fermion determinant,
instanton--anti-instanton interaction, and regulator remainder produce a
specific near-zero singular-value law for \(T\); that law is what decides the
\(\pi\)-\(\delta\) channel.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Mode-count criterion for the \(U(1)_A\)-odd
channel]
\label{ca:instanton-u1a-mode-count-restoration}
The previous criterion can be stated without assuming that the near-zero
singular values already have a smooth density.  At finite volume define the
positive counting function
\begin{equation}
  N_{\rm zm,\mathcal V_4}(\lambda)
  =
  \frac1{\mathcal V_4}
  \left\langle
    \#\{\alpha:0<s_\alpha\le\lambda\}
  \right\rangle_{\rm ens},
  \qquad \lambda>0,
  \label{eq:instanton-u1a-mode-counting-function}
\end{equation}
and let
\(\nu_{\mathcal V_4}=\mathcal V_4^{-1}\langle |n_+-n_-|\rangle_{\rm ens}\)
be the density of index-protected unpaired modes in the same ensemble
coordinate.  The finite zero-mode-zone splitting may be written as the
Stieltjes integral
\begin{equation}
  \Delta_{\pi-\delta}^{\rm zm}(m;\mathcal V_4)
  =
  \frac{2\nu_{\mathcal V_4}}{m^2}
  +
  4m^2\int_{(0,\infty)}
  \frac{\dd N_{\rm zm,\mathcal V_4}(s)}{(m^2+s^2)^2}.
  \label{eq:instanton-u1a-mode-count-stieltjes}
\end{equation}
Thus the order of limits is part of the observable.  At fixed finite volume
and nonzero index, the first term diverges as \(m^{-2}\).  The thermodynamic
limit must first make \(\nu_{\mathcal V_4}\to0\) before the chiral limit is
used to test the paired near-zero zone.

Fix a small \(\delta>0\).  Suppose that, after the thermodynamic limit and
after removing the index-protected density, the paired singular values obey a
mode-count bound
\begin{equation}
  N_{\rm zm}(\lambda)
  \le
  C\,\lambda^{2+\varepsilon},
  \qquad 0<\lambda\le\delta,
  \qquad \varepsilon>0,
  \label{eq:instanton-u1a-superlinear-mode-count-bound}
\end{equation}
and that the total retained near-zero-zone density above \(\delta\) is
bounded.  Split the Stieltjes integral in
\eqref{eq:instanton-u1a-mode-count-stieltjes} into
\((0,m]\), dyadic shells \((2^jm,2^{j+1}m]\) below \(\delta\), and the
remaining interval above \(\delta\).  The first piece is at most
\[
  \frac{4N_{\rm zm}(m)}{m^2}
  \le 4C m^\varepsilon .
\]
On the \(j\)-th shell,
\[
  \frac{4m^2}{(m^2+s^2)^2}
  \le
  \frac{4m^2}{(2^{2j}m^2)^2},
\]
so \eqref{eq:instanton-u1a-superlinear-mode-count-bound} gives a summable
bound proportional to
\[
  C m^\varepsilon 2^{-(2-\varepsilon)j}
\]
when \(0<\varepsilon<2\); the cases \(\varepsilon\ge2\) are even easier after
enlarging the constant on \(0<\lambda\le\delta\).  The tail above \(\delta\)
is \(O(m^2)\).  Therefore
\begin{equation}
  \Delta_{\pi-\delta}^{\rm zm}(m)\longrightarrow0 .
  \label{eq:instanton-u1a-mode-count-vanishing}
\end{equation}

This is the finite-regulator observable form of the criterion.  A constant
near-zero density has \(N_{\rm zm}(\lambda)\sim\rho_0\lambda\) and produces
the \(1/m\) term in
\eqref{eq:instanton-zero-mode-zone-u1a-kernel}.  A linear density has
\(N_{\rm zm}(\lambda)\sim(c_1/2)\lambda^2\) and can leave a finite remnant.
Vanishing of the Banks--Casher condensate is only the statement that
\(N_{\rm zm}(\lambda)=o(\lambda)\); it is not strong enough.  Suppression of
the \(U(1)_A\)-odd channel requires the stronger cumulative depletion
\eqref{eq:instanton-u1a-superlinear-mode-count-bound}, or an equivalent
bound, after the fluctuation determinant and the ensemble weight have been
included.
\end{controlledapproximation}

For the electroweak \(SU(2)_L\) gauge theory, the same zero-mode logic applies
to every left-handed doublet.  For one generation there are three colored
quark doublets and one lepton doublet, hence four \(SU(2)_L\) doublet zero
modes.  For \(N_g\) generations the corresponding minimal fermion operator
contains
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal O_{\rm EW}
  \propto
  \prod_{r=1}^{N_g}
  \bigl(q_{Lr}q_{Lr}q_{Lr}\ell_{Lr}\bigr),
  \label{eq:electroweak-thooft-vertex}
\end{equation}
with weak, color, spinor, and flavor contractions fixed by the zero-mode
wavefunctions and by gauge invariance.  It changes baryon and lepton numbers
by
\[
  \Delta B=\Delta L=N_g,
  \qquad
  \Delta(B-L)=0,
  \qquad
  \Delta(B+L)=2N_g .
\]
At zero temperature the amplitude is exponentially suppressed by the instanton
action.  The real-time high-temperature process is instead organized around
the sphaleron barrier discussed in
Section~\ref{sec:gauge-higgs-classical-solitons}; both effects are controlled
by the same anomalous relation between topological charge and fermion-number
violation.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Electroweak \(B+L\) response from topological
transitions]
\label{ca:electroweak-sphaleron-bplusl-response}
The operator in \eqref{eq:electroweak-thooft-vertex} is a zero-temperature
Euclidean tunneling coordinate.  A plasma rate is different data.  In a
thermal \(SU(2)_L\)-Higgs plasma, let
\[
  \Gamma_{\rm CS}
  =
  \lim_{Vt\to\infty}
  \frac{\left\langle
  (N_{\rm CS}(t)-N_{\rm CS}(0))^2\right\rangle}{Vt}
\]
be the Chern--Simons diffusion rate in the normalization where one transition
between neighboring vacua has \(|\Delta N_{\rm CS}|=1\).  The anomaly gives
\begin{equation}
  \Delta B=\Delta L=N_g\,\Delta N_{\rm CS},
  \qquad
  \Delta(B-L)=0,
  \qquad
  \Delta X=2N_g\,\Delta N_{\rm CS},
  \quad X:=B+L .
  \label{eq:electroweak-bplusl-cs-charge-ledger}
\end{equation}
Thus \(B-L\) is not washed out by these transitions, while \(B+L\) is.  If the
long-wavelength plasma free energy for a small homogeneous \(X\)-density is
\[
  f_X(n_X)=\frac{n_X^2}{2\chi_X},
  \qquad
  \mu_X=\frac{\partial f_X}{\partial n_X}=\frac{n_X}{\chi_X},
\]
then detailed balance for diffusion in \(N_{\rm CS}\) gives the linear response
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd n_X}{\dd t}
  =
  -
  \frac{(2N_g)^2\Gamma_{\rm CS}}{2\chi_X T}\,n_X .
  \label{eq:electroweak-sphaleron-bplusl-relaxation}
\end{equation}
Again the factor \(1/2\) follows from defining \(\Gamma_{\rm CS}\) as the
variance rate of \(N_{\rm CS}\), not as the Fokker--Planck diffusion
coefficient itself.
The coefficient \(\chi_X\) is the susceptibility of the actual light plasma
degrees of freedom after any imposed conserved charges have been projected out.
It is not determined by the instanton zero-mode counting.  Likewise
\(\Gamma_{\rm CS}\) is a real-time transport coefficient.  In the symmetric
high-temperature phase it is a magnetic-sector rate; in the broken phase it is
Boltzmann-suppressed by the sphaleron barrier.  In a leading-barrier
coordinate one writes
\[
  \Gamma_{\rm CS}^{\rm br}
  =
  \kappa_{\rm br}(T)\,\exp[-E_{\rm sph}(T)/T],
\]
after the negative mode, gauge zero modes, fluctuation determinant, and thermal
prefactor have been fixed.  The Euclidean instanton vertex supplies the
selection rule and the zero-temperature tunneling coordinate; the physical
baryon/lepton washout rate requires the separate sphaleron diffusion problem
and the plasma susceptibility.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Constrained susceptibility entering
electroweak washout]
\label{ca:electroweak-constrained-washout-susceptibility}
The susceptibility in
\eqref{eq:electroweak-sphaleron-bplusl-relaxation} is itself an observable
thermodynamic input.  Let \(n_i\) be a finite list of slow charge densities in
the plasma, with quadratic free-energy density
\begin{equation}
  f(n)=\frac12 n_i(\chi^{-1})_{ij}n_j,
  \label{eq:electroweak-charge-free-energy-matrix}
\end{equation}
where \(\chi\) is the static susceptibility matrix after fast reactions have
been equilibrated.  Let \(X=w_i n_i\) be the charge coordinate washed out by
sphalerons, and impose independent exactly conserved charges or neutrality
conditions \(C_{\alpha i}n_i=0\), with \(C\chi C^T\) invertible on the
constraint space.  The susceptibility of \(X\) on the constrained thermal
subspace is the Schur complement
\begin{equation}
  \chi_{X\mid C}
  =
  w^T\chi w
  -
  w^T\chi C^T
  (C\chi C^T)^{-1}
  C\chi w .
  \label{eq:electroweak-constrained-susceptibility}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, \(\chi_{X\mid C}\) is defined by minimizing
\eqref{eq:electroweak-charge-free-energy-matrix} at fixed \(X\) and fixed
conserved charges:
\[
  f_{\rm min}(X)=\frac{X^2}{2\chi_{X\mid C}}.
\]
Therefore
\eqref{eq:electroweak-sphaleron-bplusl-relaxation} becomes
\[
  \frac{\dd n_X}{\dd t}
  =
  -
  \frac{(2N_g)^2\Gamma_{\rm CS}}{2\chi_{X\mid C}T}\,n_X
\]
when the only remaining slow departure from equilibrium is this constrained
\(B+L\) coordinate.

For two charges \(n=(n_B,n_L)\), diagonal susceptibilities
\(\chi_B,\chi_L\), and fixed \(B-L\), this gives
\begin{equation}
  \chi_{B+L\mid B-L}
  =
  \chi_B+\chi_L
  -
  \frac{(\chi_B-\chi_L)^2}{\chi_B+\chi_L}
  =
  \frac{4\chi_B\chi_L}{\chi_B+\chi_L}.
  \label{eq:electroweak-bl-projected-susceptibility}
\end{equation}
The naive \(\chi_B+\chi_L\) is correct only if \(B-L\) is allowed to fluctuate
along with \(B+L\).  Conversely, if the imposed constraints already fix
\(B+L\), the Schur complement vanishes and there is no washout coordinate for
the sphaleron diffusion to relax.  This is another place where the Euclidean
't Hooft vertex is not enough: the anomaly supplies the charge step, but the
rate coefficient is set by real-time diffusion and the constrained equilibrium
thermodynamics of the plasma.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Anomalous Pion Couplings}

The axial anomaly has observable low-energy consequences.  In two-flavor QCD,
the neutral pion couples to the electromagnetic topological density through
the anomalous divergence of the axial isospin current:
\[
  \partial_\mu J_{5,3}^\mu
  =
  \frac{e^2}{16\pi^2}
  \operatorname{tr}\bigl(T_3 Q^2\bigr)
  \epsilon^{\mu\nu\rho\sigma}
  F_{\mu\nu}F_{\rho\sigma}
  +
  \text{mass terms}.
\]
Here \(Q\) is the quark charge matrix and \(T_3\) is the third generator of
flavor \(SU(2)\).  The same anomaly is reproduced in the pion effective theory
by the Wess--Zumino--Witten term introduced in the next chapter.
